601 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Holt v. Preload Technology, Inc.


No. 08-89-00095-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


774 S.W.2d 806; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1889



July 19, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 191st District Court of Dallas County, Texas. (TC# 88-1521-J).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment of dismissal entered by the 191st District Court of Dallas County, Texas, in favor of respondent employer in appellant employee's action to recover damages for injuries he sustained while at work.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was seriously injured at work. He filed suit against respondent employer to recover damages for his injuries. The trial court dismissed the action, concluding that the action was barred by the Workers' Compensation Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8306, § 3, 3(a), and 5, because the statute was the exclusive remedy available to appellant. Appellant sought review of the decision, claiming that the dual capacity doctrine was applicable to his claim and that art. 8306, § 3, 3(a), and 5 were unconstitutional. The court affirmed, concluding that the dual capacity doctrine did not permit appellant to maintain a separate suit against respondent because the Act was the sole remedy available to an injured worker and the dual capacity doctrine had been consistently rejected by the Texas courts. Further, the court concluded that art. 8306, § 3, 3(a), and 5 did not deprive appellant of his due process rights because he did not have a vested right in the common law remedies that the Act extinguished. Lastly, the court concluded that the Act did not violate the open court's provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing appellant employee's action against respondent employer because the Worker's Compensation Act was the exclusive remedy available to appellant to recover compensation for the injuries he sustained while at work.

 

602 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Mercy Hospital of Laredo v. Rios


Appeal No. 04-88-00411-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


776 S.W.2d 626; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 2432



July 19, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 341st District Court of Webb County, Trial Court No. 37,808, Honorable Elma Teresa Salinas Ender, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged the judgment of the 341st District Court of Webb County (Texas), which awarded appellee parent of deceased damages in a wrongful death and medical malpractice suit. Appellant also challenged the trial court's denial of appellant's motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellee mother of deceased 19-month-old baby filed an action for wrongful death and medical malpractice against appellant hospital. The evidence showed that appellant's nurses failed to follow doctor's orders in treating the deceased, which caused his death. The jury found appellant hospital liable. The court affirmed and held that under Tex. R. Civ. P. 327(b) and Tex. R. Civ. Evid. 606(b), an article that the jury read during deliberations, which discussed trial events, did not constitute an "outside influence." The court further held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing an undisclosed expert witness to testify because good cause was shown and because there was no surprise. Additionally, the court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to consider appellant's supplemental motion for new trial where it was filed late. The court also held that there was some evidence to support the finding of gross negligence and exemplary damages and that matters of pain and suffering were necessarily speculative, and therefore, were particularly within the province of the jury to resolve.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment awarding appellee parent of deceased damages in the wrongful death and medical malpractice suit against appellant hospital and the denial of appellant's motion for new trial because appellant failed to show reversible error and failed to show that the trial was materially unfair.

 

603 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Shakour v. State


No. 01-88-01014-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1811



July 13, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 8832719


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9, Harris County (Texas). Appellant was charged by information with violating Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 104.01(5) (Supp. 1989). According to the information, while appellant was employed by a person authorized to sell beer on premises licensed under the laws of Texas, she permitted an intoxicated person to remain on the licensed premises.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of violating Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 104.01(5) (Supp. 1989) in that, as an employee of a person licensed to sell beer, she permitted an intoxicated person to remain on the premises. Appellant argued that the information did not allege facts sufficient to give her precise notice of the offense with which she was charged. Specifically, the term "permit" did not adequately describe how she committed the offense or what conduct was required to prevent commission of the crime. The court concluded, however, that the information contained all the constituent elements of the offense and that it was obvious that the gravamen of the offense was not removing an intoxicated person from the premises. The court ruled that a determination of how one would accomplish the result was evidentiary, and need not be alleged in the information. In affirming the conviction, the court also ruled that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it used ordinary terms to express ideas that could be interpreted with reasonable certainty by a person of ordinary intelligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for permitting an intoxicated person to remain on premises licensed to sell beer. The court ruled that both the information and the statute adequately described the prohibited conduct.

 

604 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Casares v. State


No. 01-85-00829-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1755



July 6, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 262nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 425,558


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the trial court for theft of a motor vehicle and the court affirmed. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) vacated the court's judgment and remanded for the court to consider whether defendant was harmed by a parole charge based on Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, which was declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court of criminal appeals vacated the court's judgment affirming the trial court's conviction of defendant for theft of a motor vehicle, and remanded for the court to consider whether defendant was harmed by a parole charge based on Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, which was declared unconstitutional. On remand, the court concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that the error in submitting the statutory parole instruction made no contribution to the jury's assessment of punishment, in view of defendant's prior criminal record, the trial court's full curative instruction, and the presumption that the jury followed the trial court's instructions to disregard parole. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: On remand, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment which convicted defendant of theft of a motor vehicle because it found that the error in submitting the statutory parole instruction made no contribution to the jury's assessment of punishment.

 

605 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Beasley v. State


No. 01-86-00952-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1844



July 6, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 456,687.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas), vacated the court's affirmance of defendant's conviction of burglary of a motor vehicle because the conviction was upheld based on an unconstitutional parole jury charge given under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4; the case was remanded for a determination of whether defendant was harmed by the unconstitutional charge.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of burglary of a motor vehicle, found one enhancement paragraph true and assessed punishment. The trial court gave the statutory parole instruction under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 37.07, § 4. The trial judge ended the instruction, however, with an admonishment not to consider the manner in which the parole law could be applied to a particular defendant. Though defendant's conviction was initially affirmed on appeal, the affirmance was vacated and the case remanded to the court when the statutory instruction was declared unconstitutional. On remand, the court was directed to consider whether defendant was harmed by the unconstitutional parole charge. In light of defendant's prior criminal record and the curative instruction given by the trial court, which was re-emphasized by both the prosecution and defendant, the court held, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the defendant suffered no harm as a result of the parole charge; the presumption that the jury followed the trial judge's instructions to disregard parole was not rebutted by the record. Defendant's conviction was thus affirmed on remand.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court finding defendant offender guilty of burglary of a motor vehicle was affirmed on remand as defendant suffered no harm as a result of the unconstitutional parole jury charge; the presumption that the jury followed the trial court's additional instructions that parole matters were not to be considered by the jury was unrebutted.

 

606 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Bader v. State


No. 13-88-404-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


773 S.W.2d 769; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1731



June 29, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the County Court at Law No. 2 of Brazos County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the County Court at Law No. 2 of Brazos County (Texas), which convicted him of telephone harassment, a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07 (1983). Defendant contended that § 42.07 was unconstitutionally vague and that there was insufficient evidence to convict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for telephone harassment under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07 (1983), and challenged his conviction on the grounds that § 42.07 was unconstitutionally vague and that there was insufficient evidence to convict. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that § 42.07 was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the former § 42.07 had been declared unconstitutionally vague, but the legislature had corrected the problems when it enacted the current version. The court found that § 42.07 was sufficiently clear to apprise defendant that his conduct was criminal. The court also found that there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction. The prosecution presented testimony from the victim and a third party concerning defendant's telephone harassment. The court found that the jury was the sole judge of the credibility of witnesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for telephone harassment, holding that the statute governing telephone harassment was not unconstitutionally vague. The court also found that there was sufficient evidence to sustain defendant's conviction.

 

607 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Morales v. State


Nos. 01-88-00675-CR, 01-88-00676-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1667



June 22, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 31, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 262nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 495825 and 495826.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant perpetrator sought review of the decision of the 262nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), where he was convicted of aggravated sexual assault and aggravated robbery after he pled guilty to those charges.


OVERVIEW: Appellant perpetrator forced his way into victim's apartment, brandishing a revolver. He raped and then forced victim into a closet. While appellant gathered items to steal, victim escaped. Appellant pled guilty to a jury to the offenses of aggravated sexual assault and aggravated robbery. He was sentenced. The court affirmed the lower court's conviction because it was not necessary for the lower court to admonish appellant's wife about her right not to testify against her husband. Also, she testified voluntarily. The court held that sergeant responses did not naturally and inevitably refer to any extraneous offense and the jury could have reasonably concluded that when the sergeant dealt with appellant, he was already in jail on this charge. Appellant's counsel purposely did not specify appellant's objections nor did appellant request an instruction to disregard that testimony. The court also held that no reversible error was committed when the lower court permitted appellee to present character and reputation witnesses who identified themselves as juvenile parole/probation officers as their position as law enforcement was incident to their testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of appellant perpetrator for aggravated sexual assault and aggravated robbery because there was no reversible error as to the spousal privilege of appellant's wife. Also, witness responses did not refer to any extraneous offense of appellant. The lower court's allowance of character and reputation witnesses was not improper as their position in law enforcement was incident to their testimony.

 

608 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Roach


No. 07-88-0229-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


773 S.W.2d 28; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1682



June 22, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 773 S.W.2d 28 at 32.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF POTTER COUNTY; 181ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT; NO. 38,041-B; HONORABLE PAT BOONE, JR., JUDGE. Original Opinion of May 18, 1989, Reported at: 773 S.W.2d 28.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant moved for a rehearing, arguing that the court erred in affirming the 181st Judicial District Court, Potter County (Texas), decision because Texas law did not permit the appointment of joint managing conservators without joint written agreement on the date of commencement of this suit and because legislative amendments to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. ch. 14 regarding appointment of joint managing conservators could not be applied retroactively.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought a rehearing to challenge the court's earlier ruling regarding retroactive application of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. ch. 14 amendments. Appellant argued, among other things, that by holding that the amendments could be applied to a suit already pending at the time of their adoption took away or impaired a vested right belonging to appellant at such time. The court overruled appellant's motion for rehearing .The right of appellant to be considered for appointment by the district court as sole managing conservator was not taken away or impaired by the amendments here in question. The entitlement of appellant to be sole managing conservator would not become fixed or vested within the constitutional purview until and unless she was so appointed by the court. Such an appointment had not occurred by the effective date of the amendments. The court's interpretation did not deprive or impair of any vested right of appellant and did not violate either statutory or constitutional limitations.


OUTCOME: The court overruled appellant's motion for a rehearing to challenge the court's previous ruling regarding retroactive application of certain amendments. The court did not impair or deprive appellant of any vested right and did not violate statutory or constitutional rights by holding that the amendments in question regarding managing conservator appointment applied retroactively.

 

609 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hupp v. State


Nos. 05-86-00531-CR, 05-86-00532-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


774 S.W.2d 56; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 2061



June 20, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault of two children under 14. The issue before the court on remand was whether the trial court's submission of an unconstitutional good time and parole instruction to the jury contributed to the jury's assessment of his punishment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted in two cases of aggravated sexual assault of a child under 14. On appeal to the court, appellant argued that the trial court erred in submitting good time and parole instructions to the jury because the charge was predicated on an unconstitutional statute. The court rejected the constitutional challenge. Appellant then petitioned for discretionary review. The court of criminal appeals granted the petition, holding that the statute at issue was unconstitutional, and remanded the case for a harm analysis. On remand, the court considered whether the unconstitutional parole instruction contributed to the punishment assessed. The court determined that there was a rebuttable presumption that the jury followed the trial court's curative instruction, and the court found that there was nothing in the case to rebut the presumption. The court further concluded that submission of the instruction and the jury's consideration of the instruction did not contribute to the jury's assessment of appellant's punishment. The court held that the error made no contribution to the punishment assessed and thus affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for aggravated sexual assault of a child under 14. Placing emphasis upon the curative instructions by the trial court judge, the court concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that the error in question made no contribution to the punishment of life imprisonment that the jury assessed for appellant.

 

610 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Mayhew v. Sunnyvale


No. 05-88-00734-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


774 S.W.2d 284; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 2121



June 9, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled August 9, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), decision that entered summary judgment in favor of appellees, Town of Sunnyvale and individuals, in appellants' action that challenged appellee town's zoning ordinances. Appellants argued that appellee town violated various federal and state constitutional rights and that a taking without just compensation was involved.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowners challenged a trial court decision that granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, Town of Sunnyvale and individuals, in appellants' suit that challenged appellee town's zoning ordinances. Appellants contended that appellee town violated appellants' federal and state constitutional rights to procedural due process, substantive due process, and equal protection, and that a taking without just compensation was involved. The court partially affirmed, partially reversed, and partially remanded the trial court decision. A genuine issue of material fact as to whether appellee town, by rejecting appellants' application, intended to prevent appellants' development of property in order to impose a servitude upon the property to preserve the natural and traditional character of the land for the benefit of the public. Appellees failed to meet their burden of establishing that no genuine issues of material fact remained regarding appellants' various federal and state constitutional claims. Appellants were unable to maintain the portion of their action that alleged a taking without just compensation. Appellees complied with applicable statutes in initiating the taking.


OUTCOME: The court partially affirmed, partially reversed, and partially remanded a trial court decision that granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, Town of Sunnyvale and individuals, in appellee landowners' challenge to appellee town's zoning ordinances. Because appellees complied with applicable statutes, the taking was not without just compensation. Material factual issues remained regarding appellants' various constitutional claims.

 

611 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. B14-87-00485-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


774 S.W.2d 280; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1557



June 8, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] August 11, 1988, Opinion Withdrawn and Substituted.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 458,266.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted in the 182nd District Court of Harris County (Texas) of attempted capital murder. Appellant sought reversal, arguing that the trial court erred by admitting evidence of an extraneous offense and submitting to the jury appellant's parole charge, and that he was not provided notice of respondent's intent to seek a finding of use of a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of attempted capital murder. The jury made a finding of use of a deadly weapon. Appellant sought review, arguing that the deadly weapon finding should be deleted from the judgment because he had no notice respondent state would seek the finding and he was thus denied his right to know when his parole eligibility would begin, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 42.12, § 3g(a)(2); 42.18, § 8(b). The court affirmed, holding that the witness's testimony that appellant told him that he shot the police officer because he did not want to go back to jail was not erroneously admitted as an extraneous offense, because the testimony provided the jury with an explanation for the shooting. The court found that the submission to the jury of appellant's parole charge under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) which had been ruled unconstitutional, did not contribute to appellant's punishment, because the trial court instructed the jury not to consider the charge in assessing punishment. The court held that appellant had notice of the use of the deadly weapon allegation, because the indictment charged that appellant caused the officer's death by shooting a gun.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for attempted capital murder. The court held that the trial court did not err by admitting evidence of an extraneous offense or by submitting to the jury appellant's parole charge, and that the indictment provided appellant notice of respondent's state intent to seek a finding of use of a deadly weapon.

 

612 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rogers


No. 07-89-0024-CV


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Seventh District, Amarillo


772 S.W.2d 559; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1563



June 8, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled July 5, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the County Court at Law No. 2, Lubbock County; No. 85-564,950; Honorable Bradley S. Underwood, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state and appellee property owners both challenged an order of the County Court at Law No.2, Lubbock County (Texas), which awarded judgment in favor of appellant in its condemnation action against appellees, but denied appellant pre-judgment interest on the amount it overpaid appellees based upon the difference between the findings of the special commissioner and the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a finding of the special commissioner, appellant state paid appellee property owners, and took their property. After a subsequent condemnation jury trial, an amount less than that awarded by the special commissioner was found owing to appellees. The trial court entered judgment, but refused to award appellant pre-judgment interest on the amount of money it overpaid appellees pursuant to the finding of the special commissioner. Both parties appealed. The appellate court affirmed, holding that the value of appellees' property did not include the "goodwill" or "going concern" of is business. Relying on precedent, the appellate court held that the value of appellees' business was not a relevant concern in a taking of their real property. The appellate court also affirmed the denial of prejudgment interest to appellant. In so ruling, the appellate court held appellees had no control over their receipt of the money pursuant to the finding of the special commissioner. Rather, it was solely up to appellant whether to pay appellees promptly, or await judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order of the trial court, which entered judgment in favor of appellant state in its condemnation action against appellee property owners. The value of appellee's business was not a relevant concern in the taking of their real property, and appellant was not entitled to prejudgment interest on the amount it overpaid appellees because appellees had no control over their receipt of the money.

 

613 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cross v. Dallas County Flood Control Dist. No. 1


No. 05-88-00830-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


773 S.W.2d 49; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1865



June 7, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the former president of the board governing appellee flood control district, challenged the order of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which entered summary judgment declaring void, and rescinding, certain transactions whereby appellee purchased permanent easements across appellant's land.


OVERVIEW: Appellee flood control district sued appellant, the former president of the board governing the district, to rescind certain transactions whereby appellee had purchased permanent easements across appellant's land. The trial court granted summary judgment declaring the transactions void and rescinding them. The court reversed. The court held that Tex. Const. art. III, § 50 did not prohibit the use of the state's credit to acquire land for public use, and that the promissory notes appellee issued to finance the subject transaction were given as consideration for the purchase of permanent easements to permit the construction of public improvements to control floods. The court also held that the transaction did not violate Tex.Water Code § 16.236 because appellee did not carry its burden of proving that appellee could not perform its obligations without running afoul of this statute. Finally, the court held that appellee had not violated Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 71.002(a)(2) because appellant did not participate in a collateral transaction which benefited a business in which another member of appellee's board had an interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment declaring void, and rescinding, certain transactions whereby appellee flood control district purchased easements across land owned by appellant, the former president of the board governing appellee. The Texas constitution did not bar the district from assuming debt to finance the transactions because appellee purchased the easements to construct public improvements.

Johnson v. State


No. 09-86-119 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


774 S.W.2d 276; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 2200



June 7, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] February 28, 1990, Petition for Discretionary Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 75th District Court of Liberty County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant's petition for discretionary review was remanded after Texas Court of Criminal Appeals found Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4 (1989) unconstitutional and judgment of Court of Appeals of Texas, Ninth District, was ordered vacated in an action by appellant after the 75th District Court of Liberty County instructed the jury on the law concerning good time and parole after a conviction for delivery of controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant flew a planeload of cocaine into the country after he had earlier flown in marijuana. The trial court instructed the jury about the sentence for delivery of controlled substance, gave curative instruction and told the jury not to consider the extent to which good time be awarded or forfeited or the manner in which the parole law might be applied. The court of criminal appeals recited that appellant argued the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the law concerning good time and parole because the charge was based upon an unconstitutional statute, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 §4 (1989). The court of appeals rejected that challenge. The court of criminal appeals declared art. 37.07 § 4 unconstitutional and the judgment of the court of appeals was vacated and remanded. The appellate court stated the factors to consider in determining whether the parole law instruction was harmless were curative instruction, prior activities and whether the facts were aggravated. The court affirmed the judgment after finding strong and clear curative instructions, that appellant had previously flown in marijuana and the error made no contribution to the punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence for delivery of controlled substance was affirmed. The court ruled that the error in the charge made no contribution to the punishment because the trial court had given clear curative instructions and because appellant had previously flown in a large shipment of marijuana.

 

615 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


One Thousand Four Hundred Two Dollars in United States Currency v. State


No. 05-88-01370-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


774 S.W.2d 17; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 2058



June 5, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled July 24, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which awarded money and a car to appellee state pursuant to a drug forfeiture action under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 5.03-5.08 (1989), the Texas Controlled Substances Act, after appellant was convicted of possession of an analogue of 3,4-methylenedioxy amphetamine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had money and a car forfeited to appellee state pursuant to the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, §§ 5.03-5.08 (1989). Appellant challenged the forfeiture and the court affirmed. The court held that there was sufficient evidence that supported the finding that appellant possessed a drug that was an analogue of 3, 4-methylenedioxy amphetamine under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 3.10(a). The court further held that art. 4476-15, § 3.10 was not impermissibly vague or overbroad. The court determined that contentions that a statute was overbroad were traditionally reserved for complaints of alleged U. S. Const. amend. I violations, and because appellant did not allege that type of violation his contention was without merit. The court further held that art. 4476-15, § 3.10(a) was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness because it gave a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice of the substances that were treated as controlled substances. Finally, the court held that appellant could not question Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 2.09 because he had not been charged or convicted under that statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that awarded appellee state money and a car pursuant to a drug forfeiture under the Texas Controlled Substances Act (Act) and held that the Act was not impermissibly vague and overbroad, there was not an unconstitutional delegation of authority to the judiciary, and there was evidence to support the finding that the drug appellant possessed was an analogue of 3, 4-methylenedioxy amphetamine.

 

616 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hill Country Spring Water, Inc. v. Krug


Appeal No. 04-88-00137-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


773 S.W.2d 637; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1996



May 31, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 10, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 38th District Court of Uvalde County, Trial Court No. 15,795, Honorable Mickey R. Pennington, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Texas corporation sought review of the decision of the 38th District Court of Uvalde County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee administrator of estate and successor in interest of an Ohio company after appellee filed a notice of filing a foreign judgment and affidavit of filing a foreign judgment pursuant to the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 35.001 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellee administrator of estate and successor in interest of an Ohio company filed suit against appellant Texas corporation in Ohio. A default judgment was entered. A judgment nunc pro tunc was later entered which changed appellant's name to its actual business name. Appellee then filed in Texas a notice of filing a foreign judgment pursuant to the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 35.001 et seq. Appellant filed a petition to set aside the foreign judgment and an application to stay the judgment. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee and the court affirmed. The court held that appellee satisfied the requirements of the Ohio service of process rule. The court also held that there were sufficient minimum contacts to satisfy the requirements of due process and entitle the judgment to full faith and credit. The court held that appellant was not misled by appellee having the wrong name on the original case as appellant was the only target of the suit. Finally, the court held it could not pass upon the validity of § 35.001 et seq. because appellant failed to show that he was injured by its operation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of appellee administrator of estate and successor in interest of an Ohio company and held that appellee satisfied the requirements of the Ohio service of process rule, there were sufficient minimum contacts to satisfy due process and entitle the Ohio judgment to full faith and credit in Texas, and it was unnecessary to determine if the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act was valid.

 

617 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rent v. State


No. 05-88-00739-CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Fifth District, Dallas


771 S.W.2d 723; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1693



May 30, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled June 23, 1989. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Granted June 19, 1991. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied March 18, 1992. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied September 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which conviction him for promoting obscene material upon his plea of nolo contendere.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of promoting obscene material. He argued that the trial court erred in refusing to give him ten days after the criminal information was amended to prepare and file written pleadings. The court agreed, reversed, and remanded for a new trial. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 27.11 (1966) afforded defendant ten full days in which to familiarize himself with the charges that the information recited against him so that he could respond to those charges appropriately. The court held that when appellee state modified those charges by amending the information, defendant was still entitled to the full ten-day period to examine the amended charges and to prepare and file any necessary pleadings. Further, the court held that the information was amended not, as appellee contended, when the trial court granted its motion to amend, but later when the information itself was changed by the addition of certain words. The court reasoned that the actual amendment controlled because, under article 27.11, defendant would not have had notice of the amended charges against him until the wording of the charges was physically changed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment convicting defendant of promoting obscene material and remanded for a new trial because defendant was not afforded the full ten-day statutory period to respond to the charges against him. This period commenced to run anew from the physical amendment of an information's wording, not from the time appellee state's motion to amend was granted.

 

618 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 05-87-01289-CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Fifth District, Dallas


772 S.W.2d 946; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1775



May 26, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 22, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which entered his conviction, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.03 (1974), for obstructing an entrance to a place of business to which the public had access.


OVERVIEW: Defendant picketed a place of business, carrying a sign with an anti-abortion message on it. His picketing and haranguing induced a deliveryman to avoid the main walkway, and make his delivery to the business by cutting across the lawn. Defendant was arrested and convicted under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.03 (1974) for obstructing an entrance to a place of business to which the public had access. On appeal, defendant argued that § 42.03 was unconstitutional and that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. The court affirmed. The court held that state had the right to regulate the use of city streets and other facilities to assure the safety and convenience of people in their use, that this right constituted a compelling state interest, and that § 42.03, consequently, did not encroach on defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. I. The court also rejected defendant's argument that, under § 42.03, he had not received a proper order to move out of the way. The court held that the statute required that such an order could be given by any affected person, including the deliveryman who, in no uncertain terms, told defendant to move away from him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for obstructing a place of business to which the public had access. The statute under which defendant was convicted did not encroach on his First Amendment rights because state had a compelling interest in protecting members of the public in their use of city streets.

 

619 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


City of Houston v. De Trapani


No. A14-88-00610-CV


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Fourteenth District, Houston


771 S.W.2d 703; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1419



May 25, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 281st District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86-57569.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city and its sign administrator, challenged the order of the 281st District Court Harris County (Texas), which entered judgment awarding appellee billboard owner damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, based on a jury finding that appellants had effected an unconstitutional taking of appellee's property.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a city and its sign administrator, had admittedly misinterpreted the city's sign ordinance by erroneously noticing a deadline for taking down billboards. After the error was acknowledged, appellants refused to allow appellee billboard owner to erect new signs, resulting in the destruction of appellee's business. Appellee brought suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court awarded damages based on a jury finding that appellants had effected an unconstitutional taking of property. The court modified the amount of the judgment and otherwise affirmed. The issue was whether the error which damaged appellee constituted an official "policy" sufficiently to give rise to municipal liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court defined this issue as whether appellee sign administrator qualified as a policymaker, reasoning that if appellee administrator's conduct failed to qualify as execution of official policy, appellee city could not be liable under § 1983 for his actions. The court held that government policy could be executed by an administrator whose acts represented official policy, and that the acts of the city sign administrator fairly represented official policy.


OUTCOME: The court modified the amount of damages awarded appellee billboard owner and otherwise affirmed the judgment. Appellants, a city and its sign administrator, violated appellee's civil rights by unconstitutionally taking their property through acts which fairly represented municipal policy, even though carried out by appellant administrator in error.

 

620 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Thomas J. Lipton, Inc. v. Galveston Independent School Dist.


No. 01-88-00345-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1426



May 25, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 10th District Court Galveston County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 118,067.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the decision of the 10th District Court, Galveston County (Texas), which awarded appellee county judgment against appellant for delinquent ad valorem taxes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation paid its ad valorem taxes on its personal property, which included its inventory and tea stocks. After the legislature amended the Free Port Law, Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.01(d) (1982), appellant paid the taxes on its property in full for everything other than the tea. The attorney general later found the Free Port Law unconstitutional. Appellant then tendered checks for the principal taxes assessed on the tea. Appellee county refused the tender because it did not include penalty and interest. The trial court found in favor of appellee and appellant challenged the judgment. The court reversed and remanded the cause back to the trial court for computation of penalty and interest due together with the assessed tax on appellant's tea stock and inventory only. The court held that the parties had stipulated that appellant timely paid all taxes assessed against all of its personal property except taxes against its inventory and stock of tea. The court determined that the trial court erred when it levied penalty and interest on ad valorem taxes on appellant's personal property other than tea.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the issue of the assessed tax on appellant corporation's tea stocks and inventory for computation of penalty and interest due and held that the trial court erred when it levied penalty and interest on ad valorem taxes on appellant's personal property other than tea because the stipulation entered into by the parties specifically stated that appellant timely paid all taxes against its property other than the tea.

 

621 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


In re R.L.H.


No. 3-88-009-CV


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Third District, Austin


771 S.W.2d 697; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1690



May 24, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Tom Green County, 340th Judicial District no. JUV87-0150-C, Honorable V. Murray Jordan, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor challenged the decision of the District Court of Tom Green County (Texas), which determined that appellant engaged in delinquent conduct and attempted capital murder and sentenced appellant to 20 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant minor was convicted of delinquency and attempted capital murder. Appellant contended that the statute, which allowed appellant, at age 18, to be transferred to the Texas Department of Corrections to serve the remainder of appellant's sentence violated the Texas Constitution. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the statute did not violate the section of the Texas Constitution prohibiting incarceration in the penitentiary unless on an indictment of a grand jury because the petition by which appellant was charged with delinquency functioned as an indictment. The court rejected appellant's equal protection and equal rights arguments as premature, holding that appellant's transfer to the Texas Department of Corrections would occur, if at all, only after a hearing and a court order. The court held that the determinate sentence statute, under which appellant was sentenced, was enacted to provide for the care, the protection, and the wholesome moral, mental, and physical development of children. The court held that the statute furthered a compelling state interest and did not violate appellant's Texas equal rights or appellant's federal right to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant minor of delinquency and attempted capital murder and sentencing appellant to 20 years confinement because the statute did not violate the Texas Constitution's provision that prohibited incarceration in the penitentiary without an indictment by a grand jury because the petition by which appellant was charged with delinquency functioned as an indictment.

 

622 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Dennis v. State


No. 09-88-153 CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Ninth District, Beaumont


772 S.W.2d 525; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1866



May 24, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Granted October 4, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 284th Judicial District Court of Montgomery County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury found him guilty of burglary of a building, appellant sought review of his conviction and sentence imposed by the 284th Judicial District Court of Montgomery County, Texas. Appellant contended that appellee state used two peremptory challenges to impermissibly exclude blacks from the jury and that the jury was given an unconstitutional instruction on the parole law.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of burglary of a building and assessed his punishment to a life prison term based on his plea of true to three enhancements. On appeal, the court found that the record supported the trial court's rulings that no purposeful discriminations were committed by appellee state when it used two challenged peremptory strikes to exclude a black man and woman from the jury. Although the trial court gave the jury an instruction on parole law that was held to be unconstitutional, the court found that the error was harmless. Noting that the trial court gave a curative instruction, the court found that appellant's prior criminal record, the weapon found near him at his arrest, testimony about his reputation, and the seriousness of the offense clearly supported the punishment assessed by the jury. Affirming the judgment, the court found that the unconstitutional parole instruction made no contribution to appellant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for burglary of a building and the life sentence imposed. The court found that the record supported a ruling that appellee state's reasons for excluding two blacks from the jury were not based on race and that an unconstitutional jury instruction on parole was harmless error where appellant's prior criminal record and the seriousness of the offense justified the punishment assessed by the jury.

 

623 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Valero Transmission Co. v. San Marcos Consol. Independent School Dist.


No. 3-88-186-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


770 S.W.2d 648; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1575



May 24, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled June 14, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. TAX 2703, HONORABLE CHARLES R. RAMSAY, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the order of the District Court of Hays County, 22nd Judicial District (Texas), which entered summary judgment for appellee taxing unit in appellee's suit, pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 33.41-33.54, to recover delinquent ad valorem taxes, while appellant's separate action, attacking the validity of those taxes, pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 42.01-42.43, was still pending.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner sought judicial review in the trial court of the appraised values assigned to its properties, which were subsequently upheld by a county appraisal review board, by means of an action under Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 42.01-42.43. While this action was pending, appellee taxing unit, the school district, commenced an action in the same court pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 33.44 -33.54 to recover the delinquent taxes that appellant was attacking as invalid in his action. The trial court granted appellee summary judgment in its action. The issue on appeal was whether the trial court could render final judgment in appellee's § 33 action for delinquent taxes, while appellant's § 42 action, protesting the appraised values upon which those taxes were calculated, was still pending. The court noted that there was no express statutory bar to recovery of delinquent taxes in a taxing unit's § 33 suit against a property owner whose § 42 action, challenging those taxes, was pending; but held that the Tax Code implied that a judgment could not be recovered in the § 33 suit until the § 42 suit had been finally determined.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against appellant taxpayer because the summary judgment granted to appellee taxing unit for payment of delinquent taxes was premature when it was issued during the pendency of appellant's separate action challenging the appraised values on which those taxes were based.

 

624 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


McGautha v. State


No. C14-88-01047-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1370



May 18, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 466,550.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 339th District Court, Harris County (Texas), in which a jury found appellant guilty of robbery and assessed an enhanced sentence at life imprisonment. Appellant argued that the indictment was incomplete, that he did not receive a speedy trial, that a prior statement was erroneously excluded, and that he had ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of robbery. Based on prior convictions, he was sentenced to life imprisonment. The court affirmed the conviction and rejected each of appellant's arguments. The indictment, which was properly read aloud to the jury, was not required to allege the exact words of the aggravated robbery statute; it was sufficient because it charged appellant with the crime and stated every essential element of it. The Speedy Trial Act had been held unconstitutional by Texas courts; in any event, delays to appellant's trial were attributable to agreed resettings and were therefore waived. Appellant's argument that his counsel failed to require the state to make a prior statement available for cross-examination had no factual basis in the record. Counsel's decision not to call two witnesses did not support appellant's ineffective assistance of counsel argument because it was an isolated act and there was no showing that but for the decision the verdict would have been different. The evidence was sufficient to prove the sequence of appellant's prior felony convictions based on admission of a penitentiary packet; thus the sentence enhancement was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury verdict. The robbery indictment, properly read aloud by the prosecutor, charged appellant with the offense and stated all elements of the crime. The Speedy Trial Act had been declared unconstitutional. Other factors that caused delay were attributable to appellant's own resettings. Isolated acts of counsel, such as refusal to call certain witnesses, did not meet the ineffective assistance standard.

 

625 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Westergren


No. 13-88-306-CV


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


771 S.W.2d 669; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1377



May 18, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Petition for Writ of Mandamus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator district attorney sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent district judge to vacate his order convening a Court of Inquiry pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 52 to investigate the alleged illegal conduct of relator.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, a district judge, signed an order convening a Court of Inquiry pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 52, to commence a hearing to investigate the alleged illegal conduct by relator district attorney. Relator sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent to vacate the order. The court set aside its order staying the Court of Inquiry hearing, and overruled relator's petition for mandamus. The court did not have jurisdiction to consider the petition because no evidence had yet been presented in support of the hearing, and the court could not render an advisory opinion on an unripe factual situation that may or may not arise in the future. Respondent's order was not void for cause because it stated good cause in support of convening the hearing. The court could not address whether respondent was disqualified from presiding at the hearing because there was an earlier hearing involving recusal and the court did not have the outcome of the hearing in the record before it, and relator had a method of appeal from that hearing if he did not agree with the outcome. Respondent's affidavit provided relator with sufficient notice to apprise him of the scope of the inquiry.


OUTCOME: The court overruled relator district attorney's petition for writ of mandamus to compel respondent district judge to vacate an order convening a Court of Inquiry because the court did not have jurisdiction to render an opinion on a controversy that was not yet ripe, respondent's affidavit set forth good cause and gave relator sufficient notice of the scope of the inquiry, and relator had other adequate remedies at law.

 

626 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. State


No. 13-87-245-CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


771 S.W.2d 666; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1389



May 18, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 12, 1989. Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 4, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the County at Law No. 4 of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the County Court at Law of Nueces County (Texas), which found him guilty of driving and operating a motor vehicle in a public place while intoxicated, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 § (a) 2 (A) (Vernon Supp. 1989). Appellant argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that the trial court erred in refusing to quash the information and in allowing the prosecutor to misstate the charge.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving and operating a motor vehicle in a public place while intoxicated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 § (a) 2 (A) (Vernon Supp. 1989). His argument that the statute was unconstitutionally vague was not adopted by the court, which observed that the statute gave adequate notice of the prohibited conduct and did not have to specify what substances were forbidden. Appellant moved to quash the information based on the state's alleged failure to allege how he was intoxicated, but because the record did not show a ruling on the precise question of which intoxicant the state alleged, the error was not preserved for appeal. Defects in the form of the information would not render it defective absent prejudice to appellant's substantial rights. The record made it clear that the state would charge him for excess alcohol consumption and hence appellant was able to prepare an adequate defense. The prosecutor's misstatements about the charge were not preserved for appeal because the trial judge made no ruling about excluding them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury verdict. The statute, which focused not on what substance was introduced into the body but on the conduct of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, was not unconstitutionally vague. Possible errors, including denial of the motion to quash the information and prosecutor's misstatement of the charge, were not preserved for appeal.

CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: During the punishment phase of appellant's trial for possession of a controlled substance, the jury was instructed that they could consider the existence of the parole law and good-conduct time pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(b) (1988). Appellant argued that the trial court erred in submitting good time and parole instructions to the jury because the charge was based upon an unconstitutional statute. The court was unable to determine beyond a reasonable doubt that the parole instruction, reinforced by appellee's argument, did not contribute to the punishment the jury assessed against appellant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance and remanded for a new trial because the court could not conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that the parole instruction to the jury did not contribute to the punishment that the jury assessed against appellant.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County (Texas), which denied his motion to dismiss for want of jurisdiction, denied his motion to quash the information, and convicted him of the misdemeanor offense of conducting business in a sexually oriented enterprise without a permit, as required by City of Houston, Tx., Ordinance § 28-122(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested operating a cash register in a sexually oriented business located within city limits without first having secured a permit required by City of Houston, Tx., Ordinance § 28-122(a). The court held that a statute was not to be struck down for vagueness because of imprecision. Furthermore, defendant did not have standing to challenge the ordinance because he did not specifically state how the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague in its application to him. The court found that legislation authorizing the enactment of the ordinance led to the conclusion that the county court at law did have jurisdiction over this matter. The court held that the statute was not void for vagueness and affirmed defendant's conviction.

In Interest of Hughes


No. 01-88-00215-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


770 S.W.2d 635; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1110



May 4, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 246th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 87-52889.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, natural mother, sought review of the judgment of the 246th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which dismissed appellant's adoption petition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, natural mother, voluntarily relinquished her parental rights. Appellant's petition to adopt her minor child was dismissed by the trial cout. The trial court held that appellant lacked standing to adopt her own child because she was a former parent whose parent-child relationship had been terminated by a court decree. Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 11.03(g)(1) (1986). On appeal, appellant argued that the amendments to the adoption provisions of the family code did not apply to her. The court held that appellant had no legal rights with respect to her minor child. A decree terminating the parent-child relationship divests the parent of all legal rights, duties, and powers, with respect to the child. Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.07 (1986).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing appellant, natural mother's adoption petition. The court held that appellant's petition to adopt was barred, because her parental rights were terminated without provision for any right of continuing access or possession, and appellee, children's center, did not consent to the suit.

Hernandez v. State


No. 13-86-330-CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


771 S.W.2d 596; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1129



May 4, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 105th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) vacated the original judgment of the court, which had affirmed appellant's conviction of murder, for consideration as to whether the erroneous jury instruction on the law of parole under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (Supp. 1989), constituted harmless error under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2).


OVERVIEW: At trial, the jury was given the standard instruction on the law of parole as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.03, § 4(a) (1989). Appellant was convicted of murder. Appellant challenged the conviction and asserted that the trial court erred in this instruction because art. 37.07, § 4(a), had been declared unconstitutional. The court held that although art. 37.07, § 4(a), was unconstitutional it was not automatically reversible error to give the instruction. The court held that the trial court's error had to be analyzed under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2). The court set aside the trial court's judgment for reconsideration of the punishment. The court held that in light of the nature and facts of the crime, appellant's eligibility for probation, the potential range of punishment, and the uncontroverted testimony that appellant was a peaceful and productive citizen, it could not determine beyond a reasonable doubt that the jury instruction on parole did not contribute to the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment, which had sentenced appellant to 30 years imprisonment for murder, and remanded for further proceedings. The court was unable to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that giving the charge on parole and good time computation did not contribute to the punishment assessed.

 

634 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Presidio Bridge Co. v. Texas Dep't of Highways & Public Transp.


No. 3-88-129-CV


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Third District, Austin


769 S.W.2d 720; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1442



May 3, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 368,764, HONORABLE HUME COFER, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, bridge company, sought review of the decision of the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas), which granted a take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellee, state highway department, in appellant's suit arising from the construction of an international bridge.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, bridge company's, predecessor built and operated an international bridge. Appellant obtained a permit from the federal government to rebuild the old bridge. Subsequently, appellee, state highway department took bids, to construct a new bridge. When construction of the new bridge was completed, the Mexican government moved its custom facilities from the old bridge, to the new one. Appellant filed suit alleging that the construction bidding procedure violated its due process rights, that the location of the new bridge violated Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1475, and that appellee's actions constitute a taking within U.S. Const. amend. V. The trial court granted a take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellee. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that any controversy regarding the bidding process was moot, because construction was complete, and the bridge was open. The court observed that the other issues had been raised in appellant's earlier suit against the county, and that appellant was barred from relitigating those issues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting a take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellee, state highway department. The court held that any controversy regarding the construction bidding process was moot, because the construction was completed. The court held that appellant, bridge company, was barred from relitigating issues raised in an earlier suit.

 

635 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fox


No. 09-87-258 CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Ninth District, Beaumont


772 S.W.2d 455; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1562



May 3, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 3 Montgomery County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State challenged the order of the County Court at Law No. 3, Montgomery County (Texas), which dismissed an information against defendant for driving while intoxicated because state did not visually record defendant's appearance after his arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving while intoxicated, and refused both a breathalyzer test and a videotaped record of his appearance, insisting on the presence of his attorney. The trial court dismissed the information against defendant because of the lack of a videotape. On appeal, the court reversed and held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1, § 24(c) (1989), provided that the fact of the lack of a videotape was admissible at trial, but that there was no statutory provision for a dismissal when no videotape was made. The court held that the trial court had no authority to grant a motion to dismiss made by defendant, because state's attorney was the only party authorized to file a motion to dismiss under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.02 (1966). The court held that defendant's right to counsel did not attach at the time of the arrest or at the time the breathalyzer and videotape were offered. Rather, the right attached when the complaint was filed. The court remanded for a trial on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which had dismissed the charge of driving while intoxicated charges against defendant because state did not visually record defendant's appearance. The remedy for lack of a videotape of defendant's appearance was that the fact of no videotape was admissible at trial, rather than dismissal.

 

636 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Armadillo Bail Bonds v. State


No. 05-88-01369-CV


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Fifth District, Dallas


772 S.W.2d 193; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1837



May 2, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled June 12, 1989. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied January 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surety sought review of the decision of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which entered a final judgment against a bond that was posted by appellant prior to the 18-month waiting period set forth in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16(c)(2) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellant surety posted a bond on behalf of a principal who had committed a felony. The lower court forfeited and entered a final judgment against the bond. Appellant sought review of the judgment and alleged that the lower court erred because it entered a final judgment on the bond prior to the expiration of an 18-month period provided under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16(c)(2) (1989). On review, the court affirmed. The court held that the provision of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16(c)(2) (1989), which provided that a final judgment on a bond forfeiture for a felony could not be entered less than 18 months after the date of the forfeiture was a violation of the separation of powers provision of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1. The court further held that the statute required the state to act or refrain from acting within a specified time and was therefore unconstitutional. The statute, by its terms, was an unwarranted encroachment by the legislature upon the functions of the judiciary.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed, because the statute that required the lower court to wait 18 months before it entered a final judgment on a bond forfeiture violated the separation of powers provision of the state constitution.

 

637 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Pogue v. Duncan


No. 12-87-00173-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


770 S.W.2d 867; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1075



April 28, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 25, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 62ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF HOPKINS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commissioners court challenged the summary judgment rendered by the 62nd Judicial District Court of Hopkins County (Texas) in favor of appellee court reporter in a mandamus proceeding to compel appellant to fund a 10 percent increase in her salary. Appellants argued that the judge's order granting the raise under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 52.051 (1988), did not create a legal duty to perform a nondiscretionary ministerial act.


OVERVIEW: The judge for whom appellee court reporter worked issued an order under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 52.051 (1988), which increased appellee's salary by 10 percent. Appellee brought a motion for summary judgment seeking a writ of mandamus to compel appellant commissioners court to fund the salary increase. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision. However, the court's original decision was reversed on appeal. On remand, the court affirmed the summary judgment and held that a district judge's order issued pursuant to § 52.051, to increase his court reporter's pay by 10 percent or less of the court reporter's previous annual salary created "a nondiscretionary ministerial" duty on appellant's part to pay, and the county auditor to approve, the salary increase. Section 52.051, was not in fatal conflict with the provisions of former Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 689a-11, and former Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 3912k. Additionally, the court held that neither Tex. Const. art. V, § 18, nor Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 6, limited the legislature's power to modify or withdraw the powers that it conferred upon appellants.


OUTCOME: On remand, the court affirmed the summary judgment rendered by the trial court in favor of appellee court reporter in a mandamus proceeding in which appellee sought to compel appellant commissioners court to fund a 10 percent increase in her salary. The court held that an order issued by the judge for whom appellee was the official court reporter, which fixed her salary created a ministerial duty upon appellant to pay the salary increase.
