State v. Smart


No. 01-88-01023-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1002



April 27, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Court at Law No. 6 Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 8818622


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order of the County Court at Law No. 6, Harris County, Texas, which, on motion by appellee, declared Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-5 § 3(a)-(b), unconstitutional, dismissed a paragraph of the information charging appellee with driving while intoxicated, and suppressed the results of an intoxilyzer test.


OVERVIEW: Prior to his trial for driving while intoxicated, appellee filed a motion to declare Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-5 § 3(a)-(b), and regulations on breath alcohol testing, unconstitutional. The trial court declared the statute and regulations unconstitutional, dismissed the paragraph of the information dealing with .10 alcohol concentration, and suppressed the results of the intoxilyzer test. The state moved for a stay in order to appeal. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that because evidence was needed, and there was none before the trial court, the trial court's order had no support and could not be upheld based on the record.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the suppression of the intoxilyzer results, reversed the dismissal of the paragraph of the information, and ordered the paragraph reinstated. The court held that the trial court's order could not be upheld based on the record because evidence was needed, and there was none before the trial court.

 

639 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Huffman v. State


No. 08-87-00107-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


775 S.W.2d 653; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 978



April 26, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 14, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 171st District Court of El Paso County, Texas (TC# 45062).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 171st District Court of El Paso County, Texas, which convicted and sentenced him to 40 years imprisonment for murder.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the appellant's conviction and sentence of 40 years imprisonment for murdering his wife because given appellant's repeated version of his wife's departure and the testimony of his sister, the jury was free to reasonably conclude that appellant was lying about the time of his wife's departure by two hours, and that the vehicle was positioned and the tire punctured for purposes of deception. The court concluded that the jury had sufficient credible evidence to conclude that appellant lied about the time of his wife's departure, that he lied about her having packed her suitcase for a voluntary departure because the suitcase's contents attracted suspicious attention, and that he altered the evidence in his possession prior to police seizure. The court concluded the jury could have reasonably reached its verdict when considering the other evidence such as appellant's inconsistent statements as to the car keys, his fortuitous finding of the victim's missing keys in the woods away from the car, and the restaurant incident where he said he had two boys to "get rid of" depicted by the waitress provided circumstantial support to support the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and 40 year imprisonment sentence for murdering his wife because the jury was free to reasonably conclude that appellant fabricated the time of his wife's departure from their house, positioned the vehicle she had been driving to deceive, and lied about her having packed her suitcase because of the unusual contents inside, as well as other circumstantial evidence.

 

640 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Behn v. State


No. B14-87-00220-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 907



April 20, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 18, 1989
Petition for Discretionary Review Denied October 4, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 447,670


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas), remanded the cause for reconsideration of the harm caused to appellant felon by the inclusion of a jury charge on parole pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2).


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to delivery of cocaine weighing less than 28 grams and was sentenced by the jury to nine years confinement. Appellant sought review and contended that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the parole law as mandated by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4)(a). The court of criminal appeals held the statute unconstitutional, stating that Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2), should have been the standard to determine if reversible error resulted from the charge. The court of criminal appeals remanded the cause for reconsideration of the harm, if any, caused appellant by the inclusion of a jury charge on parole. The court affirmed its prior judgment and found that beyond a reasonable doubt, the unconstitutional parole charge made no contribution to appellant's conviction or punishment. The court held that the facts of the case militate in favor of the sentence imposed, there were no references to the parole law in closing arguments, and the court gave a curative instruction that the jury should not consider the application of the parole law to appellant.


OUTCOME: The court found that beyond a reasonable doubt, the giving of the jury charge made no contribution to either appellant felon's conviction or punishment. The court affirmed its prior judgment, which convicted appellant of delivery of cocaine and sentenced him to nine years confinement.

 

641 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Collom v. State


Nos. A14-88-00787-CR, B14-88-00788-CR, C14-88-00789-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 908



April 20, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10 Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 8814142, 8814143 & 8814144


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10, Harris County (Texas), which convicted her of three counts of obscenity and sentenced her to four days' confinement in the county jail after a plea of nolo contendere.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered pleas of nolo contendere and was convicted of three offenses of obscenity. Defendant contended that the trial court erred by denying her pretrial motion to quash the informations. The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of obscenity without reaching the merits of defendant's points of error because defendant failed to preserve error. The court held that there was nothing in the record that supported defendant's contention that she obtained a ruling from the trial court on her motion to quash the information. Further, because defendant voluntarily pleaded nolo contendere without a plea bargain, all nonjurisdictional defects, including claimed deprivations of federal due process were waived, pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1). The court held that defendant did not contend that her pleas were other than voluntarily entered and all nonjurisdictional error was waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of obscenity without ruling on her points of error because she failed to preserve error by not obtaining a ruling from the trial court on her motion to quash the information prior to her voluntary plea of nolo contendere, and all nonjurisdictional errors were waived.

Standage v. State


No. A14-88-00841-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 924



April 20, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No.8, Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 8821635


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of obscenity under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) and sentenced him to confinement for three days after he pleaded nolo contendere.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of nolo contendere and was convicted of obscenity under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1). Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the information based on vagueness of the obscenity statute, and that there was no timely and proper determination of obscenity. The court affirmed the judgment. The state obscenity statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court held that defendant failed to direct the trial court to any statutory language that was indefinite, vague, or uncertain, and in the absence of a specific attack upon the definition of obscenity contained in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(1), which had been held to be otherwise constitutional, it would not engage in a search for constitutionality. Further, the court held that nothing in the record supported defendant's assertion that no prior judicial determination of probable cause was made with respect to whether the alleged obscene material sold by defendant was in fact obscene.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of obscenity because the state obscenity statute was not unconstitutionally vague, indefinite, or uncertain. In the absence of a specific attack upon the definition of obscenity, the court would not engage in a search for constitutionality.

 

643 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Barehill v. State


No. 01-86-00723-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


782 S.W.2d 506; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 939



April 20, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 185th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 433,645, DAVID WEST, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas), vacated the judgment and remanded the cause to the court to consider whether appellant was harmed by a parole charge that was based on an unconstitutional statute, Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a).


OVERVIEW: The Court of Criminal Appeals vacated the judgment of the court and remanded the cause for the court to consider whether appellant was harmed by a parole charge that was based on an unconstitutional statute, Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a). The court affirmed its prior judgment after it analyzed the harm under the guidelines of Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2), which provided that the court must reverse a judgment unless it determines, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the error did not contribute to the punishment. A jury convicted appellant of aggravated robbery and assessed his punishment at 12 years confinement. During closing arguments at the punishment stage, the prosecutor recommended a punishment of 50 years and did not mention the parole laws. Defense counsel asked the jury to consider probation or the minimum sentence of five years. The statutory instruction telling the jury not to consider the parole laws creates a rebuttable presumption that the jury followed the instruction and there was no evidence to rebut the presumption. The court concluded, beyond a reasonable doubt, the parole instruction did not contribute to the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed its judgment and held that beyond a reasonable doubt, appellant was not harmed by a parole charge that was based on an unconstitutional statute. The court found that the error did not contribute to the punishment of appellant who was sentenced to 12 years of confinement for aggravated robbery where the punishment range was from 5 to 99 years or life.

Flakes v. State


No. 01-88-00332-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 967



April 20, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Discretionary Review Refused August 30, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 928027


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court al Law No. 4, Harris County (Texas), which found appellant guilty of driving while intoxicated. Appellant was sentenced to probation for two years and fined.


OVERVIEW: A trial court found appellant guilty of driving while intoxicated. Appellant was fined and sentenced to probation for two years. Appellant sought review and the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in accepting the jury's punishment verdict because the jury did not set a term for probation. The jury's verdict assessed a punishment of 730 days in jail plus a fine. The jury recommended that jail time be probated but did not specify the probationary period. The trial court entered a judgment probating the punishment for two years. Appellant argued that only the jury, and not the court could determine the probationary period pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 3a(b) (1989). The court held that since appellant did not object to his sentencing in the trial court, any error was waived pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 52(a). The court disagreed with appellant's contention that the driving while intoxicated statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 (1989), was an unconstitutional extension of the state's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which found appellant guilty of driving while intoxicated, fined him, and sentenced him to probation for two years. The court held that the appellant did not object to his sentencing in the trial court, thus any error was waived.

 

645 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


De Leon v. State


No. 13-87-512-CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


771 S.W.2d 569; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 970



April 20, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] June 29, 1989. Motion for Rehearing Overruled. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 206th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the 206th District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas), which entered a judgment of conviction on charges of aggravated sexual assault, and assessed punishment at 35 years' imprisonment. Defendant contended the trial court erred in giving the parole law charge to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault and appealed, contending error in giving parole law charge to the jury. At trial defendant moved for the state to elect which sexual assault it was relying on, sought an instruction pursuant to that election, which the trial court modified to read "on or about". Defendant claimed that the instruction amounted to no election. The court held that the modification of the charge was proper. The court found that the trial court included the parole law instruction mandated by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(2) (1988), which was unconstitutional, that the error was not automatically reversible absent a finding beyond a reasonable doubt that the error made no contribution to the conviction or to the punishment, that harmful error existed in the present case because the jury assessed a punishment which was 30 years greater than the five-year minimum sentence, the evidence was sufficient but not overwhelming, and the state included the parole law charge. The court held that the trial court committed reversible error, set aside the judgment, and remanded the case for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was set aside and the case was remanded because the court determined that it was harmful error to include a charge to the jury based on an unconstitutional parole law statute.

Carter v. State


No. 2-86-043-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


770 S.W.2d 604; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1474



April 20, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY, Charles Dickens, Trial Court Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A conviction against defendant for aggravated assault was affirmed on appeal, but the Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) vacated the judgment and remanded for determination in light of its decision that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1989) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the offense of aggravated sexual assault and the conviction was affirmed on appeal. The court of criminal appeals vacated the judgment and remanded, pursuant to its determination that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.04, § 4, was unconstitutional. The court affirmed its earlier judgment. The court applied the harm analysis of Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) to the facts to decide whether the parole instruction contributed to the punishment defendant received. The court found that the absence of jury inquiries regarding parole, together with the curative instruction, the heinous facts of the case, the fact that the sentence imposed fell in the mid-range of permissible punishment, and the absence of references to parole during argument, indicated that the jury did not consider the existence of parole for any purpose. The court held that the facts indicated beyond a reasonable doubt that the unconstitutional jury charge made no contribution to the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed its earlier conviction, holding that the jury did not consider the unconstitutional jury charge, instructing on parole, and the factors indicated beyond a reasonable doubt that the charge made no contribution to the punishment assessed against defendant.

State v. French


No. 3-88-121-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


770 S.W.2d 600; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1356



April 19, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW OF TOM GREEN COUNTY, NO. 75,445, HONORABLE GEORGE W. SVANAS, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the order of the County Court at Law of Tom Green County (Texas), which granted defendant's special plea of former jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found not guilty of negligent homicide after a jury trial and faced trial on a charge of driving while intoxicated. Defendant entered a special plea of former jeopardy and the state appealed. The court found that the state relied on and sought to prove the same act of driving while intoxicated on a public roadway that it relied on in the negligent homicide prosecution, that the offense consisted solely of one or more of the elements of the greater offense, criminally negligent homicide, for which defendant had already been tried and acquitted. The court held that trial on the driving while intoxicated information would unconstitutionally place defendant in jeopardy a second time for the same offense, and affirmed the order of the trial court sustaining the special plea of former jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court sustaining the special plea of former jeopardy was affirmed because trial on the driving while intoxicated information would unconstitutionally place defendant in jeopardy a second time for the same offense.

 

648 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Austin v. State


No. 09-88-131 CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Ninth District, Beaumont


769 S.W.2d 369; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1392



April 19, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE COUNTY COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY AT LAW NUMBER 3.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the County Court of Jefferson County at Law Number 3 (Texas), which entered a conviction for promoting an endless chain scheme under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.48 (1974).


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for promoting an endless chain scheme because it found that the state had met its burden when it showed that members of the scheme were required to recruit new members to participate in the illegal, endless-chain-scheme aspect of the business. The court found that the company that employed defendant and promoted a chain scheme fell within the statutory definition of an endless chain scheme under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 32.48(a)(1), (2) (1989). The court held that defendant was not entitled to the defense of mistake under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 8.02(a) (1974) because he could not rely on the legal advice the founder of the company had received regarding the legality of the business. The court held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.48 was not unconstitutionally vague and overbroad because defendant failed to show that the statute violated any commercial speech or association.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for promoting an endless chain scheme because it found that the state had properly shown that the members of the scheme were required to recruit new members, and the company fell within the statutory definition of an endless chain scheme.

 

649 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Garrett v. State


No. 07-88-0214-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


768 S.W.2d 943; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 963



April 18, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Granted September 27, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF POTTER COUNTY; NO. 50,934; HONORABLE MORRIS L. OVERSTREET, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the County Court at Law No. 1 of Potter County (Texas), which convicted him on a guilty plea for possession of less than two ounces of marijuana and sentenced him to jail, after the trial court refused to suppress marijuana found during an inventory search of his pockets following his arrest under a warrant for violation of parole under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.18, § 14(a) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Marijuana was found during an inventory of appellant's pockets after his arrest for violation of parole. Appellant challenged the trial court decision which convicted him on a guilty plea for possession of less than two ounces of marijuana and sentenced him to jail. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that because the full panoply of rights due a defendant in an ordinary criminal proceeding did not apply in parole revocations, the warrant for parole revocation, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.18, § 14(a) (1989), was sufficient for arrest without a supporting affidavit, and § 14(a), allowing the parole board to issue arrest warrants on less than probable cause, did not violate U.S. Const. amends. IV, XIV or Tex. Const. art. I, § 9. The issue of whether the warrant under § 14(a) should have stated that the parole board had "reason to believe" that appellant violated his parole was not preserved for review. Section 14(a) did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, where the parole board's authority derived from Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.18, § 15(a), provided sufficient due process protection for termination of a parolee's liberty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that under the lesser constitutional protections afforded to parolees, the parole board's arrest warrant for parole violation, which was not supported by an affidavit, issued by a magistrate, or based on probable cause, was sufficient, the parole board's authority properly derived from the Texas Constitution, and parolees received sufficient statutory due process protection for termination of their liberty.

 

650 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cline v. State


No. 6-88-042-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


770 S.W.2d 844; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 912



April 18, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 9, 1989.
Related proceeding at Cline v. Longview, 985 F.2d 557, 1993 U.S. App. LEXIS 2794 (5th Cir. Tex., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 188th Judicial District Court of Gregg County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 188th Judicial District Court of Gregg County (Texas), which convicted defendant of two counts of arson, for burning a truck and a house, and enhanced his punishment because of prior convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant burned a truck and a house, and was convicted by jury of two counts of arson, arising from a single criminal episode. His sentence was enhanced because of prior convictions. Defendant represented himself, but also had appointed counsel. Defendant appealed that his right to self-representation was violated and other errors. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict. It reversed the judgment as to punishment only, and remanded for hearing under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.29(b). The court held that defendant was properly afforded his right to self-representation, that the trial court did not err in permitting defendant's wife to testify against him, and that defendant received effective assistance of counsel. The court held that the trial court erred in submitting a single jury charge on punishment because Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 2(c) (1981) and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 3.03 (1974) mandated that punishment be assessed on each count arising out of one episode, and that the sentence for each offense be pronounced. The court reversed the punishment because egregious harm resulted to defendant as a result of the charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant on two counts of arson, but it reversed the punishment. It held that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict, that defendant was afforded his right to self representation, that counsel was effective, that testimony of defendant's wife was proper, but that the trial court erred in submitting a single jury charge on punishment and that, as a result, defendant was egregiously harmed.

 

651 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


First Bank of Deer Park v. Deer Park Independent School Dist.


Case No. 06-88-09661-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


770 S.W.2d 849; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 914



April 18, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 16, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 270th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant, a bank, sought review of a decision by the 270th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which entered summary judgment in favor of the appellee, a school district, in appellee's action for a refund of ad valorem taxes assessed on its stock.


OVERVIEW: The appellant, a bank, filed an action against the appellee, a school district, and sought a refund of ad valorem taxes paid by the appellant on its stock. The lower court entered summary judgment in favor of the appellee. On review, the court affirmed the lower court's summary judgment ruling. In so holding, the court held that a decision by the United States Supreme Court, American Bank and Trust Co. v. Dallas County, 463 U.S. 855 (1983), which invalidated the ad valorem tax at issue, did not have retroactive application. Moreover, the court rejected the appellant's contention that the appellee incorrectly assessed the taxes against the appellant, instead of the appellant's shareholders. The court explained that the tax was assessed against the true owners, the shareholders, even though the appellant's name appeared as record owner. The court further explained that nothing restricted the appellant from passing the assessment on to its shareholders. Lastly, the court rejected the appellant's other bases for its entitlement to a refund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the appellant, a bank, was not entitled to a refund of ad valorem taxes paid to the appellee, a school district. The court held that a decision by the United States Supreme Court, which invalidated the tax at issue, did not have retroactive application. Therefore, the case did not apply to the appellant's claim against the appellee.

Jones v. State

1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 844

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 474,547


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal challenged his conviction of delivery of a controlled substance from the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of delivery of a controlled substance after selling a rock of cocaine to a police officer. In challenging his conviction, appellant claimed that the chain of custody of the evidence was not clearly established. The court held that because appellant failed to object to the admission of the cocaine at trial, the objection was waived. Appellant also challenged the parole instruction given to the jury. The instruction was at one time found to be unconstitutional. The court held that the error in giving the instruction made no contribution to the conviction or sentence. The court considered the curative instruction, the nature of the offense, and appellant's prior record. The court affirmed, because the trial court gave a properly curative instruction, because appellant sold the drug to a police officer, who had investigated after neighbors' complaints and watching pedestrian and vehicle traffic to and from the house, and who saw approximately 10 other rocks of cocaine, and becauseappellant had a prior drug conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for delivery of a controlled substance, holding that appellant criminal waived his objection to the chain of custody of evidence and that the court's parole instruction to the jury was proper given the circumstances.

 

653 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hardy


No. 01-88-01010-CV


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, First District, Houston


769 S.W.2d 353; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 871



April 13, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 129th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 87-54776, HUGO A. TOUCHY, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county and associated individuals, challenged a judgment of the129th District Court Harris County (Texas), which declared that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2372h-12 was unconstitutional as violative of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1, in an action by appellee, county district clerk, for injunctive relief and a declaratory judgment.


OVERVIEW: After deputy district clerks filed grievances according to the procedures established by the county Commissioners Court, appellee, county district clerk, filed an action for injunctive relief and a declaratory judgment. The trial court declared that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2372h-12 was unconstitutional as violative of the separation of powers doctrine of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that art. 2372h-12 did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, because appellee's powers were not judicial. Therefore, any encroachment upon his powers did not constitute a transfer of a whole mass of powers from the judicial department to another. Also, the court noted that art. 2372h-12 did not take away appellee's power to appoint, discharge, and supervise his deputies and to maintain internal control over the responsibilities of his office, but merely provided for standardized procedures in handling grievances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment that the statute requiring employee grievance procedures was unconstitutional, holding that the statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, because the statute did not take away to power of appellee, county district court, to appoint, discharge, and supervise his deputies and to maintain internal control over the responsibilities of his office.

North Alamo Water Supply Corp. v. Willacy County Appraisal Dist.

Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


769 S.W.2d 690; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 897



April 13, 1989  
April 13, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 11, 1989. Motion for Rehearing of Cause Overruled March 27, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 197th District Court of Willacy County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant water supply corporation sought review of the judgment of the 197th District Court of Willacy County (Texas), which denied appellant's claim that sought to exempt its property from ad valorem taxation as a charitable organization, pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.18 (1988).


OVERVIEW: Appellant water supply corporation filed a claim with appellees, county appraisal and county review board, and sought to exempt its property from ad valorem taxation as a charitable organization, pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.18 (1988). Appellees denied the exemption, and the trial court rendered a judgment in favor of appellees. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that the statement in appellant's articles of incorporation that appellant furnished a water supply for general farm use and domestic purposes did not amount to a charitable dedication of appellant's assets as contemplated by Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.18(f)(1). Appellant's bylaws did not expressly pledge its assets for use in performing charitable functions, nor did they provide for the exclusive performance of a charitable function, which justified the trial court's conclusion that appellant was not a charitable organization. The court concluded that the evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that appellant did not satisfy the elements of § 11.18, and that the trial court was justified in concluding that appellant was not a purely public charity as described in Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied appellant water supply corporation's claim that sought to exempt its property from ad valorem property taxes as a charitable organization. The court held that appellant was not a charitable corporation because appellant's bylaws did not expressly pledge its assets for use in performing charitable functions, nor did they provide for the exclusive performance of a charitable function.

Holland v. State


No. 3-88-037-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


770 S.W.2d 56; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1140



April 12, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Granted November 22, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 277TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 87-586-K, HONORABLE JOHN R. CARTER, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the District Court of Williamson County, 277th Judicial District (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1989). The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. It found that the trial court properly admitted appellant's confession because appellant was not in custody and nothing in his testimony on his motion to suppress suggested that he thought he was being restrained. The court further found that even if appellant had been in custody his confession was properly admitted because it was freely and properly made following proper warnings given to him. The court concluded that the trial court properly admitted hearsay testimony about the child's allegation of abuse under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.072 (Supp. 1989) because the trier of fact had evidence to conclude that the witness was not fabricating what the child had told her and the judge had evidence to conclude that the child's declaration was sufficiently reliable under art. 38.072. The court held that art. 38.072 did not unconstitutionally deny appellant his right to confrontation because the right to confrontation did not preclude exceptions to the hearsay rule such as art. 38.072.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1989). The court found that the trial court properly admitted appellant's conviction and hearsay testimony about the child's allegations of sexual abuse.

Shearer v. State


Appeal No. 04-86-00582-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


768 S.W.2d 926; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1355



April 12, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 216th District Court of Gillespie County, Trial Court No. 2,845, Honorable Robert R. Barton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 216th District Court of Gillespie County (Texas), which convicted him of delivery of marijuana and sentenced him to 15 years in prison, arguing that the trial court's use of an unconstitutional jury instruction, Tex. Parole Law Instruction, art. 37.07, § 4, merited reversal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of delivery of marijuana after the trial court charged the jury in accordance with Tex. Parole Law Instruction, art. 37.07, § 4, which had been declared unconstitutional. On review, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that it was required to look to the entire record in its application of Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2). In reviewing the record, the court found that the trial court's error in instructing the jury was not harmless. The trial court did not offer a curative instruction, the facts of the case were not heinous, the appellant did not have a prior record, and remarks made by appellee state added to the prejudice suffered by appellant. As a result, the court held that it could not find beyond a reasonable doubt that the unconstitutional charge made no contribution to appellant's 15-year sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded appellant's marijuana delivery conviction because the trial court's use of an unconstitutional jury instruction was reversible error as it could not be said beyond a reasonable doubt that the instruction did not contribute to the sentence handed down by the jury.

Brooks v. State


No. 01-86-00206-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


768 S.W.2d 481; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 788



April 6, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 209th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 433,447.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 209th District Court Harris County (Texas), which gave a parole charge to the jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, sec. 4, convicted appellant of aggravated robbery, and assessed punishment at 20 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of aggravated robbery and assessed punishment at 20 years confinement. In his appeal, appellant asserted that the parole charge given to the jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, violated the United States Constitution and the Texas Constitution. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence and found that neither appellee nor the defense mentioned the effect of parole law, and appellant was subject to a potential punishment range of 5 to 99 years or life. The court held that while the record did not indicate any prior convictions for appellant, it did amply indicate appellant's participation in the violent crime from its beginning to end. The record showed that appellant initiated the contact, drove the car, and wielded a gun during the actual robbery. Thus, the court held that because the trial court properly included a curative charge, and neither side focused on parole during final arguments, the parole charge did not affect the jury's assessment of punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and found beyond a reasonable doubt that the parole charge did not affect the jury's assessment of punishment because the trial court properly included a curative charge, and neither side focused on parole during final arguments.

Lowe v. Harris County Hospital Dist.


No. A14-88-00187-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


809 S.W.2d 502; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 807



April 6, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 80th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86-39974


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surviving family members sought to overturn an order of summary judgment entered against them in the 80th District Court Harris County (Texas) and in favor of appellee state hospitals, which held that the sovereign immunity provided by the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.001 et seq., barred appellants' claims for negligence arising out of the death of appellants' family member.


OVERVIEW: Appellant surviving family members brought an action against appellee state hospitals claiming that the negligent use of certain tangible personal property, the telephone, the paging system, the gurney apparatus, and medical history forms, caused the death of their family member while being treated for psychiatric problems. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, holding that appellants' claim was barred by the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.001 et seq. The court affirmed, holding that appellants had sovereign immunity and appellant did not come within the use of tangible personal property exception to sovereign immunity contained in § 101.021(2). The court determined that appellants had simply routinely used the telephones, the paging system, the medical forms, and the gurney apparatus and that these devices played no substantial role in the death of the family member. In ruling for appellees, the court also decided that no leave to amend would be granted to appellants because the particular acts of appellees which appellants alleged as being negligent plainly failed to state a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment entered in favor of appellee state hospitals, holding that the sovereign immunity provided by the Texas Tort Claims Act barred the negligence claim of appellant surviving family members. The court held that the tangible items used by decedent did not play a significant role in his death and that appellants did not come within the tangible personalty exception to the tort claims act.

Smith v. State


No. B14-86-00659-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 794



April 6, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Discretionary Review Refused August 30, 1989
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 08/30/1989
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Smith v. Davis, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 69327 (N.D. Tex., Mar. 28, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 448,121


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of murder from the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas), where the prosecution sought and received an affirmative finding from the jury that defendant used or exhibited a deadly weapon in the commission of the offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. The jury found that defendant used or exhibited a deadly weapon in the commission of the offense. After the court directed the trial court to conduct a hearing to determine whether and how the prosecution notified defendant that it would seek an affirmative jury finding on defendant's use of a deadly weapon, the trial court found that defendant had adequate verbal notice through plea negotiations with the prosecution. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. A witness who was staying at defendant's apartment at the time of the murder testified that when defendant and the codefendants returned, defendant reenacted the crime. He demonstrated how he used a pipe and a knife to strangle and stab the victim. Her testimony satisfied the statutory definition for use of both weapons, and the trial court properly submitted the deadly weapon issue to the jury. The trial court's jury instruction on the law of parole during the punishment phase of the trial was harmless error. Considering the court's curative instruction and the heinous nature of the murder, the court found that the parole charge did not contribute to the conviction or punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and found that the prosecution gave defendant adequate verbal notice of its intent to seek an affirmative deadly weapon finding. The trial court properly submitted the issue of defendant's use of a deadly weapon to the jury, and testimony from supported the finding that defendant's used a pipe and a knife in a manner which was capable of causing death or great bodily injury.

Dove v. State


No. 07-87-0152-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


768 S.W.2d 465; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 733



March 31, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; 72ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT; NO. 87-405,998; HONORABLE SAM W. CALLAN, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child molester attacked her conviction by the District Court of Lubbock County, 72nd Judicial District (Texas) of the offense of aggravated sexual assault of a child, claiming that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.072 (1989), authorizing the admission of outcry statements of the complainant, was an unconstitutional ex post facto law, the state did not meet its requirements, and statements of the other children were prejudicial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant child molester, a pre-school teacher of three-year-old children, was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a child. Testimony, admitted upon a showing of facial compliance with the requirements of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.072 (1989), of outcry statements of the three-year-old complainant evinced that appellant had committed acts of sexual abuse upon the child, including the insertion of a pencil into his rectum. The court held that the outcry statements of other children, implicating appellant in the sexual abuse of children in addition to complainant, evidenced offenses extraneous to the offense for which appellant was on trial. The state did not discharge its burden to show the extraneous offenses with third parties were relevant to any material issue in the prosecution, so as to outweigh their inflammatory or prejudicial potential. The admission of the evidence was erroneous in the light of appellant's objections. The court sustained the point of error in this regard, because it could not be said beyond a reasonable doubt that the error did not contribute to appellant's conviction. Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2).


OUTCOME: The court sustained appellant child molester's point of error, and reversed her conviction of the offense of aggravated sexual assault of a child, because it could not be said beyond a reasonable doubt that outcry statements of additional children of other sexual abuse offenses did not contribute to appellant's conviction as required by Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2).

Ruiz v. State


No. B14-86-00212-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 684



March 30, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 180th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 402,654


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 180th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which instructed the jury on the parole law as mandated by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4)(a), which was reviewed by the criminal appeals court and remanded for reconsideration of harm.


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the parole law as mandated by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4)(a). The criminal appeals court held the statute unconstitutional, stating that Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) was the standard and remanded the cause to determine if reversible error resulted from the charge. The court identified the factors to be used in applying Rule 81(b)(2) which were whether a curative instruction was given, whether the facts of the offense militated in favor of the sentence imposed, whether any reference to the parole law was made in closing argument, and if the defendant had prior felony convictions. The proof showed that appellant had no prior felony convictions. There was no argument by either side on the parole charge and the court submitted a curative instruction charging the jury that it should not consider the application of the parole law to appellant. Additionally, the jury properly assessed punishment. After examining the factors, the court found beyond a reasonable doubt that the unconstitutional parole charge made no contribution to appellant's conviction or punishment.


OUTCOME: On remand from the criminal appeals court to determine if the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the parole law in appellant's conviction for robbery at gunpoint, the court found beyond a reasonable doubt that the unconstitutional parole charge made no contribution to appellant's conviction or punishment.

Arrington v. Mattox


No. 3-88-086-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


767 S.W.2d 957; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1079



March 29, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled May 3, 1989; Application for Writ of Error Denied September 6, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 353,498, HONORABLE HARLEY CLARK, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land owners sought review of a decision of the 53rd District Court, Travis County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee Attorney General of Texas in appellee's "open beaches" suit. The judgment prohibited appellants from interfering with the public's right of free access over the beach adjacent to appellants' property which was seaward of the natural vegetation line.


OVERVIEW: After a hurricane moved the vegetation line to a point landward of appellant land owners' property, appellants built a retaining wall on the beach in front of their home and constructed numerous improvements on the seaward side of the wall. Appellee Attorney General of Texas filed suit pursuant to the Open Beaches Act, alleging that a public easement and right of use existed on the seaward side of the natural vegetation line across appellants' property and that appellants had encroached upon that right of use by placing structures and objects on the easement. The trial court granted appellee's summary judgment motion, ordered the removal of the obstructions on the easement, and enjoined appellants from further activity which restrained or interfered with the public's right of access to the beach. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, holding that there was no unconstitutional taking of appellants' land because the Open Beaches Act did not empower appellee to take rights from a land owner, but furnished a means to enforce the public's existing rights of acquiring its easements through prescription, dedication, and custom.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment because appellant land owners' property was not unconstitutionally taken without compensation as the easement over appellants' land was acquired not by statute, but through prescription, public dedication, or custom.

Diaz v. State


Appeal No. 04-86-00037-CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Fourth District, San Antonio


769 S.W.2d 307; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1354



March 29, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by, 03/14/1990
Motion for rehearing on petition for discretionary review denied by, 04/25/1990
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Diaz v. Collins, 51 F.3d 1041, 1995 U.S. App. LEXIS 8143 (5th Cir. Tex., 1995)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 341th District Court of Webb County, Trial Court No. 18,958, Honorable Elma Teresa Salinas-Ender, Judge Presiding.
Diaz v. State, 761 S.W.2d 1, 1988 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 197 (Tex. Crim. App., 1988)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 341st District Court, Webb County (Texas), in which the jury received a parole law instruction under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 (1989), which was later declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The parole law jury instruction, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 (1989), was declared unconstitutional subsequent to being given in the guilt/innocence phase of defendant's trial. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, finding beyond a reasonable doubt that the error in the trial court's instruction to the jury on the parole law did not contribute to the punishment in this case. Because the trial court gave cautionary instructions which the jury was presumed to have followed; defense counsel admonished the jury to consider only the facts of the case and not be misled by the parole laws and both the defense and the state made further cautionary remarks regarding the parole laws; proof of defendant's guilt was overwhelming; and the jury assessed fewer years of imprisonment than were asked for by the prosecution, the court concluded that the statutory parole law instruction did not affect defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The court concluded that no harm resulted from the trial court's jury instruction on the parole law because curative instructions regarding the parole laws were given, both the defense and the state made cautionary remarks to the jury about the parole laws, there was overwhelming proof of defendant's guilt, and the jury assessed fewer years of imprisonment than were requested by the state.

Adams v. State


No. 01-86-00152-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 554



March 23, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 434,597


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the 177th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted defendant of sexual assault and sentenced him to 15 years and 1 day of confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of sexual assault. At trial and on appeal, defendant objected that the trial court erred in giving the jury a parol instruction during the punishment phase of the trial. The court affirmed the judgment. The matter was remanded to the court by the criminal appeals court so that defendant's points of error concerning the parole charge would be reconsidered in light of Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2), the harmless error rule. On remand the court again affirmed, finding that there was no basis in the record for assuming that the jury's assessment of the particular term, the minimum possible to preclude bail pending appellate review, was in any way based upon the trial court's instruction on the parole laws. The court held that the record, considered in its entirety, showed beyond a reasonable doubt that the parole law instruction had made no contribution to the punishment assessed and thus, the trial court's instruction was harmless error.


OUTCOME: On remand, the court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual assault and defendant's sentence to 15 years and 1 day of confinement. The court held that the record, considered in its entirety, showed beyond a reasonable doubt that the parole law instruction had made no contribution to the punishment assessed and thus, the trial court's instruction constituted harmless error.

Howard v. State


No. 01-86-00589-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 561



March 23, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 453,707


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order by the 338th District Court, Harris County Texas, which gave a parole charge to the jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, as it violated the separation of powers and due process doctrines. The criminal appellate court vacated the judgment of the court and remanded the cause for reconsideration whether defendant was harmed by the parole charge.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of aggravated robbery. After finding an enhancement paragraph to be true, the jury assessed punishment of 65 years confinement. The trial court made an affirmative finding on the use of a deadly weapon. Defendant sought review and asserted that the parole charge given to the jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, violated the separation of powers and due process doctrines. The court upheld the constitutionality of the statute and overruled the point of error. The criminal appellate court vacated the judgment of the court and remanded the cause for reconsideration whether defendant was harmed by the parole charge. On remand, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment because, although Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 was unconstitutional, it was harmless error in the instant case. Pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2), the court found beyond a reasonable doubt that the unconstitutional parole charge made no contribution to the jury's assessment of defendant's punishment. The court based this on the heinous facts of the offense, defendant's prior criminal record, and the sentence that was assessed.


OUTCOME: On remand, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because it found beyond a reasonable doubt that the unconstitutional parole charge given was harmless error and made no contribution to the jury's assessment of punishment for defendant.

Escobar v. State

PRIOR HISTORY: ON REMAND FROM THE COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) remanded the matter before the court because the appellate court had determined that a statute requiring jury instruction concerning parole was unconstitutional. The jury in the instant case was so instructed, therefore, the case was remanded to determine beyond a reasonable doubt whether the error made any contribution to the conviction or the punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery and sentenced to life imprisonment. On remand, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Defendant claimed an error in evidence concerning the parole law that was given to the jury. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, which mandated jury instruction on parole law, had been declared unconstitutional and the court had to determine whether the error of instructing the jury on parole law contributed to defendant's conviction or punishment beyond a reasonable doubt. The court reviewed the entire record and determined beyond a reasonable doubt that, in light of the evidence and defendant's past conduct, the parole law instruction did not contribute to defendant's conviction or punishment. Because defendant first broached the subject of parole law, he could not thereby claim reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court determined beyond a reasonable doubt that the error of instructing the jury about parole did not make any contribution to the conviction or the punishment. Because defendant introduced the subject of parole law, he was not entitled to claim error on appeal.

Severn v. State


No. 6-87-016-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


767 S.W.2d 914; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 560

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 188th Judicial District Court of Gregg County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the 188th District Court, Gregg County, Texas, which was entered after a jury convicted him of indecency with a child.

Thus, the court found beyond a reasonable doubt that the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of indecency with a child, holding that the trial court's admission into evidence of a videotaped interview with the child victim was harmless error where the child testified in the state's case-in-chief after the videotape was shown, and the defense had the opportunity to cross-examine her.

Roberts v. State


No. 01-87-00005-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 527



March 16, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 174th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 459,277


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment by the 174th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted defendant of aggravated sexual assault and assessed punishment at 60 years confinement. Defendant claimed that the charge given the jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 3707(4)(a) violated the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his companion pulled over the victim by using a red light on the dashboard of their pick-up, making the victim think she was being pulled over by police. Defendant struck the victim on the head, hand-cuffed her, and then defendant and his companion had sexual intercourse with her. Afterwards, they forced the victim to withdraw money with her automatic teller card. Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault and assessed punishment at 60 years confinement. Defendant appealed, contending that the trial court violated the separation of powers doctrine by giving the parole charge to the jury pursuant to Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 3707(4)(a). The court overruled the error and affirmed the judgment. After giving the statutory parole charge, the trial court gave a curative charge that the jurors were not to discuss the effect of parole on the sentence, and that the issue of parole was one for the executive branch. The state reiterated the curative charge during the punishment phase. The court applied Tex. R. App. Proc. 81(b)(2) to determine that it found, beyond a reasonable doubt, that defendant suffered no harm as a result of the parole charge.


OUTCOME: The court overruled defendant's point of error and affirmed the judgment entered upon the jury's determination that defendant was guilty of aggravated sexual assault, and assessed a punishment of 60 years confinement, because the trial court's parole charge in violation of the separation of powers doctrine was harmless error.

 

671 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Laseries v. State


No. 01-86-00483-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 531



March 16, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 179th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial COurt Cause No. 435,693


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Texas Court of Criminal Appeals, defendant appealed from the judgment of the 179th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of actual delivery of cocaine weighing less than 28 grams, with one enhancement paragraph found true, and assessed punishment at 40 years confinement, on the ground that he was harmed by an unconstitutional parole charge based on Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.03(4)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who sold and delivered a small amount of cocaine to an undercover police officer, was ultimately convicted after a jury found him guilty of actual delivery of cocaine weighing less than 28 grams, found one enhancement paragraph true, and assessed punishment at 40 years confinement. Defendant appealed, and the court reversed and remanded to the trial court for a new trial on the issue of punishment only, and affirmed the remainder of the judgment. The court held that the trial court erred in giving the unconstitutional parole instruction, and that, after applying the harm analysis set forth in Tex. R. App. Proc. 81(b)(2), the court could not find beyond a reasonable doubt that the error did not contribute to the punishment assessed. The trial court did not give the curative instruction that parole matters came within the exclusive jurisdiction of the executive branch and, thus, were no concern of the jury. Additionally, the state argued in closing that defendant could earn time off the sentence through an award of good conduct time and that the sentence could be reduced by the award of parole. Thus, the court could not say that the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded to the trial court for a new trial on the issue of punishment only, and affirmed the remainder of the judgment that convicted defendant of delivery of a cocaine weighing less than 28 grams, because the court could not find beyond a reasonable doubt that the error in giving an unconstitutional parole charge without a curative instruction did not contribute to the punishment assessed.

 

672 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lyon v. State


No. 3-88-167-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


766 S.W.2d 879; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 832



March 15, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court at law No. 6 of Travis County, No. 302,569, Honorable Wilford Flowers, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the County Court at Law No. 2, Travis County (Texas), which convicted her of awarding a door prize at a bingo occasion in violation of the Bingo Enabling Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 179d, § 11(q) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating of the Bingo Enabling Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 179d, § 11(q) (1989), which prohibited the award of any prizes to persons present at a bingo occasion, other than prizes for the games themselves. The appellate court reversed and reformed the conviction to reflect an acquittal, holding that defendant did not violate the statute by awarding a door prize during the intermission between two bingo sessions. Because the statute did not define "bingo occasion", the court looked first at the plain meaning of the word "occasion" and the legislative history of the Act and held that the statute did not apply to the intermission. The court noted that the Act required the issuance of a license, and that there were specified time limits on the series of games an organization could operate. Viewing the statute as a whole and under the rule of strict construction, the court held that "bingo occasion" referred to the time during which a series of successive bingo games were conducted by a licensed organization, and time outside of an organization's licensed hours could not be considered part of the "bingo occasion".


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment convicting defendant of violating the provision of the Bingo Enabling Act prohibiting the award of prizes other than for the games during a bingo occasion. The court held that the award of a prize during an intermission between two bingo sessions was not part of the bingo occasion specified in the statute.

Graham v. State


No. 07-88-0332-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


767 S.W.2d 271; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 494



March 13, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT AT LAW NO. 12 OF HARRIS COUNTY; NO. 8829268; HONORABLE JOE TERRACINA, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed conviction by information entered against him in the County Criminal Court of Law No. 12 of Harris County (Texas) for selling obscene material in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with selling obscene material in violation of Texas Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (1989). After defendant's motion to quash the complaint was denied, he entered his non-negotiated plea of nolo contendere which was accepted by the lower court. Defendant appealed and contended there were two points of error committed by the lower court in its denial of his motion to quash. As to defendant's first point, the court held that the statute prohibiting the sale of obscene material was not unconstitutionally vague. Not only did defendant not request a prior determination of obscenity, but the material purchased did not constitute an unconstitutional "seizure" that would require a pre-seizure hearing to determine whether the material was obscene. As to defendants' second point, the court held that defendant could not argue on appeal that his conviction was invalid because no timely and proper determination of obscenity was raised. Even if defendant's second contention had once been correctly predicated by defendant's later plea of nolo contendere, he admitted every element of the offense including the element that the material was obscene when he sold it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for selling obscene material, holding that the statute prohibiting the sale of obscene material was not unconstitutionally vague and that there was no unconstitutional "seizure" that would have required a pre-seizure hearing to determine whether the material was obscene.

Rolling v. State


No. 05-85-01064-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


768 S.W.2d 834; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1282



March 13, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the grant of a petition for discretionary review of an error in submitting good time and parole instructions to the jury on defendant's murder conviction, defendant's murder conviction was remanded from the Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) for a harmless error analysis under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and was assessed 99 years and a fine of $ 2500. Defendant petitioned for discretionary review contending that the trial court erred in submitting good time and parole instructions to the jury on the grounds that the charge was predicated on an unconstitutional statute, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 and was a violation of due process. Defendant's petition on the constitutional issue was granted and remanded for the court to conduct a harmless error analysis under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) which required a review of the entire record. The court found that state made an erroneous summary of the parole law to the jury in its opening argument, providing the jury a reason to give the defendant maximum sentence, and attributed it to the trial court's charge. The state concentrated on the facts and the severity of defendant's offense and offered no evidence during the punishment phase of the trial. Further, no mitigating instruction was included in the court's charge. Thus, the court ruled that the error in submitting the statutorily mandated charge contributed to the assessment of defendant's punishment and was not harmless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's error in submitting good time and parole instructions to the jury on defendant's murder conviction and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings as it contributed to the punishment assessed based on an unconstitutional charge.

Trevino v. State


No. 13-86-311-CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


769 S.W.2d 601; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 461



March 9, 1989  
March 9, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 27, 1989. Petition for Discretionary Review Refused July 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 206th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 206th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas, which convicted him of aggravated assault and assessed punishment at 20 years of confinement and a fine of and a $ 1,000 fine, alleging that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the law concerning good conduct time and parole because the charge was predicated upon an unconstitutional statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault and sentenced to twenty years' confinement and a $ 1000 fine. The Court of Criminal Appeals remanded the case back to the court for a harmless error analysis under the guidelines of Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2), after the court had affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that it was unable to hold beyond a reasonable doubt that an erroneous jury instruction predicated upon an unconstitutional statute made no contribution to the punishment assessed. The court found that appellee state conceded that harmful error resulted, because the prosecutor invited the jury to apply the parole laws in assessing punishment. The court ruled that any jury argument, which urged jurors to apply the parole laws, was highly improper. The court also found that the jury charge contained an instruction that contained typographical errors, and that a curative instruction in addition to the statutory parole instruction was not given to the jury. Thus, the court set aside the judgment of the trial court, and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the trial court, and remanded, because the court was unable to hold beyond a reasonable doubt that an erroneous jury instruction had made no contribution to the punishment assessed to defendant. The court noted that no curative instruction was given to the jury, and the state conceding harmful error had occurred after jurors were improperly urged to apply the parole laws during the penalty stage.
