Khalaf v. Odiorne


No. 3-88-084-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


767 S.W.2d 856; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 1082



March 8, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled April 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 98TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 398,492, HONORABLE JAMES MEYERS, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured challenged the order of the District Court of Travis County, 98th Judicial District (Texas), which granted appellee, insurance company receiver, take-nothing summary judgment that barred appellant's insurance claim pursuant to Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28 § 3(h) (1981).


OVERVIEW: Appellant insured's property was destroyed by fire, after which the insurer was placed in receivership. Appellee, insurance company receiver, mailed notice of rejection of appellant's claim to an address incorrectly provided by appellant, so appellant never received it. The trial court granted appellee's summary judgment that barred appellant's claim pursuant to Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28 § 3(h) (1981). The court affirmed the summary judgment, and held that the appellee's notice of rejection of claims should have been done in a manner determined by the receivership court. The court found that even though notice requirements were not defined under § 3(h), they needed to be read in relation to other sections of the statute, because statutory provisions were not to be isolated from the surrounding language. Under Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28 § 3(a), notice was to be done in a manner determined by the receivership court. The court determined that the receivership court's order stated that mailing of letters was sufficient proof of notice, and appellant had not filed suit on the claim within three months after such service of notice as required under § 3(h).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order granting summary judgment to appellee, insurance company receiver, against appellant insured, because appellee had followed rejection notice requirements of controlling statute that were determined by looking at surrounding statutory sections of the controlling statute.

 

678 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Spencer Gifts, Inc. v. Bullock


No. 3-88-079-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


766 S.W.2d 593; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 739



March 8, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Travis County 53rd Judicial District, No. 384,181, Honorable Pete Lowry, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retailer sought relief from a take-nothing judgment entered by the District Court of Travis County (Texas), which denied appellant any refund in a suit involving sales tax assessed by appellee Comptroller of Public Accounts of the State of Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant retailer operated a mail order catalog. Sales invoices assessed charges for "postage and handling" and appellant excluded that total charge from its taxable receipts. A sales tax deficiency notice was issued to appellant after an audit by appellee Comptroller of Public Accounts of the State of Texas. Appellant paid under protest and sought a refund in the district court. The court affirmed the district court's take-nothing judgment, holding that appellant had improperly commingled taxable and non-taxable charges. The court found that handling charges did not fall within the definition of "transportation" which excluded activities at the retailer's premises prior to loading goods on trucks for shipment. Charges for handling, the court held, could not be excluded from taxable receipts, although charges for postage could be excluded. The court went on to hold that appellant had not complied with the requirements of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 151.007 which required that transportation charges be separately stated to customers because appellants' charges were commingled with handling charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the take-nothing judgment denying a sales tax refund to appellant retailer because the notice of tax deficiency issued to appellant by appellee Comptroller of Public Accounts of the State of Texas was proper, as appellant had commingled charges that were taxable with charges that were non-taxable and had excluded the total charge from its taxable receipts.

Tarrant Appraisal Dist. v. Colonial Country Club


No. 2-87-224-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


767 S.W.2d 230; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 945



March 8, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 20, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 17TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY



DISPOSITION:  The court reformed and affirmed the judgment against appellants, Tarrant County Appraisal Review Board and Tarrant Appraisal District, holding that the Greenbelt Act was constitutional and applicable to private country clubs, and finding that appellee country club had satisfied its requirements; deed restrictions were valid and enforceable, land was only used for recreation, and no private gain was realized.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Tarrant County Appraisal Review Board and Tarrant Appraisal District challenged a judgment of the 17th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which held that deed restrictions filed by appellee country club were valid, land was used only for recreation, and no private gain was realized. Appellee sought review of the holding that it was not entitled to assessment under the Greenbelt Act, Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 23.81-23.87 (1982).


OVERVIEW: Appellee country club filed suit protesting a determination by appellants, Tarrant County Appraisal Review Board and Tarrant Appraisal District, that it was not entitled to special appraisal under the Greenbelt Act (act), Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 23.81-23.87 (1982). The trial court ruled that the act was not applicable to appellee, but refused to allow appellee's land to be taxed at full fair market value, and based the value on a self-imposed restriction filed by appellee in the county deed records. Both parties appealed, and the court reformed and affirmed the judgment, holding that the act provided a method of assessing value based on the reasonable classification of property and was therefore constitutional, and that appellee was entitled to appraisal under the act. The court found that deed restrictions limiting land use to recreational filed by appellee in accord with the act were binding on buyers and enforceable by the state, that use of the property for restaurants and a barbershop did not violate the mandate of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.83 that the land be used only for recreation, and that indirect benefits to members did not constitute private gain.


OUTCOME: The court reformed and affirmed the judgment against appellants, Tarrant County Appraisal Review Board and Tarrant Appraisal District, holding that the Greenbelt Act was constitutional and applicable to private country clubs, and finding that appellee country club had satisfied its requirements; deed restrictions were valid and enforceable, land was only used for recreation, and no private gain was realized.

Lewis v. State


No. B14-87-00644-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston

NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 448,102


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment form the 178th District court Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of aggravated robbery and sentencing him to seven years in prison. The court held that although the trial court improperly allowed prosecution to bolster the testimony of the complaining witness, the error was harmless. The court also found that testimony about information obtained from a computer search was not hearsay and was properly admitted. Prosecution's reference to defendant, during argument, a "stone pathological liar" was not manifestly improper and not reversible error. While the trial court committed error in giving an instruction on statutory parole pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 37.07 § 4, the court held that the error was also harmless based on a curative instruction that was given and the fact that the jury recommended a sentence at the low end of the punishment range. The court further found that there was no showing that any information that was material or that was in prosecutor's possession had been denied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of aggravated robbery. Prosecutor's bolstering of witness was harmless error, no improper hearsay evidence was taken, prosecutor's argument during closing followed the evidence and was proper, the facts indicated that the jury followed a curative instruction on satutory parole, and there was no evidence that prosecutor withheld exculpatory evidence from the defense.

Cardona v. State


No. B14-88-00074-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


768 S.W.2d 823; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 417



March 3, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 338th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 434,759.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from an order of the 338th District Court Harris County, Texas, which found appellant guilty of delivery of over 400 grams of cocaine and sentenced him to fifteen years' confinement in the Texas Department of Corrections and a $ 250 fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of delivering over 400 grams of cocaine an sentenced to 15 years' confinement and a $ 250 fine, the minimum sentence under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 4476-15 §§ 4.02(b)(3)(D) and 4.03(d) (1989). Appellant alleged entrapment, and the court disagreed, noting that appellant failed both to meet his initial burden of showing that an inducement to sell cocaine occurred and to show that a party to the sale was a law enforcement agent or under the control of one. The court also rejected appellant's contention that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 § 4.03 (d)(3) (198) violated due process and equal protection because the mandatory sentence precluded the possibility of probation. The court held that constitutional due process and equal protection generally demanded only a rational basis for legislatively created classifications, and that the state's legitimate interest in deterring unlawful deliveries provided sufficient rational basis for proscribing probation. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, overruling both of appellant's points of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that found appellant guilty of delivery of over 400 grams of cocaine because appellant failed to plead a defense of inducement. The court affirmed the sentence of fifteen years' confinement without possibility of probation, finding that the statute that set the punishment was rationally related to a legitimate state interest, and was not unconstitutional.

 

682 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Payne v. State


No. 05-85-01244-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


766 S.W.2d 585; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 730



March 3, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of murder following the submission of good time and parole law instructions to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in submitting good time and parole instructions to the jury. The court affirmed defendant's conviction on remand and found that the submission of the unconstitutional instructions was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2). The court found that during jury argument at the close of the punishment phase, neither the state nor defense counsel mentioned the parole instructions. Although a note from the jury showed that they were considering the parole instructions included in the charge, the court found that it did not necessarily follow that such consideration contributed to defendant's punishment. Based upon the calculated, cold-blooded execution of a crippled, intoxicated, and sleeping man, together with the deadly weapon finding, and defendant's prior convictions which revealed a propensity for violence, the court held that beyond a reasonable doubt the error made no contribution to defendant's punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder because the trial court's error in submitting good time and parole law instructions to the jury made no contribution to defendant's conviction or punishment.

 

683 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Montoya v. State


No. 01-88-0505-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 369



March 1, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion For Rehearing is Overruled March 30, 1989Petition for Discretionary Review Granted July 26, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 179th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 451,057-A


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, bail bond principal and sureties, challenged a final judgment of the 179th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which ordered a bond forfeited to appellee State of Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, bail bond principal and sureties, executed a bail bond in favor of appellee State of Texas. The bond was then forfeited, and appellee was awarded the amount of the bond after a trial. Appellants challenged the judgment, arguing that the recently amended version of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16 (1987), which provided that a final judgment could not be entered against a bond earlier than 18 months after the date the forfeiture was entered, should have been applied retroactively to their case. The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that Tex. Const. art. I, § 16 stated that the legislature could not make a retroactive law or a law impairing the obligation of contracts. The court then found that the bail bond was a contract between appellants and appellee. The court concluded that retroactive application of art. 22.16 would have impaired appellee's vested rights under the bond agreement. The court also held that art. 22.16 was a substantive change in the law and should not have been applied retroactively. As the case was determinable on other grounds, the court did not consider appellee's argument that amended art. 22.16 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which awarded the full amount of a bail bond to appellee State of Texas. The court held that retroactive application of a recent statutory amendment regarding when final judgment could be entered against a bond would have impaired appellee's vested rights under the bond agreement. The court also held that the amendment was a substantive change in the law and should not have been applied retroactively.

 

684 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Flakes v. State


No. 01-88-00137-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 372



March 1, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion For Rehearing is Overruled March 30, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 179th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 449702


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the 179th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted defendant of the felony offense of driving while intoxicated. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred by denying his requested jury instruction, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, and that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 6701L-1, under which he was convicted, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for driving while intoxicated and asserted that because his testimony was in direct conflict with the testimony presented by the officers, a factual dispute was raised over the legality of the initial stop, and as a result of this dispute, he was entitled to a jury instruction pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 35.23 (1959). On appeal, the court held that in any case where the legal evidence raises an issue, the jury shall be instructed that if it believes, or has a reasonable doubt, that the evidence was obtained in violation of the provisions of article 35.23, the jury shall disregard any such evidence so obtained. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and concluded that defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction regarding the admissibility of the officer's testimony. The court also held that in light of the above decision it was unnecessary to address the issue of ineffective assistance of counsel. In addition, the court noted that the issue of the constitutionality of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 6701L-1 had previously been decided.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of driving while intoxicated. The court held that the officers were justified in stopping defendant for the traffic violation of following too closely and thus he was not entitled to a jury instruction regarding the admissibility of the officer's testimony. Based upon the above holding, the court did not address the issue of ineffective assistance of counsel.

 

685 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Randolph v. State


No. 01-86-00349-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 374



March 1, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 409,836


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the 351st District Court, Harris County, Texas, of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft, and two enhancement paragraphs were found true.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft after he was identified by a county sheriff deputy as being seen leaving the building where a burglar alarm was triggered. At trial, defendant objected to the inclusion of the parole charge. At the end of the statutory parole instruction, the trial court gave an instruction telling the jury that they could not consider the manner which the parole law may be applied to defendant. The court found that the presumption that the jury followed was to totally disregard parole, coupled with defendant's prior extensive criminal record, lead to the conclusion that the statutory parole instruction did not affect defendant's sentence. The court applied the harm analysis required under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2), and held that defendant was convicted of a non-heinous crime, the enhancement paragraphs found true were for two non-violent crimes, burglary of a building with intent to commit theft and felony theft, and his punishment fell within the range of the allowed by statute. The court found beyond a reasonable doubt that the parole charge did not contribute to the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft, holding the presumption that the jury followed to totally disregard parole, coupled with defendant's extensive record, lead to the conclusion that the statutory parole instruction did not affect defendant's sentence. The court found beyond reasonable doubt that the parole charge did not contribute to the punishment assessed.

Gilliam v. State


No. 01-85-01053-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


766 S.W.2d 867; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 388



March 1, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 435,510.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged a judgment of the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault following the submission of parole law instructions to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault after the trial court submitted an instruction to the jury on the existence of the parole law pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 (1989). On appeal, the court found that art. 37.07 had been deemed unconstitutional, and it then stated that reversal was required under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) unless it determined, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the error made no contribution to the punishment assessed. The court concluded that the error was harmless and affirmed appellant's conviction. The court found that appellant not only did not object to the parole charge, he argued it as a fact in his favor. Moreover, he made his argument over the state's objection. Thus, the court held that the record reflected that inclusion of the unconstitutional parole charge was viewed at trial by both sides as favorable to appellant and harmful to the state. Under the facts of the case, the court found that it was apparently part of appellant's trial strategy to have the jury receive this charge.


OUTCOME: The court overruled appellant criminal defendant's sole point of error and affirmed his conviction for aggravated sexual assault because the trial court's error in submitting a parole law instruction to the jury made no contribution to appellant's punishment.

 

687 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Lynaugh


No. 12-88-00109-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


766 S.W.2d 393; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 362



February 28, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 17, 1989. Motion for Rehearing of Application for Writ of Error Overruled November 7, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 349th Judicial District Court of Anderson County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the order of the 349th Judicial District Court of Anderson County, Texas, dismissing his suit upon the trial court's determination that it was frivolous. Appellant alleged that appellee, Director of the Texas Department of Corrections (TDC), violated his rights guaranteed by the Texas Constitution. Appellant also contended that three TDC disciplinary rules were unconstitutionally void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate complained of a policy denying him a cassette player in his cell. He asserted that a tape player was necessary in order for him to meditate three times daily, a practice of his religion. Appellant claimed denial of a tape player violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 6, as well as § 19 (due process), § 13 (cruel or unusual punishment), and §§ 3 and 3a (equality under the law). He also contended that three disciplinary rules were unconstitutionally void for vagueness. The court, in affirming the dismissal of appellant's suit as frivolous, held that realistic chances of ultimate success for the claim were slight. Appellee Director of the Texas Department of Corrections (TDC) had the power to promulgate reasonable rules governing the treatment and discipline of prisoners with the consent of the TDC. The court held that a rule denying inmate's unfettered possession of objects, which could be used for weapons, was reasonable. The court held that appellant's complaint regarding the disciplinary rules was equally frivolous. Although he asserted that the rules were void for vagueness, appellant failed to allege or show how he was harmed by any of the rules.


OUTCOME: In affirming the order of the trial court, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in dismissing the cause as frivolous. The court further concluded that appellant, inmate's chance of succeeding on any of his allegations were slight, and that he did not have standing to litigate any matter regarding the rules.

The appellate court affirmed, finding that the parole law instruction mandated by Tex Code Crim. Proc. art. 37.07, § 4 was constitutional, and the Court of Criminal Appeals remanded for a harm analysis pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2).

In affirming, the court held that the parole law instruction mandated by Tex Code Crim. Proc. art. 37.07, § 4 was constitutional. The Court of Criminal Appeals reviewed and remanded the case to the court to conduct a harm analysis pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) and determine whether reversible error arose. It was necessary that a harm analysis be made in order to make the determination whether, beyond a reasonable doubt, the error in the charge made no contribution to defendant's conviction. The court concluded that no reversible error arose.

Myers v. State


No. C14-87-00999-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 347



February 23, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Overruled March 30, 1989 Petition for Discretionary Review Refused July 26, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 383,094


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of delivery of a controlled substance and sentenced him to five years of confinement, after a finding of probation violation, and a $ 750 fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for the offense of delivery of a controlled substance. He pled guilty and was given a probated sentence of five years' confinement and a $ 750 fine. Later, appellee state brought a motion to revoke probation, which the trial court granted. On appeal the court affirmed the trial court, holding that the trial judge was within her discretion to find that appellant had failed to report to his probation officer as ordered during three months, or to the required Alcoholics Anonymous meetings, given appellant's admission that he falsified the forms that would prove he attended. The court also held that the cover sheet, a copy of the indictment, and a specific recess taken by the trial court indicated that the trial court was laboring under the constitutionally correct range of punishment when she sentenced appellant. Finally the court held that substances containing quantities of barbituric acid were designated by name in the controlled substances act as a penalty group three drug, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.02(d)(2) (1988), so that it was not necessary for appellee to allege and prove that the drug was a controlled substance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's probation revocation and confinement because the record showed that appellant failed to attend monthly meetings with his probation officer or twice weekly Alcoholics Anonymous meetings, the trial court knew and applied the constitutionally correct range of punishment, and barbituric acid substances were designated by name as controlled substances, and did not have to be proved to be so.

General Life & Acci. Ins. Co. v. Handy


No. 08-88-00118-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


766 S.W.2d 370; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 337



February 22, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 358th District Court of Ector County, Texas. (TC# D-76,325), Hon. Bill McCoy, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer challenged an order of the 358th District Court of Ector County (Texas), which damages and attorney fees to appellee insured in appellee's claim for breach of contract, breach of the duty of good faith and fair dealing, violation of Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.21 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Appellee insured filed a claim against appellee insurer for breach of contract, breach of the duty of good faith and fair dealing, and violation of Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.21 (1981). Appellant denied coverage, contending that appellee's health condition was pre-existing. The lower court found in favor of appellee and awarded damages and attorney fees to appellee. Appellant challenged the ruling, contending that the evidence did not support the submission of special issues to the jury or the verdict and that the trial should have been severed. The court reformed the lower court's judgment by awarding attorney fees to appellee instead of his lawyer. The court affirmed the rest of the judgment, concluding that appellant waived some objections by failing to preserve them in the record, that the lower court had discretion to deny severance of issues at trial, and that interest of 10 percent was proper. Moreover, the evidence supported the submission of special issues to the jury and the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The court reformed the lower court's judgment for appellee insured in appellee's breach of contract action by changing the award of attorney fees to appellee policyholder instead of his attorney. Otherwise, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment due to appellant insurer's waiver of objections, and the fact that sufficient evidence supported both the submissions of special issues to the jury and the jury's verdict and judgment.

Bell v. State


No. C14-87-00219-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


768 S.W.2d 790; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 260



February 16, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Refused August 30, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Case No. 423,385.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), after a jury convicted him of the solicitation of another to commit capital murder and the trial court assessed punishment at 38 years confinement in the Texas Department of Corrections.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the solicitation of another to commit capital murder and the trial court assessed punishment at 38 years confinement in the Texas Department of Corrections. On appeal, the court affirmed. In reviewing the sufficiency of the evidence, the court found that the witness testimony, even disregarding the testimony of the alleged person who was solicited, sufficiently corroborated both the solicitation and defendant's intent that the murder be carried out. The trial court had not erred in not excluding evidence of several extraneous offenses because the evidence was admissible to show the context and circumstances surrounding the crime charged. The trial court's charge properly informed the jury under what circumstances they could have considered defendant's extraneous offenses. The trial court's charge properly informed the jury to consider the testimony of the solicited person only if they determined that his testimony was corroborated by evidence showing the solicitation itself and defendant's intent that he act on the solicitation. Any delays in bringing defendant to trial were caused by defendant and therefore he waived his right to speedy trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of the solicitation of another to commit capital murder. The court found that there was sufficient evidence of both the solicitation and defendant's intent that the murder be carried out, and that the evidentiary and discovery rulings, the trial court's jury charge, and the trial court's failure to dismiss the indictment on speedy trial grounds were proper.

Higginbotham v. State


No. B14-87-00422-CR


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, Fourteenth District, Houston


769 S.W.2d 265; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 264



February 16, 1989  
February 16, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Granted August 30, 1989. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied May 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 448,784.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas which convicted defendant of murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02 (1974), and sentenced appellant to 50 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a church where he shot and killed a pastor. Defendant subsequently surrendered to authorities and was arrested. At trial, defendant pled not guilty and raised the affirmative defense of insanity. After rejection of defendant's not guilty plea, defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to 50 years imprisonment. Defendant sought review of the decision alleging that the lower court erred in allowing his recorded confession into evidence because it was taken in violation of his right to counsel. The court affirmed and reformed the judgment holding that the totality of the circumstances did not show any waiver of defendant's request for counsel. The court held that the lower court did not commit reversible error by allowing in defendant's confession because there was an abundance of evidence demonstrating defendant's guilt and the state did not need the statement to establish that guilt. The court held that defendant did not receive notice of the state's intent to pursue a deadly weapon finding and therefore the affirmative deadly weapon finding could not be employed against defendant and was stricken from the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and reformed defendant's conviction of murder because the lower court did not commit reversible error by allowing into evidence defendant's recorded confession which was merely cumulative evidence of existing relevant facts. The court held that the deadly weapon finding should be stricken from the judgment because defendant never received notice of the state's intention to pursue a deadly weapon finding.

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 331ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 78,219, HONORABLE BOB PERKINS, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the 331st Judicial District, Travis County, Texas, which had convicted him of injury to a child. The Court of Criminal Appeals granted defendant's petition for discretionary review and vacated the judgment of the Court of Appeals of Texas, Third District, Austin, and remanded the case to that court for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of injury to a child and sentenced to a term of imprisonment of 65 years. Defendant was alleged to have beaten a 21-month old child for a period of a week, eventually resulting in the child's death. Defendant's conviction was affirmed on appeal, but vacated by the Court of Criminal Appeals after discretionary review of defendant's petition. The prosecution mentioned during the punishment stage of the trial of defendant's eligibility for parole which resulted in a motion for rehearing. On review, the court overruled the motion for rehearing and affirmed defendant's judgment of conviction. The court reasoned that the repeated brutality alleged to have been committed in this case by the defendant was the cause of defendant's lengthy sentence. The court found nothing to suggest that the jury ignored a trial court instruction to not consider how parole or good behavior would affect their sentence. Thus, the court found the prosecution's erroneous statement harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and overruled the motion for rehearing because the erroneous parole instruction was harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt and did not compel reversal of defendant's conviction.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Criminal District Court Jefferson County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision entered after a jury trial in the Criminal District Court Jefferson County, Texas, convicting defendant for the offense of burglary of a habitation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in a jury trial for the offense of burglary of a habitation and the jury assessed punishment at 99 years confinement. Defendant appealed and argued that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the law concerning good time and parole as the charge was based on an unconstitutional statute, Tex. Code Crim. Thus, reversal was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of defendant's conviction after a jury trial for the offense of burglary of habitation and remanded the cause for a new trial on the issue of punishment only. The lack of curative instruction was important in the determination of whether the error of submitting an unconstitutional parole law instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.

697 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Barzar v. State


No. 01-88-00161-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 211



February 9, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by, 05/24/1989
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Barzar v. Thaler, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 93090 (S.D. Tex., May 29, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 209th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 479,102


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the 209th District Court, Harris County, Texas, after a jury found him guilty of capital murder and the trial court assessed punishment at life imprisonment for intentionally and knowingly causing the death of two persons during the same criminal transaction by shooting them with a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder for intentionally and knowingly causing the death of two persons during the same criminal transaction by shooting them with a firearm. The trial court assessed punishment at life imprisonment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The indictment was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness because the indictment properly alleged an act prohibited by statute and defendant failed to show that it was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him. In reviewing the sufficiency of evidence, the court found that the evidence supported a finding that a pistol, admittedly fire by defendant, was used in a deadly manner, and that defendant intentionally and knowingly caused the two victims to be shot in the head, resulting in their deaths. The trial court had not erred in refusing defendant's requested instruction on the lesser-included offenses because there was no evidence that defendant was guilty of only the lesser-included offenses. The trial court had not erred in dismissing a prospective juror for cause because he failed to meet the requirement of the ability to write and express his ideas in writing where he was unable to fill out juror questionnaire.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital murder and the trial court's assessment of life imprisonment as punishment. The court held that the indictment was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness, there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction, the trial court's refusal to submit defendant's instruction on lesser-included offenses was not improper, and the dismissal of a prospective juror for cause was not improper.

King v. Bauer


No. 13-87-548-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


767 S.W.2d 197; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 226



February 9, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] April 6, 1989, Motion for Rehearing Overruled. Application for Writ of Error Denied September 6, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 135th District Court of Victoria County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged the order of the 135th District Court, Victoria County, Texas, which rendered judgment for appellee doctor in appellant's malpractice action for negligence in the administration of radiation therapy.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient brought a malpractice action against appellee doctor for negligence in the administration of radiation therapy. The lower court entered a take-nothing judgment against appellant after the jury's finding against her. Appellant challenged the judgment, and the court affirmed. The court found that the lower court did not err in refusing to consider the testimony of the juror in appellant's claim of jury misconduct because the juror's affidavit did not raise an issue of outside influence as required. The court held that the rules regulating jury deliberations were not unconstitutional as a violation of the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. 1, § 13 because appellant had her day in court and her substantive right to have her dispute heard was not denied. The court held that the lower court did not err in admitting portions of a textbook that was published after the incident because the information was relevant, admissible, and material to the informed consent negligence issue. The court determined that the jury's finding was not against the weight or preponderance of the evidence, and the judgment was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for appellee doctor in appellant's malpractice action because there was no evidence of jury misconduct, the rules dealing with jury misconduct were not unconstitutional, and the jury's finding was not against the preponderance of the evidence.

 

699 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Goodlow v. State


No. 6-88-038-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


766 S.W.2d 352; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 199



February 8, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 28, 1989. Petition for Discretionary Review Refused August 30, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 276th Judicial District Court of Titus County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the 276th District Court, Titus County, Texas, for delivery of marihuana of less than four ounces but more than one-quarter of an ounce.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, convicted of delivery of marihuana of less than four ounces but more than one-quarter of an ounce, appealed. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial based upon an impermissible jury argument at the punishment stage of the trial. On remand, the trial court granted the state's motion to proceed to the punishment stage of the trial; a jury assessed defendant's punishment and defendant appealed. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that defendant had no right to a new trial on the guilt-innocence stage as there was no harmful error in defendant's first trial on guilt or innocence, and he was not entitled to two error-free trials on guilt or innocence. The court found that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.29(b) did not deprive defendant of his right to appeal as the error in the first trial occurred only in the punishment stage and art. 44.29(b) required the trial court to proceed to trial at the punishment stage; defendant failed to file a motion for rehearing or seek further review on the points of error overruled by the court; and defendant was not retroactively deprived of a substantive right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, holding that defendant was not entitled to two error-free trials on guilt or innocence as the error in his first trial was in the punishment stage only. The court found that defendant was not deprived of his right to appeal but failed to exercise the right by not filing a motion for rehearing or seeking further review on the points of error overruled by the court after the first trial.

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 85th District Court, Brazos County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 14,322


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the 85th District Court, Brazos County, Texas, which denied his application for writ of habeas corpus regarding his conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife reported to the police that defendant had committed a sexual assault on her daughter. Defendant approached an officer at the police station, who was unaware of the report, and confessed that he had sexual relations with his stepdaughter. Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a child. Defendant filed a writ of habeas corpus on the grounds that he was immune from prosecution under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 34.03 (1986), which was denied by the trial court. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and held that defendant's report of his own conduct was not grounds for immunity under § 34.03 because a statement made by the perpetrator of child abuse, which was the same as a confession, was not a nonaccusatory report as set forth within the statute. The court overruled defendant's second contention that § 34.03 was unconstitutionally vague because, as written, § 34.03 excluded self-reporting child abuse offenders from immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child. The court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus because defendant's report of his own conduct was not grounds for statutory immunity because a statement made by the perpetrator of child abuse, which was the same as a confession, was not a nonaccusatory report as set forth within the pertinent statute.

Watt v. State


No. B14-86-00868-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 157



February 2, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 122nd District Court, Galveston County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 85-CR-650


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 122nd District Court, Galveston County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1989). He challenged his conviction, alleging that the trial court's parole instruction under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 constituted reversible error. The court disagreed, and affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the parole instruction was unconstitutional but that the error was harmless. The court applied the following factors for determining whether the error was harmless under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) : (1) whether a curative instruction was given; (2) whether the prosecution invited consideration of the instruction; (3) whether the facts of the offense militated in favor of the sentence imposed; and (4) whether the defendant had a history of prior felony convictions. Finding that the unconstitutional instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt and made no contribution to the punishment assessed, the court held that there was no reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that the jury instructions did not constitute reversible error because they were harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, made no contribution to the punishment assessed, and the facts of the case militated in favor of the assessed punishment.

Burgess v. State


No. 01-87-01103-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 160



February 2, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 27, 1989; Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 27, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 973,002


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County, Texas, which entered a judgment of conviction for a misdemeanor offense of resisting arrest, Tex. Penal Code § 38.03, after defendant allegedly attempted to grab a uniformed officer's gun while the officer was attempting to restrain defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for resisting arrest, a misdemeanor offense under Cal. Penal Code § 38.03, after he allegedly attempted to take a uniformed officer's gun while the officer attempted to restrain defendant to investigate a possible auto theft. The court affirmed the conviction because there was sufficient evidence to prove the offense, and the jury was not bound to accept defendant's testimony that he was unaware that he was being apprehended by a police officer. The court found that a failure to define terms in § 38.03 such as "arrest" was at most harmless error and the admission of evidence of the extraneous offense of auto theft was proper to show the context in which the resisting arrest offense occurred. The court further found that defendant's own testimony as to whether he knew of the police officer's status abrogated the necessity of a defensive instruction of mistake of fact or other defenses. The court held that a motion to suppress filed on the day of trial was untimely and properly denied, and any error in the examination of witnesses was not preserved. The court found that § 38.03 was not unconstitutionally vague and gave fair notice of prohibited acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for resisting arrest because the evidence was sufficient to support a finding of guilt where defendant attempted to grab an officer's gun while being restrained. The court found that the jury was not obligated to believe that defendant was unaware of the uniformed officer's status, and that evidence of an extraneous offense was properly admitted to show the context in which the criminal act occurred.

Plilar v. State


Nos. 01-88-00757-CR, 01-88-00758-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 164



February 2, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law #13 of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 88-18804 and 88-17000


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the County Criminal Court at Law #13 of Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of two misdemeanor offenses of selling obscene material, alleging that the Texas Obscenity Statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 (1988), was unconstitutionally vague, and therefore void, and that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash because there was no timely and proper determination of obscenity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two misdemeanor offenses of selling obscene material. Defendant alleged that the Texas Obscenity Statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 (1988), was unconstitutionally vague, and therefore void, and that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash because there was no timely and proper determination of obscenity. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and overruled his points of error, holding that defendant failed to allege or argue any deficiency of § 43.21 and therefore the court would not engage in a search for unconstitutionality. The court also held that it lacked jurisdiction to consider defendant's argument that an independent, pre-arrest, judicial determination of obscenity was a prerequisite of a constitutional prosecution for the sale of obscene material. The court found that because § 43.21 tracked the Miller test for obscenity and did not inject considerations of community standards into the separate determination of the work's value, it passed constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and overruled his points of error, holding that the court would not engage in a search for unconstitutionality because defendant failed to allege or argue any statutory deficiency and found that the statute used to convict defendant passed constitutional muster because it tracked the Miller test for obscenity.

Thibeadeau v. State


No. 09-86-142 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


765 S.W.2d 538; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 497



February 1, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 75TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LIBERTY COUNTY, TEXAS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) remanded the matter to the court to conduct a "harmless error analysis," pursuant to the guidelines of Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) regarding the trial court's instruction to the jury on the law concerning good time and parole because that type of instruction had been deemed unconstitutional by the Court of Criminal Appeals.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for possession of marijuana and cocaine after police discovered the drugs when they pulled defendant over for speeding and smelled the strong odor of marijuana. At trial, the trial court gave an instruction to the jury which allowed them to speculate with regard to the amount of time that would be served. The appellate criminal court remanded the matter to the court to determine whether defendant's conviction should be affirmed or reversed in light of a recent decision by the appellate criminal court regarding the fact that this type of instruction was based on an unconstitutional statute. On appeal, the court held that the situation and facts in the present case were entirely different from that in the recent appellate criminal court opinion. The court also held that the jury reached the correct verdict. However, the court held that its hands were tied by the recent appellate criminal court opinion which simply forbade the verdict to stand. Therefore, the court reversed and remanded as to the punishment phase of the proceeding only, because the court held that it could not be said that the charge had no effect whatsoever on the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court as to the punishment phase only because its hands were tied due to a recent opinion by the appellate criminal court and the court could not say with certainty that the instruction given to the jury about good time and parole did not have any effect on the punishment given to defendant.

Fisher v. State


No. B14-86-00254-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 104



January 26, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 208th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 435,046


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 208th District Court, Harris County, Texas, convicting him of attempted sexual assault on a minor. Appellant challenged the trial court's instruction to the jury on the law of parole pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of attempted sexual assault on a minor. Appellant challenged his conviction, and alleged that the trial court's jury instruction on the law of parole pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4 was erroneous. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court found that an analysis under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) was required to determine whether reversible error resulted from the erroneous parole law jury instruction. The court held that under that analysis, a trial court's instruction to a jury pursuant to the now unconstitutional statute would require reversal unless the court determined beyond a reasonable doubt that the charge made no contribution to either conviction or punishment. After the required analysis, the court found that the trial court's curative parole law instructions, the facts of the case, the absence of reference to the parole law by the state and appellant's prior felony conviction all led to the conclusion, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the parole charge, although erroneous, made no contribution to appellant's conviction or punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of attempted sexual assault on a minor because the trial court's curative parole law instructions, the case facts, the absence of reference to the parole law by the prosecutor, and appellant's prior felony conviction led to the conclusion, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the parole charge, although erroneous, made no contribution to appellant's conviction or punishment.

Paxton v. State


No. B14-86-00404-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 115



January 26, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 445,557


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which found defendant guilty of attempted burglary of a building by prying a window, because of the trial court's instruction to the jury on the law of parole pursuant to Tex. OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted burglary of a building by prying a window. Defendant pleaded true to the forgery and burglary of building felonies alleged as enhancement and the jury assessed punishment at ninety-nine years' confinement. The criminal appeals court vacated and remanded the case back to the court for a harmless error analysis under the guidelines of Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2), after the court had affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court affirmed, and found beyond a reasonable doubt that the jury instruction on the law of parole pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4, although an error, had not contributed to the sentence and was therefore harmless. The court considered the fact that a curative admonishment instructing the jury not to consider the effect of parole on any sentence had been read, and that the record had not reflected or even suggested that any juror did otherwise, defendant's determined attempt to break into the complainant's home militated in favor of the sentence imposed, and the fact that defendant had five prior felony convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and held that the erroneous jury instruction was considered harmless error, because it found beyond a reasonable doubt that the error had not contributed to the sentence of defendant after the court considered the curative instruction read to the jury, defendant's offense, and defendant's five prior convictions.

Gunther v. State


Nos. 13-87-515-CR, 13-87-517-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


764 S.W.2d 903; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 128



January 26, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Court Court at Law No. 3 of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Court at Law No. 3 of Nueces County (Texas), convicting him pursuant to a plea of guilty for the offense of failing to timely submit an invoice to the Texas Parks and Wildlife Department pursuant to 31 Tex. Admin. Code § 57.372 (1988).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted pursuant to a guilty plea for failing to timely submit an invoice, pertaining to the intrastate shipment of redfish, to the Texas Parks and Wildlife Department. On appeal, the court found that 31 Tex. Admin. Code § 57.376 (1988), as adopted by the Texas Parks and Wildlife Commission and as applied, was inconsistent with Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 66.201(f) (1989) as adopted by the legislature. Under 31 Tex. Admin. Code § 57.372(e)(1) (1988) an invoice was required to accompany all intrastate shipments of redfish and § 57.372(f) provided that failure to comply would be a Class A misdemeanor. The court, in reversing and remanding, held that § 57.376 was unconstitutional because its requirement of a Class A misdemeanor exceeded the penalty of a Class C misdemeanor which the legislature set forth in Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 66.201(f). The court found defendant's contention that Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 66.201 (1989) was unconstitutional because it delegated to an administrative agency the power to make a law prescribing a penalty to be without merit because the legislature itself mandated the failure to account for an invoice was unlawful.


OUTCOME: The order sentencing defendant for failure to timely submit an invoice to the parks and wildlife department was reversed and the issue remanded for a new punishment hearing because the regulatory statute defendant violated was unconstitutional in that its penalty classification exceeded that proscribed by the legislature.

 

709 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Diggles v. Horwitz


No. 09-87-192 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


765 S.W.2d 839; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 526



January 26, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE 172ND DISTRICT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY, TEXAS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, wife and child of man who committed suicide with a handgun, appealed from order of 172nd District Court of Jefferson County, Texas, which granted summary judgment to appellees, owner of store that sold the handgun to the man and the gun's manufacturer, in appellants' personal injury suit against appellees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant wife's husband committed suicide after purchasing a gun from appellee storeowner that was manufactured by appellee manufacturer. Appellant wife, individually and on behalf of her minor child, filed a personal injury suit against appellees. The trial court granted appellees' summary judgment motions. The court reversed the summary judgment for the storeowner. While suicide generally constituted an intervening force that broke the line of causation from the wrongful act to the death, it was not an absolute bar. Although the storeowner alleged suicide as the sole cause of death in his summary judgment motion, he gave no proof in his brief in support of the motion. Thus, summary judgment could not be sustained on this ground. There were fact issues relating to another ground for summary judgment raised by the storeowner. The court affirmed the summary judgment for the manufacturer. There was evidence that all it did was manufacture the gun. The sale of handguns was not an ultrahazardous activity for purposes of strict liability in tort. There was no duty to warn the storeowner of the dangers of handguns because the manufacturer submitted proof that he knew of such dangers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment for storeowner because there was no evidence to support his affirmative defense of suicide and because there were fact issues relating to his other ground for summary judgment. It affirmed summary judgment for manufacturer because it had no duty to control improper use of firearms.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his murder conviction from the 230th District Court Harris County (Texas), challenging the sufficiency of the evidence to prove his intent beyond a reasonable doubt and alleging that the trial court committed reversible error because the jury charge contained both counts of the indictment in one paragraph.

Further, the verdict was upheld because there was sufficient evidence to support a finding under the charge, which alleged different ways of committing the same offense of murder rather than different offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's murder conviction, concluding that there was sufficient evidence to prove appellant's intent beyond a reasonable doubt and to support the jury's finding under either of the two different ways of committing the offense of murder contained in the charge.
