714 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Flowers v. Lavaca County Appraisal Dist.


No. 13-88-455-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


766 S.W.2d 825; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 78



January 19, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 9, 1989. Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 16, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 25th District Court of Lavaca County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the order of the 25th District Court of Lavaca County (Texas) granting judgment to appellee Lavaca County Appraisal District for six years of delinquent taxes on an automobile. Appellant claimed lack of jurisdiction, statute of limitations, lack of evidence showing appellee's jurisdiction over the automobile and of authority, and other procedural errors.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer disputed the six years delinquent ad valorem taxes assessed by appellee Lavaca County Appraisal District, and appealed the trial court decision awarding appellee $ 364.75. Rejecting appellant's argument that the amount involved did not meet the minimum under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 33.41 (1982), the court ruled that the trial court retained jurisdiction because appellant never alleged the valuation was made in bad faith or fraudulently. However, the court rejected appellee's argument that Tex. Const. art. III, § 55 permitted its suit for all six years, saying that Tex. Prop. Tax Code § 33.05 (Supp. 1989) set the limit at four years. Therefore, the court reversed the decision for two of the years, and affirmed liability for the other years. The court added that appellant waived wrongful inclusion of his property by failing to exhaust his administrative remedies and waived any complaint under Tex. R. Civ. P. 296. The court also held that a compilation of delinquent taxes was admissible under Tex. Prop. Tax Code § 33.47(a) (Supp. 1989).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision on appellant taxpayer's liability for two years of taxes because barred by the statute of limitations, but affirmed liability for the other four years, and remanded for a determination of the amounts due in the cause brought by appellee Lavaca County Appraisal District for delinquent taxes. The court held the trial court had jurisdiction and a compilation from the delinquent tax rolls was admissible.

 

715 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. State


Nos. 05-87-01281-CR, 05-87-01282-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


764 S.W.2d 367; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 294



January 13, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF COLLIN COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the District Court of Collin County, Texas, which convicted him of arson and solicitation of capital murder and assessed punishment at 20 years and 75 years respectively.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of arson and solicitation of capital murder. On review, appellant contended that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 15.03(a) (1974) was unconstitutionally vague, the indictment was defective, the evidence was insufficient to sustain the arson conviction, a motion to quash should have been granted, and an objection to jury argument should have been sustained. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and held that § 15.03(a) was not vague, indefinite or uncertain. The court found that appellant made no objection to the indictment at trial, and because he failed to object within the time specified in Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 1.14(a) (1989), he waived his right to raise any objection to the indictment on appeal. The court concluded that any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of arson as defined in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 28.02(a)(2) (1989).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision to convict appellant of arson and solicitation of capital murder because appellant waived his right to raise any objection to a solicitation indictment on appeal, and the essential elements of arson could have been found by any rational trier of fact.

 

716 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


James v. State


No. A14-86-00103-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 18



January 12, 1989 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 436,345


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the 337th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of robbery. Defendant claimed that the trial court's inclusion of jury charge on a parole, mandated by statute that was declared unconstitutional, constituted reversible error.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's trial for robbery, the trial court instructed the jury on the parole law as mandated by statute, which was later held unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence and held that the instruction did not contribute beyond a reasonable doubt to defendant's conviction or sentence, where a curative instruction was given and the closing statements did not reference the charge. The court further held that the evidence at trial was substantial enough to warrant conviction and militate in favor of the sentence imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the trial court's inclusion of a jury charge on a parole, mandated by a statute which was declared unconstitutional, did not contribute beyond a reasonable doubt to defendant's conviction or sentence.

 

717 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Eiland v. Wolf


No. 01-87-00266-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


764 S.W.2d 827; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 42



January 12, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 212th District Court, Galveston County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86CV1311.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state medical college and its officials, challenged the order of the 212th District Court of Galveston County (Texas), directing appellants to award appellee student his medical degree and declaring invalid appellant college's determination to dismiss student for poor academic performance.


OVERVIEW: Trial court held that academic dismissal of appellee student by appellants, state medical college and its officials, violated the student's constitutional rights of procedural and substantive due process and equal protection, as well as a contract between the student and appellant college created by the college catalog. On appeal, the court reversed and held that, in light of the limited role allowed to the trial court in reviewing academic decisions of educational institutions, as well as a de novo review of trial record, appellant college and its officials did not exceed their authority in dismissing the student for academic reasons. The court also held that, regarding the student's contract claim, appellants' defense of sovereign immunity had been waived by appellants' failure to plead it as an affirmative defense; however, the court held that no contract arose out of appellant college's catalogue.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the injunction against appellants, state medical college and its officials, reversed the trial court's judgment, and rendered judgment against appellee student in his action to compel appellants to award him a medical degree. Appellants' academic dismissal of student did not violate due process or equal protection, and no contract existed between the parties preventing academic dismissal.

 

718 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Texas Dep't of Human Servs. v. Methodist Retirement Servs.


No. 3-88-110-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


763 S.W.2d 613; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 202



January 11, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NOS. 428,927 AND 429,202, HONORABLE PETE LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state human services department sought review of the judgment of the 147th Judicial District Court, Travis County, Texas, which awarded attorney's fees to appellee corporations in a contract dispute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state human services department challenged the judgment of the trial court that awarded attorney's fees to appellee corporations in a contract dispute. Appellant contended that the trial court was without statutory authority to award attorney's fees under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 37.009, 104.001. The court reversed and held that appellant was immune from liability for attorney's fees except when that immunity was waived by clear statutory authority under § 104.001. The court found that § 104.001 did not waive the state's immunity from liability for attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that the trial court erred in awarding attorney's fees to appellee corporation when appellant state human services department was immune from liability.

 

719 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. 05-86-00541-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


763 S.W.2d 926; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 309



January 10, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 10, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS, Criminal District Court #1, Dallas, Texas, Judge Ron Chapman.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted appellant of arson, and a punishment was assessed at 15 years of confinement in state prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of arson The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the parole law instruction mandated by Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 37.01, § 4 was constitutional. This was error, and the cause was remanded to the court to conduct a harm analysis of the error pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2). The court held that no reversible error arose and affirmed appellant's conviction. The court concluded, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the trial court's error in charging the jury, as mandated by Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 37.01, § 4, made no contribution to the punishment that was assessed by the jury. The court held that if the laboring party failed to meet its burden, the court would overrule or sustain points of error, asserting that the trial court's error in charging the jury, as mandated by art. 37.07, § 4, made a contribution to the punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of arson and held that there was no reversible error because the trial court's parole law jury instruction mandated by Tex. Crim. Proc. Code was harmless and did not contribute to the punishment that was assessed by the jury.

 

720 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Skeen v. Tunnell


No. 12-88-00313-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


768 S.W.2d 765; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 14



January 6, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ORIGINAL PROCEEDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator state sought writ of mandamus to compel respondent judge of a district court (Texas), to set aside his order which reinstated a prospective juror, who was peremptorily struck by relator, and to call a new array in the case.


OVERVIEW: Relator state exercised one of its peremptory challenges against a black venireman. Respondent judge determined that the venireman had been challenged on the basis of race. Relator sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent to set aside his order reinstating the venireman and to call a new array in the case. The could held that it would issue the writ of mandamus if respondent did not set aside his oral orders that reinstated the venireman, quash the venire of which the venireman was a member, and summon a new panel of jurors. The court ruled that Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 35.261(b) (1989), which required a trial court to call a new array in a case when it determined that an attorney representing the state challenged a juror on the basis of race, was mandatory, and its enforcement did not violate U.S. Const. amends. V, VI, or XIV, or Tex. Const. art. II, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court held that it would issue a writ of mandamus if respondent judge did not set aside his orders reinstating a venireman because it was mandatory that respondent call a new array in the case once he determined that relator state challenged a potential juror on the basis of race.

 

721 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Texas State Bd. of Dental Examiners v. Silagi


No. 08-88-00165-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


766 S.W.2d 280; 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 207



January 5, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled February 8, 1989, Reported at: 766 S.W.2d 280 at 285.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 120th District Court of El Paso County, Texas, TC# 86-1517.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Texas State Board of Dental Examiners challenged an order of the 120th District Court of El Paso County (Texas), which overruled appellant's order that revoked the dental license of appellee dentist.


OVERVIEW: Appellee dentist was charged with failure to use proper diligence in the conduct of his dental practice, negligence, and malpractice after one of his patient's died. Appellant Texas State Board of Dental Examiners revoked his license, but the trial court overruled its order. The court reversed the judgment and rendered judgment affirming appellant's order revoking the dental license of appellee. The court held that appellant's findings adequately expressed factual matter based upon the evidence sufficient to support their conclusions of law. The court found that Tex. Admin. Code and Tex. Reg. art. 6252-13a, § 13(a), which provided for reasonable notice prior to a hearing, were not unconstitutionally infirm; there was substantial compliance by appellant, and the exception to complaint filed by appellee was untimely.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a decision to overrule appellant Texas State Board of Dental Examiners' order revoking appellee dentist's license because appellant's findings expressed factual matter based upon the evidence and was sufficient to support their conclusions of law.

 

722 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Friedrich Air Conditioning & Refrigeration Co. v. Bexar Appraisal Dist.


Appeal No. 04-88-00265-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


762 S.W.2d 763; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3362



December 30, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] January 12, 1989, As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 225th District Court of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 87-CI-11707, Honorable David Peeples, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company challenged a judgment of the 225th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) that granted cross-motion of appellees, appraisal district and appraisal review board, for summary judgment in appellant's action challenging appellee appraisal review board's order that adversely determined appellant's tax protest; appellees challenged the court's finding that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.01(d) (1982) was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee appraisal district found that certain property it had previously found to be exempt from taxation, under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.01(d) (1982), the free-port law, had escaped taxation in the two previous tax years. Appellee district appraised the omitted property and sent notice of the appraised value to appellant company. Appellant protested. Appellee appraisal review board upheld appellee district's appraisal. Appellant challenged appellee board's order in the trial court. Appellees counterclaimed for a declaratory judgment that the free-port law was unconstitutional. The trial court expressly upheld the constitutionality of the free-port law. On cross-motions for summary judgment, the trial court granted summary judgment to appellees. On appeal and cross-appeal, the appellate court affirmed. Appellees met their burden on cross-motion for summary judgment of establishing that the presumption of exemption from taxation under the free-port law was rebutted. Hence, the trial court should not have reached the constitutionality question.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellees, appraisal district and appraisal review board; appellees met their burden on cross-motion for summary judgment, and the trial court should not have reached the constitutionality question raised by appellees.

 

723 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Moinzadeh v. State


Nos. B14-87-00734-CR, C14-87-00735-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3182



December 29, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 13, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 947,037 & 951,098


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 13, Harris County (Texas) which, on pleas of nolo contendere, convicted appellant of two offenses of obscenity, violations of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two offenses of obscenity under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1). Appellant raised two points of error, asserting that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motion to quash the informations. In his first point of error appellant attacked the constitutionality of the state's obscenity statute maintaining that the statute made the basis of his prosecution indefinite, uncertain, and vague. In his second point of error, appellant contended that the statute was violative of U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. The court affirmed, finding that appellant failed to preserve error. The court held that a point of error, which did not comport with the objection made at trial, failed to preserve anything for review. Here, appellant's motions to quash complaint did not mention the state's obscenity statute at all, instead mounting an attack upon a city adult arcade ordinance. The trial court was never confronted with the questions of whether the state's obscenity statute, which served as the basis of these prosecutions, was void for vagueness or whether that statute was constitutionally infirm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's obscenity convictions because appellant failed to preserve error. Appellant raised points of error which did not comport with his objections at trial.

 

724 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hermosa v. State


No. B14-88-00227-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3208



December 29, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 973,207


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convict sought review of his conviction that was entered in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5, Harris County (Texas), on one charge of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1), and his sentence of confinement for four days and fine of $ 650.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant convict on one charge of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1). Appellant challenged the conviction and his sentence of four days confinement and a fine of $ 650. Appellant asserted that the obscenity law was void for vagueness and that the trial court erred in its denial of his pre-trial motions to quash the information because there was not a timely and proper determination of obscenity. The court affirmed and found that appellant failed to specify which part of the statute was vague. The court also noted that appellant failed to direct attention to any statutory language that he alleged to be indefinite, vague or uncertain. There was nothing in the record that supported appellant's contention that there was no prior judicial determination of probable cause with respect the whether the allegedly obscene material sold by appellant was in fact obscene. The court held that the statutory standard of obscenity mirrored the federal standard in that it regulated works taken as a whole and determined by the average person who applied contemporary community standards to have appealed to a prurient interest in sex.


OUTCOME: A conviction on one count of obscenity was affirmed because appellant convict failed to specify language in the obscenity statute that was indefinite, uncertain, or vague, because the record did not reflect appellant's contention that there was no probable cause determination with respect to whether the material sold by appellant was obscene, and because the state definition of obscenity mirrored the federal definition.

Smith v. State

729 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Spring Branch I.S.D. v. Reynolds


No. 01-87-00375-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


764 S.W.2d 16; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3229



December 29, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 295th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 87-16348.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, school district, association, and agency, sought review of a judgment from the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas), enjoining appellants from preventing appellee student from participating in high school track and field competition. Appellee moved to dismiss for mootness.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, school district, association, and agency, declared appellee student ineligible for extracurricular activities under Tex. Educ. Code § 21.920 (1987) when appellee failed a course. The lower court enjoined appellants from preventing appellee's participation in a track competition because appellee did not receive statutory notice of his failing grade, and track was not an extracurricular activity under 19 Tex. Admin. Code § 97.113(m). On review, appellee moved to dismiss on mootness grounds. The court found that appellee's graduation extinguished actual controversy. The "capable of repetition, yet evading review" exception to the mootness doctrine did not apply because appellee challenged section 97.113(m). Appellee agency could avoid repetition and review by changing its rules. The court rejected appellants' claim of collateral consequences to persons who would have received a medal but for appellee's competition participation. Appellants would not suffer collateral consequences, and the potentially aggrieved persons had not joined suit. Further, collateral consequences contemplated serious prejudice. Appellee's motion was granted and the injunction was vacated.


OUTCOME: Appeal of an injunction preventing appellants, school district, association, and agency, from preventing appellee student's participation in a track competition after he failed a course was dismissed. Appellee's graduation extinguished the actual controversy and rendered the case moot. The "capable of repetition, yet evading review" and collateral consequences exceptions to the mootness doctrine did not apply.

 

730 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Tartali v. State


Nos. 01-88-00561-CR, 01-88-00562-CR, 01-88-00563-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3234



December 29, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law Number Nine, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 8816033, 8816032, 8816031


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an order from the County Court at Law Number Nine, Harris County (Texas), where appellants were convicted of operating a sexually oriented business without a permit in violation of Houston, Tex., Ordinance ch. 28, art. III, § 28-122(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellants pled guilty to the misdemeanor offense of conducting sexually oriented enterprises without a permit and were sentenced to 25 days confinement. On review, appellants asserted that Houston, Tex., Ordinance ch. 28, art. III, § 28-122(a) was unconstitutionally vague and that the county court lacked jurisdiction over the case. The court affirmed appellants' convictions. According to the court, when challenging the constitutionality of a statute or ordinance, it was incumbent upon appellants to show that in its operation, the statute or ordinance was unconstitutional to them in their situation. The court held that the fact that the statute could be unconstitutional as applied to others was not sufficient. The court stated that appellants did not have standing to challenge the statute because appellants did not demonstrate or even allege that the ordinance was unconstitutional as it was applied to them. Next, the court held that the county court had jurisdiction over the case because a violation of section 28-122(a) was a class B misdemeanor and jurisdiction over class B misdemeanors lied with the county court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' convictions for operating a sexually oriented enterprise without a permit because appellants did not have standing to argue that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and because the county court had jurisdiction over the case.

Beavers v. State


Nos. B14-87-00743-CR, C14-87-00744-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3241



December 29, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 13, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 944,627 & 944,628


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 13, Harris County (Texas), which entered pleas of nolo contendere to charges of obscenity, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1). Defendant contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that his pretrial motions to quash the information should have been granted because there was not a timely and proper determination of obscenity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of obscenity, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1). The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that the obscenity statute complied with the constitutional requirements and that defendant failed to point out what specific portions of the statute were unconstitutionally vague. The court found that defendant neither alleges nor argued how the statute reached constitutionally protected conduct. The court held that the definition of obscenity contained at Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(1) complied with constitutional standards because it applied an "average person" standard that was not in any way linked to a determination of the value of the work.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for obscenity. The court held that the obscenity statute was not unconstitutionally vague and that the obscenity standard was constitutional because it applied an "average person" standard that was not in any way linked to a determination of the value of the work.

Roeder v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


768 S.W.2d 745; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3266



December 29, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 6, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 275,540


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 182nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of first-degree murder after a plea of nolo contendere and sentenced him to confinement for life.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after a co-conspirator informed the police of defendant's involvement in a robbery, kidnapping, and murder plot. Defendant was tried and convicted of capital murder. On appeal the conviction was overturned and defendant was retried. At his second trial he pleaded nolo contendere. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to life in prison. Defendant appealed his conviction and the court reversed and remanded for a new trial, holding that evidence seized from defendant's apartment without a warrant and in the absence of emergency circumstances was illegally obtained and should have been excluded. The court further held that the error in admitting that evidence was not harmless because it linked defendant to the crimes committed. The court also held that defendant was illegally arrested because there was no crime charged at the time of the arrest and no independent finding of probable cause sufficient to allow arrest without a warrant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's first-degree murder conviction and remanded the case for a new trial, holding that defendant's apartment was illegally searched without a warrant, and that defendant was illegally arrested without a warrant or an independent assessment of probable cause.

 

735 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Houston v. 2618, Inc.


No. 01-87-00192-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3373



December 29, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion on Rehearing dated November 3, 1988 Withdrawn and Substituted; Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 2, 1989; Application for Writ of Error Denied September 6, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86-52952


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant government challenged an order from the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which issued an injunction ordering appellant to issue a permit to appellee business to operate a sexually oriented business.


OVERVIEW: Appellee business sought declaratory and injunctive relief against appellant government asserting that appellant had misconstrued and misapplied the provisions of Houston, Tex., Ordinance 86-323, § 2, which resulted in a deprivation of appellee's rights. The trial court granted appellee relief and an appeal ensued. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and dissolved the injunction. According to the court, it was well settled that a court of equity could not enjoin the enforcement of a penal ordinance unless the ordinance was unconstitutional or otherwise void and the enforcement of the ordinance caused irreparable injury to vested property rights. The court held that because the ordinance was a penal statute, the court lacked jurisdiction to issue the injunction because appellee expressly stated that it was not contending that the ordinance was unconstitutional or otherwise void. The court continued and held that the rule denying injunctive relief against enforcement of the criminal laws applies with equal force to a declaratory action construing a penal ordinance. The court stated that a mere allegation that a penal ordinance was misapplied did not confer jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the injunction ordering appellant government to issue a permit to appellee business to operate a sexually oriented business because the court lacked jurisdiction to issue injunctive and declaratory relief against a penal ordinance. According to the court, a court of equity could not enjoin the enforcement of a penal ordinance unless the ordinance was unconstitutional or caused irreparable injury to vested property rights.

 

736 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


International Asso. of Firefighters, Local Union No. 399 v. Beaumont


No. 09-88-010 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


763 S.W.2d 57; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3386



December 29, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled January 18, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 60TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant union sought relief from a judgment from the 60th Judicial District, Jefferson County (Texas), which authorized an ordinance that repealed an earlier ordinance that provided for binding arbitration in collective bargaining impasses between appellant and appellee city.


OVERVIEW: Voters adopted the Fire and Police Employee Relations Act (FPERA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5154c-1 (1987), which gave firefighters and policemen the right to organize for purposes of collective bargaining. Furthermore, FPERA prohibited strikes and provided "reasonable alternatives" to the right to strike. Subsequently, the lower court authorized an ordinance that repealed an earlier ordinance of appellee city that required binding arbitration in collective bargaining impasses between appellant union and appellee. Appellant argued that the repealing ordinance conflicted with FPERA, which was state law. The court held that an ordinance could not be legally enacted by the governing body of a city which conflicted or was inconsistent with a state statute; however, the court found that, because nothing in FPERA required binding arbitration, the ordinance which repealed the ordinance requiring binding arbitration was not inconsistent with FPERA. As such, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment authorizing an ordinance which repealed an earlier ordinance requiring binding arbitration in collective bargaining impasses between appellant union and appellee city, holding that nothing in the Fire and Police Employee Relations Act required binding arbitration; therefore, the authorized ordinance did not conflict with state law.

Ybarra v. State


Appeal Nos. 04-87-00505-CR, 04-87-00506-CR, 04-87-00507-CR, 04-87-00508-CR, 04-87-00509-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


762 S.W.2d 368; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3349



December 28, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeals from County Court No. 5 of Bexar County, Trial Court Nos. 369,733, 356,832, 394,896, 360,732, 389,831, Honorable Tim Johnson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction that was entered in the County Court No. 5 of Bexar County (Texas), of five counts of selling obscene videotapes to police officers in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1), and his sentence of six days in jail and $ 150 fine for each count.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction in the trial court of five counts of selling obscene videotapes to police officers in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) and his sentence of six days in jail and $ 150 fine on each count, and asserted that the trial court erred when it refused to quash on the basis that the statute was vague, indefinite, and uncertain, and because there was not a timely determination of obscenity. The court affirmed and found that appellant's general attack on the statute was unsupported by prior decisions of the federal appellate court. The statute was not void for vagueness. The court found that the definition of obscenity that was originally crafted by the United States Supreme Court was only later enhanced and not reversed by subsequent decisions. The court found that the test was not whether an ordinary person who applied community standards would have found an allegedly obscene work to have had serious value, but whether a reasonable person would have found such value. The court held that the Texas statute was not offended by the subsequent federal decisions.


OUTCOME: A conviction of the sale obscene videotapes was affirmed because the statute was held by both federal and state courts to have not been void for vagueness, because the standard for the determination of obscene material was whether a reasonable person who applied community value found serious value in the work, and because the federal definition did not counter the statutory state definition.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of an order of the District Court of Lubbock County, 99th Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor in appellant's medical malpractice action. Appellee claimed that the action was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient underwent surgery for injuries to his right knee and right ankle sustained in an automobile accident by doctors, which was supervised by appellee doctor. While receiving post-operative care appellant learned that he had a fracture of his right foot that went undiagnosed and untreated by appellee. Appellant filed a notice of health care liability as provided by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 4.01 (1988) and a suit against doctors, and later filed suit against appellee after learning that appellee had been the supervisory physician. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment, claiming that appellant's suit was barred by the two-year statute of limitations. Appellant responded with the argument that his notice of health care liability tolled the statute for 75 days, making his claims against appellee timely. The trial court granted appellee's motion and appellant sought review of that decision. The court reformed the judgment so that appellant take nothing from appellee and affirmed the reformed judgment, holding that only one 75-day tolling period was provided under the statute, which appellant had used when he filed his original suit against doctors.

OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered, and remanded in part in appellee residents' suit to declare appellant city's annexation ordinances invalid. Tenner v. State


No. 2-86-285-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


763 S.W.2d 877; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3401



December 23, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Refused July 26, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 3 OF TARRANT COUNTY, DON LEONARD, TRIAL COURT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Criminal District Court No. 3, Tarrant County (Texas), convicting him of the offense of murder arguing that the jury should have been instructed on a lesser included offense of negligent homicide.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction by a jury of the offense of murder. Appellant argued that the court erred in failing to submit to the jury the lesser included offenses of negligent homicide and involuntary manslaughter. The judgment was affirmed because the evidence did not establish that if appellant were guilty at all, he was guilty only of the offense of negligent homicide or of involuntary manslaughter. There were only two theories presented by the evidence as to how appellant's child suffered the injuries that caused her death. One theory was that appellant caused it by grabbing the victim's hair and slamming her head against the floor. The other theory was that the injury might have been caused when the child fell over the coffee table and hit her head on the couch. The jury found that appellant intentionally, with intent to cause serious bodily injury, committed an act clearly dangerous to human life, which caused the child's death. The judgment was affirmed because the evidence was consistent with the offense of murder as found by the jury, and there was no evidence reflecting a lack of intent to cause serious bodily injury.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for murder was affirmed because appellant was not entitled to an instruction on any lesser included offenses because appellant intentionally caused the death of his daughter by beating her without mercy.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3188



December 22, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 13, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 959,691


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the County Criminal Court at Law, No. 13, Harris County (Texas). He had entered a plea of nolo contendere before the trial court to the offense of obscenity under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) and was convicted and sentenced by the trial court to confinement and a fine. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred by denying his pretrial motion to quash the information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the trial court wherein he had entered a plea of nolo contendere to the offense of obscenity under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1). Defendant claimed that the trial court erred by denying his pretrial motion to quash the information and raised two points of error on appeal. He asserted that § 43.23(c)(1), which was the basis of his prosecution, was unconstitutionally indefinite, uncertain and vague and that his pretrial motion to quash should have been granted because there was not a timely and proper determination of obscenity. In affirming his conviction, the court did not reach the merits of defendant's points of error, finding that he failed to preserve error for review. The court observed that his motion to quash the complaint had not mentioned § 43.23(c)(1) but instead had mounted an attack upon City of Houston, Tex., Adult Arcade Ordinance §§ 28-91(a), 28-84 and thus the trial court was never confronted with the points of error raised on appeal regarding § 43.23(c)(1). The court concluded that where his points of error did not comport with his objection made at trial, he had failed to preserve error for review.


OUTCOME: The judgment of defendant's conviction of obscenity was affirmed, where he had claimed error in denial of his pretrial motion to quash the information, on grounds that defendant's points of error raised on appeal as to the constitutionality of the state's obscenity statute did not comport with his objection made at trial, wherein his motion had attacked a city adult arcade ordinance, and thus he failed to preserve error for the court's review.

Chapman v. State


No. A14-87-00922CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3189



December 22, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 476,080


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 232nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting and sentencing him for burglary of a building.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was caught exiting a closed restaurant's window. When the restaurant manager was called to the scene, he determined that the window had been damaged and that a cigarette machine had been tampered with. Officers searched defendant, finding $ 95 in quarters and a screwdriver. Defendant waived a jury trial and was convicted and sentenced for burglary of a building. On appeal, defendant claimed the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction because the manager was not the owner of the building. The court noted that the manager was a statutory owner because he was an employee who exercised control or management of the property and had a greater right to possession of the property than defendant. Under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 42.03(2)(a), the defendant was entitled to credit for all time spent in jail from the day of his arrest until his sentence. Because defendant was not given the proper credit, the sentence was modified to reflect credit for time served. Defendant's constitutional challenge to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. 1.15 was rejected because he waived his right to a jury trial and did not offer evidence at trial. The judgment, as modified, was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for burglary of a building was affirmed because restaurant manager who confirmed the burglary was a statutory owner of the building. Defendant's constitutional challenge to bench trials was rejected because defendant waived his jury trial right before trial. Defendant's sentence was modified to reflect credit for time served from the time of his arrest.

 

744 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Standage v. State


No. A14-88-00346-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3215



December 22, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 973,205


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County (Texas), convicting and sentencing him for obscenity. Defendant claimed that his motion to quash the information was erroneously denied because Tex. Penal Code § 43.23(c)(1) was unconstitutionally vague and that there was no timely and proper determination of obscenity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his obscenity conviction under Tex. Penal Code § 43.23(c)(1) on grounds that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that there was not a timely and proper determination of obscenity. The court found that defendant failed to specify what part of § 43.23(c)(1) was vague or how it reached constitutionally protected conduct. There was nothing in the record to support defendant's contention that there was no judicial determination of probable cause as to whether the materials he sold were obscene. The court noted that defendant did not properly preserve the issue for review. Defendant also claimed that the obscenity definition of § 43.23(c)(1) applied an inappropriate standard to determine a work's value. The court rejected that argument, noting that § 43.23(c)(1) properly applied an average person standard to determine if a material or performance taken as a whole appealed to the prurient interest in sex. This average person standard was not linked to the statute's second inquiry, which required a determination of whether the material or performance as a whole lacked serious literary, artistic, political, and scientific value. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting and sentencing defendant for obscenity was affirmed. Defendant's constitutional challenge to the obscenity statute failed because he failed to show how it reached constitutionally protected conduct. The statute did not improperly apply an average person standard to the determination of whether the material or performance lacked serious literary, artistic, political, and scientific value.

 

745 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hardy v. State


No. A14-88-00334-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3230



December 22, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4 Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 8801731


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4, Harris County (Texas), where appellant was convicted of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code § 43.23 (c)(1).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code § 43.23 (c)(1). On review, appellant asserted that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that the statute used the wrong standard for determining whether a piece of work was obscene. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. First, the court held that in response to the overbreadth attack upon specific sections of 43.23(c)(1), the statute complied with the law and was not unconstitutionally vague. Moreover, the court held that in the absence of a specific attack upon a statute, the court would not engage in a search for unconstitutionality. Next, the court held that section 43.23 did not violate any constitutional mandates because it clearly applied the reasonable person standard for determining whether a piece of work had any value. The court stated that the trier of fact in an obscenity case must determine whether the average person, applying contemporary community standards, would find that a work, taken as a whole, appealed to the prurient interest. The court held that the average standard mentioned in the statute applied only to determining whether the work appealed to the prurient interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for obscenity because the statute was not unconstitutionally vague and because the statute incorporated the reasonable person standard in determining whether a piece of work had any value.

Haway v. State


No. A14-88-00283-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3231



December 22, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 973,208


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7, Harris County (Texas), where appellant was convicted of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code § 43.23.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1). On review, appellant asserted that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that the statute used the wrong standard for determining whether a piece of work was obscene. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. First, the court held that in response to the overbreadth attack upon specific sections of 43.23(c)(1), the statute complied with the law and was not unconstitutionally vague. Moreover, the court stated that in the obscene material of a specific attack upon a statute, the court would not engage in a search for unconstitutionality. Next, the court held that section 43.23 did not violate any constitutional mandates because it clearly applied the reasonable person standard for determining whether a piece of work had any value. The court stated the trier of fact in an obscenity case must determine whether the average person, applying contemporary community standards would find a work, taken as a whole, appealing to the prurient interest. The court held the average person standard mentioned in the statute applied only to determining whether the work appealed to the prurient interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for obscenity because the statute was not unconstitutionally vague and because the statute incorporated the reasonable person standard for determining whether a piece of work had any value.

Tipa v. State


Nos. A14-87-00802-CR, B14-87-00803-CR, C14-87-00804-CR, A14-87-00805-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3249



December 22, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 1, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 949,908; 947,649; 947,650 and 945,687


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction that was entered in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 1, Harris County (Texas), on four offenses of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1), and his sentence to confinement of three days and a fine of $ 300 for each offense.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant on four offenses of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1). Appellant challenged the conviction and sentence to three days confinement and fine of $ 300 on each offense, and asserted that the obscenity statute was vague, indefinite, and uncertain, and because the trial court erred when it failed to quash because there was no timely determination of obscenity. The court affirmed and found that appellant failed to specifically point out where the statute was vague as applied in his case, and that appellant failed to identify any indefinite, uncertain, or vague language in the statute. The court found that there was nothing in the record that supported appellant's assertion that there was no pretrial judicial determination of probable cause that appellant sold allegedly obscene material. The court held that the Texas statute mirrored the federal definition of obscenity and that the determination of whether taken as a whole allegedly obscene material contained serious artistic, literary, political, or scientific value was made by a reasonable person.


OUTCOME: A conviction of four offenses of obscenity was affirmed because appellant failed to identify how the obscenity statute was vague as applied to his case, because appellant was unable to identify language in the statute that was vague, indefinite, or uncertain, and because the possible literary, artistic, political, or scientific value of allegedly obscene material was determined by a reasonable person who reviewed such works as a whole.

CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1). Accordingly, defendant did not preserve error for appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of obscenity was affirmed, because defendant failed to preserve any error for appeal.

Netzley v. State


Nos. A14-87-00823-CR, B14-87-00830-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3277



December 22, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 944,625 & 944,626


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9 of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him, on pleas of nolo contendere, of obscenity under Tax. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1), and sentenced him to confinement and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two offenses of obscenity under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1), and was sentenced to confinement and a fine. On appeal defendant claimed that the statute on which his prosecution was based was unconstitutionally vague. In a second point of error defendant claimed that his pretrial motions to quash should have been granted because there was no timely and proper determination of obscenity. The court affirmed. Defendant did not point to any statutory language that was unconstitutionally vague and uncertain. There was nothing in the record that supported defendant's assertion that no prior judicial determination of probable cause was made with respect to whether the allegedly obscene material sold by defendant was in fact obscene. Moreover, because defendant did not raise this argument in his motions to quash, and did not obtain permission of the trial court to argue the issue on appeal, the court had no jurisdiction to consider it. The trial court's standard for "obscenity" did not use an unconstitutional "average person" standard to determine whether a work had serious literary, artistic, political or scientific value.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of obscenity and sentencing him to confinement and a fine was affirmed. The obscenity statute was not unconstitutionally vague, and there was a timely and proper determination of obscenity.

Texas Nat'l Bank v. Harris County


No. B 14-88-00101-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


765 S.W.2d 823; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3275



December 22, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 281st District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 83-73158


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant national banking association challenged summary judgments granted by the 281st District Court, Harris County, Texas, in favor of appellee county. Appellant alleged that taxes were unlawfully collected under an unconstitutional statute, Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 11.02, where it violated 31 U.S.C.S. § 3124.


OVERVIEW: Appellant national banking association sued to recover taxes paid on bank stock. At trial, the court granted summary judgment to appellee county, and appellant sought appellate review. The appellate court held that the trial court correctly considered appellant's evidence that it did not know that the federal obligations it held were beyond the jurisdiction of the local taxing authorities. The court held that these claims were insufficient to raise a material fact issue regarding the voluntary nature of appellant's payment. The appellate court held that the mistakes alleged were unilateral mistakes of law which were not an exception to the voluntary payment rule. Since there was no issue of material fact regarding any defense to the voluntary payment rule, summary judgment was proper. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant national banking association's mistakes were unilateral mistakes of law which were not an exception to the voluntary payment rule, leaving no issue of material fact, and making the lower court's summary judgment to appellee county proper. Accordingly, the court affirmed.

 

753 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ray v. State


Nos. A14-87-00346-CR, B14-87-00347-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


764 S.W.2d 406; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3284



December 22, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by, 06/28/1989
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Motion denied by Ray v. Davis, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 147571 (S.D. Tex., Oct. 25, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 232nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 446,599 and 446,600.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 232nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted her for the murder of her parents and assessed punishment at confinement for life for each offense, the sentences to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant for the murder of her parents and made an affirmative finding on the use of a deadly weapon. The jury assessed punishment at confinement for life for each offense. The person who fired the fatal shots testified at defendant's trial pursuant to a plea bargain agreement with the state. The court rejected defendant's argument that her convictions must be reversed because of insufficient evidence to corroborate the accomplice testimony, finding that the cumulative weight of the independent incriminating evidence was more than sufficient to corroborate the accomplice witness testimony. The court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting tape-recorded conversations between the accomplice and another person and in excluding testimony regarding prior violent acts by the accomplice. Because there was no specific finding that defendant used the deadly weapon herself, the court held that the trial court erred by including the affirmative finding. Thus, the court reformed the judgment to delete any mention of the affirmative finding and, as reformed, affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, as reformed, a judgment that convicted defendant for the murder of her parents and sentenced her to confinement for life where sufficient incriminating evidence corroborated accomplice testimony. The court reformed the judgment to delete any mention of an affirmative finding on the use of a deadly weapon because there was no specific findings that defendant used the deadly weapon herself.

 

754 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Owens v. State


No. 05-88-00032-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


763 S.W.2d 489; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3381



December 21, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 30, 1989. Petition for Discretionary Review Denied July 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of a District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, under 28 grams. The trial court assessed punishment at 10 years in prison and probated the sentence, then revoked probation on the state's motion and sentenced defendant to prison. The trial court denied defendant's motion for new trial without a hearing.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, under 28 grams. The trial court imposed a probated sentence, then revoked defendant's probation and sentenced him to prison. Defendant's motion for new trial was denied without a hearing. On appeal, the court set aside the judgment revoking probation, the sentence, and the notice of appeal and remanded the case for a hearing on the new trial motion. The court concluded that the trial court erred in denying the new trial motion without a hearing because the hearing was a critical stage of the proceedings, the trial court abdicated its fact-finding function, and the trial court denied defendant the opportunity to make a record for review. The court ruled that defendant's statement, which constituted an unsworn declaration in substantial compliance with Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 132.001, 132.002, and 132.003, could be used in lieu of any sworn declaration, verification, oath, or affidavit requirement applicable to defendant's motion for new trial in a criminal case. Defendant's motion comprised a sufficient pleading presenting matters that should have been taken up in a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment revoking probation, the sentence, and the notice of appeal and remanded the cause to the trial court for a hearing on the motion for new trial. The court held that the trial court abdicated its fact-finding function and denied defendant a meaningful appellate review by not conducting a hearing on defendant's timely motion for new trial, which was sufficiently supported by an unsworn declaration.

Campbell v. State


Appeal Nos. 04-87-00287-CR, 04-87-00288-CR, 04-87-00289-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


765 S.W.2d 817; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3419



December 21, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 21, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from County Court at Law No. 7 of Bexar County, Trial Court Nos. 350,020, 357,530 & 352,851, Honorable Tony Jimenez, III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments of the County Court at Law No. 7 of Bexar County (Texas) that convicted her in three obscenity cases pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann § 43.23(c)(1) (1988), and sentenced her to six months confinement and a $ 50.00 fine probated for one year, plus 20 days confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with three separate violations of Tex. Penal Code Ann § 43.23(c)(1) for selling obscene materials. A jury found her guilty and she was sentenced to six months confinement and a $ 500.00 fine, probated for one year. As a condition of probation she was also assessed 20 days confinement. Defendant appealed her conviction and sentence. The court affirmed and held that obscenity was not protected speech under Tex. Const. art I, § 8, and that the Texas obscenity law was not unconstitutional. The court also held that even if the prosecutor's jury argument was improper, an instruction by the trial judge to the jury to disregard the improper argument was sufficient to cure the error. Reversible error occurred only when a statement to a jury was so inflammatory that its prejudicial effect could not reasonably be removed by such admonition. There was no reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's obscenity convictions and sentence and held that obscenity was not protected speech under the Texas constitution.

Pena v. State


No. 01-88-00200-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3046



December 15, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 25th District Court, Colorado County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 6-87


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged denial of his pre-trial speedy trial motion, from the 25th District Court, Colorado County (Texas), regarding his guilty plea to burglary of a building, arguing that it was error for the lower court to have not dismissed his case because he was denied his right to a speedy trial under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Tex. Const. art. I, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of denial his pre-trial speedy trial motion, pertaining to his guilty plea to burglary of a building, contending that the lower court erred in not dismissing his case because his rights to a speedy trial, under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Tex. Const. art. I, § 10, were denied. On appeal, the conviction was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held while the state could not justify at least 10 months of a year delay in bringing appellant to trial, appellant's rights were not violated as appellant did not assert any constitutional rights to a speedy trial. The court further held that even though the original motion on statutory speedy trial grounds was on file for a year, appellant did not request a hearing, urge the motion at any subsequent trial setting, or otherwise attempt to assert his rights to a speedy trial. The court also noted that while appellant experienced some prejudice from the delay, such prejudice was outweighed by appellant's failure to assert his right to a speedy trial on a basis upon which relief could be granted.


OUTCOME: The lower court judgment was affirmed as, even though the prosecution could not explain several months of delay in bringing appellant to trial, appellant failed to assert his right to a speedy trial.

Stump v. Outboard Marine Corp.


No. C14-87-00897-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3068



December 15, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 127th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 80-21331


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment from the 127th District Court, Harris County (Texas), granting summary judgment in favor of appellee manufacturer in an action brought by appellants for failure to warn, breach of warranty, and misrepresentation following the death of decedent in a boating accident. Appellee manufactured the engine of the boat decedent was riding in.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought review of a judgment from the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of appellee manufacturer in an action brought by appellants for failure to warn, breach of warranty, and misrepresentation following the death of decedent in a boating accident. The boat the deceased was riding in included a motor manufactured by appellee. The court affirmed the judgment. Appellants failed to present any summary judgment evidence concerning appellee's alleged prior knowledge of the defect, and therefore, the court could not consider allegations of appellee's prior knowledge on appeal. With regard to the breach of warranty claim, the court held the action was barred by the four-year statute of limitations pursuant to Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 2.725 (1968). The breach of warranty cause of action accrued when the engine was delivered. The court also affirmed the judgment with regard to appellants' negligence and misrepresentation claims because they were premised on the contention that appellee had prior knowledge of a defect. Appellants presented no summary judgment evidence concerning appellee's prior knowledge, and therefore, the court could not consider it on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting appellee manufacturer summary judgment. Appellants failed to present summary judgment evidence concerning appellee's prior knowledge in order to establish appellants' claims for failure to warn, negligence, and misrepresentation. As such, the court could not consider the allegations regarding appellee's prior knowledge on appeal. Also, the breach of warranty claim was barred by the statute of limitations.

 

758 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rainey v. State


No. C14-88-00219-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


763 S.W.2d 470; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3070



December 15, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 232nd District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 476453.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted him of aggravated sexual assault. Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in admitting outcry testimony under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.072 (Supp. 1988), that art. 38.072 violated the confrontation clause of the U.S. Const. amend. VI, and that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict.


OVERVIEW: The outcry testimony was properly admitted under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.072 (Supp. 1988). Appellant contended that the outcry witness was not the first person the complainant had spoken to after the offense. This was true, as another person had asked the complainant whether appellant had done anything to her, and the complainant had answered no. But art. 38.072 was applicable to statements describing the offense. The first such statement made by the complainant was to the outcry witness, and it was thus admissible. Art. 38.072 did not violate appellant's confrontation right under U.S. Const. amend. VI. The law itself provided for sufficient indicia of reliability, and furthermore, the complainant had testified and had been cross-examined by appellant. The evidence was sufficient to convict appellant. The complainant testified that appellant had stuck his "thing" in her, and described him by name, and she was found coming out of his house.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction. Outcry testimony was properly admitted, as it related the first statement made by the complainant that described the offense. The outcry law did not deprive appellant of his right to confront the complainant. The evidence was sufficient to identify appellant as the assailant.

Wheatly v. State


No. 01-87-00878-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


764 S.W.2d 271; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3085



December 15, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 178th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 462089.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of aggravated robbery, from the 178th District Court of Harris County (Texas), arguing that it was error for the lower court to have overruled his objection to the prosecution's remarks to the jury which remarks contained a parole instruction that was held to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review from his conviction of aggravated robbery, contending that the lower court erred in overruling his objection to a jury charge on punishment that contained a parole instruction that was held unconstitutional. On appeal, the conviction was reversed. In support of its ruling, the court held that the prosecution erred in telling the jury to consider the number of years appellant would spend in jail prior to receiving probation in their deliberations. The court further held that if the court had the duty to reverse a conviction because of an error unless it determined beyond a reasonable doubt that the error made no contribution to the conviction or the punishment. With respect to the instant case, the court noted that while a curative jury instruction was given, the fact that appellant was relatively young, had no prior felony convictions, and had no misdemeanor convictions for crimes of violence or moral turpitude prevented the court from determining beyond a reasonable doubt that the prosecution's error did not contribute to the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed, as the court could not conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that the remarks of the prosecutor to the jury, which were in error, did not contribute to the punishment assessed against appellant.

Donovan v. Rankin


No. 01-86-00815-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


762 S.W.2d 342; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3089



December 15, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Original opinion of August 31, 1988 Withdrawn and Substituted.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 234th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Cause No. 79-53966.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners, sought review of the judgment of the 234th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which entered judgment in favor of appellees, sheriff, creditor, and attorney for creditor, in an action for wrongful execution and for associated violations of appellants' civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, property owners and payor, brought an action for wrongful execution and violations of appellants' civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Appellee sheriff's deputy was advised that the property sought belonged to appellants individually rather than the judgment debtor. Notwithstanding, appellee attorney for judgment creditor caused appellee sheriff to carry out the levy. In lieu thereof, appellants used borrowed funds to pay appellee sheriff to forestall the levy. The court held that the evidence before the jury, that the money was paid under protest and solely to prevent appellee sheriff from seizing and carrying away the office furnishings and fixtures which appellants claimed was their personal property, was not refuted and was sufficient to support the jury's finding that a wrongful execution on property was made. The judgment was reversed as to appellees, creditor and attorney.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment in favor of appellees, judgment creditor and his attorney, in an action brought for wrongful execution and violation of civil rights. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's finding that appellee sheriff carried out a wrongful execution on property belonging to appellant property owners, individually, rather than to the corporate judgment debtor.

 

761 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Kirby v. Edgewood Indep. Sch. Dist.


No. 3-87-190-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


761 S.W.2d 859; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3292



December 14, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 362,516, HONORABLE HARLEY CLARK, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state officials challenged a judgment from the 250th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas) that held that the school financing system, Tex. Educ. Code § 16.001, et seq., was unconstitutional. Appellants asserted that education was not a fundamental right, wealth was not a suspect class, the system was authorized under Tex. Const. art. VII, § 3, and that the system was efficient, as required by Tex. Const. art. VII, § 1.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the school financing system, Tex. Educ. Code § 16.001, et seq., was not unconstitutional. The financing system provided that approximately 50 percent of the costs for each school district was to be funded from local property taxes, creating a disparity between wealthier and less wealthy districts. The court rejected the assertions of appellees, parents, teachers, and students of certain district, that the school financing system, supported by appellant state officials, violated equal protection rights, the due course of law, and the efficient school system provisions of the Texas Constitution. The court held that education was not a fundamental right and that wealth was not a suspect classification. Applying the rational relation test, the court found that the school financing system did not violate equal protection rights. The court held that the school financing system was authorized by Tex. Const. art. VII, § 3. Finally, the court concluded that, given the enormous complexity of a school system educating three million children, the question of efficiency was essentially a political question not suitable for judicial review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that found the Texas school financing system to be unconstitutional. The court held that education was not a fundamental right and that wealth was not a suspect class. Applying the rational relation test, the court found the system did not violate equal protection. The court held that system was authorized under constitution and that efficiency was a political question and not a proper subject for judicial review.

 

762 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rodriguez v. State
