763 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Gray v. State


Nos. A14-87-00370-CR, A14-87-00371-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2980



December 8, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 463,198 & 463,199


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Texas Court of Criminal Appeals remanded appellant's challenge to jury charges on parole law for reconsideration of whether the trial court committed harmful error under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) when it made a jury charge at appellant's criminal trial.


OVERVIEW: After trial for his underlying offense, appellant contended that the trial court erred when it instructed the jury on the parole law as mandated by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a). The court found no error. Thereafter, the Texas Court of Criminal Appeals found that statute unconstitutional and directed the court on remand to evaluate the alleged error under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2). The court noted that the factors to be used in applying Rule 81(b)(2) to the subject parol charge included whether a curative instruction was given, whether the facts of the offense militated in favor of the sentence imposed, if any reference to the parole law was made in closing argument, and if defendant had prior felony convictions. Looking upon the charge as whole in view of those factors, the court found beyond a reasonable doubt that the unconstitutional parole charge made no contribution to appellant's conviction or punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence was affirmed. The jury charge on parole did not constitute a harmful error as it made no contribution to appellant's conviction or punishment.

 

764 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. State


No. 01-87-00708-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2995



December 8, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Discretionary Review Granted March 14, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd Judicial District Court Brazoria County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 17,547


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 23rd Judicial District Court of Brazoria County, Texas, entered after a jury found him guilty of aggravated sexual assault, enhanced by two prior felonies, and assessed punishment of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of a judgment entered after a jury found him guilty of aggravated sexual assault. Shortly after appellant was taken into custody after running down a street naked and jumping into a river, police received a report that a suspect in a sexual assault had fled the scene naked. Police later found appellant's clothes and wallet in the house next door to complainants. The court found sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding that a deadly weapon was used as complainant and her sister testified that they were cut by a knife during the attack and that the sister saw the blade, the injuries were shown in photographs, and a cutting instrument was used in the break-in. The court rejected the complaint that a photo spread was impermissibly suggestive as the sister made a tentative identification from the first set of photos depicting appellant with wet hair and a positive identification from a second set of pictures taken with dry hair. The court also found that appellant's statements made to an officer that directly refuted statements made at trial were properly admitted for impeachment purposes under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22(1985).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment after rejecting appellant's points of error and finding sufficient evidence to support the jury finding that a deadly weapon was used in the commission of the offense, that under the totality of the circumstances there was not a substantial likelihood that a misidentification occurred, and that statements made to an officer were properly admitted at trial for purposes of impeachment.

 

765 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Phelps v. State


No. 01-88-00118-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3020



December 8, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 488912


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted and sentenced him for possession of cocaine. On appeal, he contended that the trial court erred when it admitted the written affidavits of two police officers because he did not waive in writing his right to cross-examine those witnesses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of possession of cocaine. On appeal, he challenged the trial court's admission of the affidavits of two police officers against him. The affidavits recited the facts given to the officers by an informant, the surveillance of appellant prior to his arrest, appellant's arrest, and the subsequent seizure of a briefcase that contained the contraband. No other evidence presented by appellee linked appellant to the contraband or established his knowing and intentional possession of it. On appeal, the court determined that the affidavits were improperly admitted during the guilt/innocence phase of the trial because they violated appellant's right to confrontation and cross-examination under U.S. Const. amend. VI . The relevant question was thus whether the admission of the affidavits constituted harmless error. Given that the erroneously admitted affidavits were the only evidence that affirmatively linked appellant to the contraband or established his knowing and intentional possession, their admission was not harmless. The trial court's judgment was thus reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of possession of cocaine was reversed. The trial court's admission of the affidavits of two officer's violated appellant's right to confrontation. Accordingly, without the admission of the affidavits, there was no evidence that affirmatively linked appellant to the contraband or established a knowing and intentional possession necessary for conviction of the charged offense.

 

766 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


American General Fire & Casualty Co. v. Schattman


No. 2-88-210-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


761 S.W.2d 582; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3235



December 8, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ORIGINAL PROCEEDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurer sought a writ of mandamus to review the order of respondents, judge and District Court, Tarrant County (Texas), to reinstate a case after it had been dismissed for want of prosecution for over 254 days. In this action, the real party in interest failed to discover that the case had been dismissed until after the statutory periods of time for allowing a motion to reinstate had already elapsed.


OVERVIEW: Real party in interest's attorney (attorney) failed to learn that a matter had been dismissed for lack of prosecution until well after the statutory period of time allowing motions for reinstatement had elapsed pursuant to Tex. R. Civ. P. 306a(1), Tex. R. Civ. P. 165a(3), and Tex. R. Civ. P. 306a(4). Nevertheless the attorney filed a motion for reinstatement, which was then granted by the trial court. Petitioner insurer sought a writ of mandamus and argued that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to grant reinstatement. The court granted the writ of mandamus and set aside the trial court's order of reinstatement. The court stated that while attorney had not received notice of the judgment, part of the reason for the lack of notice was attorney's lack of diligence. The court also stated that while the trial court had no jurisdiction to grant reinstatement, the attorney was not left without a remedy because the judgment could still be attacked in a bill of review procedure to prevent unjustness. Finally, the court stated that Tex. R. Civ. P. 165a and Tex. R. Civ. P. 306a were not violative of the open courts provision under Tex. Const., art. I, §13.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus and held that the trial court had no jurisdiction to reinstate real party in interest's matter. The court stated that the lack of notice to the real party in interest's attorney was not egregious, that the judgment could be attacked via a bill of review procedure and that the restrictive statutory time periods on reinstatement had not violated the open courts provision of the Texas Constitution.

 

767 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Purcella v. State


Appeal No. 04-87-00577-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


762 S.W.2d 696; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3360



December 7, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 198th District Court of Kerr County, Trial Court No. 1,171, Honorable V. Murray Jordan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REFORMED, AND AS REFORMED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a jury sentence following a conviction in the 198th District Court of Kerr County (Texas) for the offense of burglary of a habitation with the intent to commit aggravated assault. Following a plea of guilty, the jury assessed punishment. Appellant contended that an erroneous charge to the jury of the laws relating to parole was reversible error.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to the offense of burglary of a habitation with the intent to commit aggravated assault. The jury assessed punishment. The trial court instructed the jury in regard to parole and the prosecutor made argument on the same subject, but both admonished the jury to not consider parole. On appeal, the court held that both the instruction and argument were error. Case law relieved appellant of the obligation of objecting at trial to the charge which contained the unconstitutional parole law instruction. It was unclear if appellant was likewise relieved of the obligation of objecting at trial to the prosecutor's improper comments. The court analyzed harm in light of Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2). The presumption that the jury followed the trial court's instructions not to consider the parole law, the prosecutor's clear admonishment to the jury to ignore the application of the parole law completely, together with the past violent assaults of appellant, convinced the court that the errors complained of did not affect the sentence. The court found beyond a reasonable doubt that the errors made no contribution to the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The court reformed the judgment to delete a reference to use of a deadly weapon as agreed by appellant and the state, but otherwise affirmed the judgment because although the trial court's instruction and the prosecutor's argument were in error for referring to the parole law, the court found beyond a reasonable doubt that the errors made no contribution to the punishment assessed.

 

768 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Byrum v. State


No. C14-88-00108-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


762 S.W.2d 685; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2960



December 1, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4 Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 960,252.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her misdemeanor conviction for the offense of public lewdness by sexual contact in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.07(a)(3) and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.01(2) entered in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4, Harris County, Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of public lewdness by sexual contact under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.07(a)(3) and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.01(2) arising from specific acts committed in her performance as a topless dancer on an undercover police officer in the nightclub where appellant was employed. On appeal, appellant challenged the constitutionality of the statutes and the sufficiency of evidence for her conviction. The court affirmed, holding that because the statutes did not attempt to regulate constitutionally protected activity, appellant's facial overbreadth challenge was without merit. Appellant's vagueness challenge was also without merit because the statutes clearly proscribed both the acts committed by appellant and her knowing intent. There was sufficient evidence that appellant touched the officer's genitals, that she knew she was doing so, and that she did so to arouse his sexual desire, in violation of the statutes. The denial of appellant's motion to set aside the state's amended information which substituted the term "groin area" for the term "genitals" in order to comply with the statutes was proper because the there was no prejudice to appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of the offense of public lewdness by sexual contact because there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction, the applicable statutes under which appellant was convicted were not unconstitutionally overbroad or vague, and the denial of appellant's motion to quash the state's amended information was proper.

Handl v. State


Nos. A14-87-00685-CR, B14-87-00686-CR, C14-87-00687-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


763 S.W.2d 446; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2894



November 23, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 945,844, 948,020 & 950,151.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County, Texas, convicting him of three offenses of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of three offenses of obscenity. On appeal, appellant contended that the trial court erred by denying his pretrial motions to quash the informations because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(a)(1) was unconstitutionally indefinite, uncertain, and vague, and because there was not a timely and proper determination of obscenity. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the statute was enacted within the United States Supreme Court guidelines setting forth the constitutional limits of obscenity statutes. The court further held that appellant failed to preserve his argument that there was no timely and proper determination of obscenity for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for obscenity, holding that the Texas obscenity statute was not unconstitutionally indefinite, uncertain, or vague, because it complied with the United States Supreme Court guidelines establishing the constitutional limits of obscenity statutes.

Thomas v. State


No. C14-87-00147-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2895



November 23, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Discretionary Review Denied October 4, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 16,687


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County (Texas), which convicted him, upon a jury trial, of aggravated assault on a prison guard, a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for aggravated assault on a prison guard in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that the evidence was sufficient to establish proof of each element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The court determined that the evidence did not establish evidence to support a jury charge for the lesser-included offense of resisting arrest because the victim was not attempting to arrest defendant when the assault occurred. The court found that the indictment provided defendant notice, in ordinary and concise language, of the charge against him and the manner and means by which it was committed. The court concluded that the prosecutor did not improperly make a plea for law enforcement in his summation to the jury because he did not indicate the community expected or desired that defendant be convicted or punished. The court determined that defendant failed to establish ineffective assistance of counsel because the record as whole indicated that, based upon the totality of the representation, counsel's performance was not deficient and did not prejudice the defense of the matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for aggravated assault on a prison guard, finding that the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction on each element of the offense charged. The court determined that the evidence did not support defendant's request for a jury charge on a lesser-included offense and that the indictment provided him notice of the offense charged in ordinary and concise language.

Palmer v. State


Nos. 01-87-01012-CR, 01-87-01013-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2901



November 23, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 180th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 480,421; 480,422


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 180th District Court of Harris County (Texas), convicting him, upon a jury trial, of aggravated sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping, contending that he had ineffective assistance of trial counsel, that the evidence was insufficient to support the finding that he used a knife as a deadly weapon, and that language in the charging statute for aggravated sexual assault was void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for aggravated sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping, claiming that he had ineffective assistance of trial counsel, that the evidence did not support the finding that he used a knife as a deadly weapon, and that the language in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 referencing "criminal episode" was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. VI and Tex. Const. art. I, § 10, defendant did not have ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The court determined that counsel was not deficient in failing to object to admissible testimony. The court found that the evidence was replete with accounts of defendant using the knife in his possession as a deadly weapon during the commission of both crimes. The court concluded that the challenged language in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 was neither meaningless nor unconstitutionally vague, and referenced that period commencing when defendant in any way restricted the victim's freedom of movement and ending with the final release of the victim from defendant's control.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of defendant for aggravated sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping, finding that his counsel's failure to object to admissible testimony did not constitute ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The court determined that the record was replete with evidence that defendant used a knife as a deadly weapon and that the language in the charging statute was neither meaningless nor unconstitutionally vague.

Pullman v. Brill, Brooks, Powell & Yount


No. C14-87-00468-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


766 S.W.2d 527; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2910



November 23, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 157th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 84-40287.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client sought review of a judgment of the 157th District Court, Harris County (Texas), that awarded attorney's fees to appellee law firm on appellee's successful suit for other unpaid legal fees. The jury awarded $ 10,000 for possible appeal to the Supreme Court of Texas, where the evidence showed $ 1,500 as reasonable.


OVERVIEW: Appellee law firm brought a successful action for unpaid legal fees against appellant client. The jury awarded appellee attorney's fees, including fees for potential appellate work if appellant should seek further review. Appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence for attorney's fees, but the court affirmed, finding that appellant's motion for a new trial had not stated insufficiency of the evidence as a basis. The court further found that attorney's fees for future appellate work could be awarded, but ordered appellee to submit a remittitur of $ 5,000 because the jury had awarded $ 10,000 in case of an appeal to the Supreme Court of Texas but appellee's own testimony showed that only $ 1,500 was reasonable. Finally, the court found that attorney's fees were permissible even though appellee represented itself and did not hire outside counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee law firm which granted it attorney's fees from appellant client for its successful prosecution of a suit for other unpaid fees. However, the court ordered that the judgment as to appeal fees would be reversed and remanded unless appellee submitted a remittitur of $ 5,000.

Fives v. State


No. 01-87-00519-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2833



November 17, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 439,726


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 185th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated robbery. The indictment alleged that the store's money belonged to a sacking clerk, and appellant challenged ownership under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 1.07(a)(24) (1974).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery and sentenced to five years in prison after robbing a grocery store at gunpoint. The indictment alleged that the store's money belonged to the sacking clerk, who was present at the time but who did not own the money or hand it over to appellant. Appellant sought review, but the court affirmed the conviction, finding that the clerk, while not being the owner of the store's money, still had a greater right to possession of it under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 1.07(a)(24) (1974) than appellant. The court also found that the trial court erred in charging the jury on parole law during the punishment phase, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a), but found that the error was harmless where the state recommended a sentence of 20 years and appellant received five. Finally, the court held that the testimony of the store manager's psychiatrist was properly excluded as improper bolstering of a witness, where appellant wished the psychiatrist to rebut the state's implication that the store manager had cooperated in the robbery and, thus, was lying in testifying that appellant was not the robber.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery, finding that the sacking clerk did not own the store's money but had the greater right to possession of it, as compared to appellant. The court further found that the jury instructions regarding parole law were improper but did not contribute to either the conviction or the punishment.

Smithwick v. State


No. 3-87-241-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


762 S.W.2d 232; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3314



November 16, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] July 26, 1989, Petition for Discretionary Review Refused.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 86,226, HONORABLE BOB JONES, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 167th Judicial District (Texas), which found him guilty of aggravated promotion of prostitution under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.04 (1974).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated promotion of prostitution. On appeal he challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to support his conviction, claimed the trial court erred in refusing to submit a requested instruction to the jury, and attacked Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.04 (1974) as unconstitutionally vague for failing to define the term "prostitute." The reviewing court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that a policemen's testimony constituted overwhelming evidence of a prostitution enterprise, and that there was sufficient evidence that defendant "controlled, supervised, or managed" the enterprise. Further, the reviewing court held that the trial court properly charged the jury on the definition of "prostitution enterprise." Lastly, the Court of Criminal Appeals had on many occasions ruled on the constitutionality of § 43.04, and had specifically upheld § 43.04 in the face of an argument that the term "prostitution enterprise" was vague and ambiguous. Accordingly, the reviewing court held that, within the context of § 43.04, the term "prostitute" was capable of only one meaning. All of defendant's points of error were overruled and the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction for aggravated promotion of prostitution. Further, the trial court properly charged the jury regarding the definition of "prostitution enterprise," even though it refused to give the definition requested by defendant. Lastly, the statute upon which defendant's conviction was based was held to be constitutional.

 

777 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. State


No. 6-87-086-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


762 S.W.2d 640; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2746



November 8, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] November 29, 1988, Motion for Rehearing Overruled.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from County Court No. 1, Galveston County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for criminal trespass under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05 (1988) in the County Court No. 1, Galveston County (Texas), because he was passing out anti-abortion leaflets on school grounds and did not leave when asked to do so. Defendant complained that the application of the statute violated his free speech rights under U.S. Const. amend. I and Tex. Const. art. I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was distributing anti-abortion booklets to students on a high school campus. He refused to leave when a school official asked him to leave, and was arrested, tried, and convicted for criminal trespass under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05 (1988). The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that because the school was a nonpublic forum, officials had the power to restrict speech and not violate U.S. Const. amend. V or Tex. Const. art. I, § 8. The charging instrument was sufficient per Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 21.09. Defendant waived his argument that the information failed to allege sufficient facts because he failed to raise it at trial. School officials could testify that they would have let defendant leave his booklets at the school, because it showed that they were not trying to stifle his speech, and defendant had failed to object to such testimony earlier. There was no error regarding inflammatory remarks by the prosecutor. Defendant successfully objected at the time, and did not request a jury instruction or move for a mistrial. There was no need to prove any criminal intent beyond defendant's refusal to leave the property when asked to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that because a school is a nonpublic forum, speech may be restricted more strictly. It was not defendant's speech being regulated, but his conduct. The information was not defective, school officials could testify about their willingness to let defendant place pamphlets on school grounds, and the statute's only mental state required defendant to intend not to leave when asked.

 

778 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. State


Nos. 01-87-00741-CR, 01-87-00752-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2709



November 3, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 460,244


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions for aggravated assault and murder in the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), after waiving a jury trial and pleading guilty to the charges. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1977) and claimed he did not knowingly and intelligently waive his right to trial by jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated assault and murder. The court affirmed the trial court's conviction. Defendant claimed that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1977) was unconstitutional because it did not afford him the chance to rebut the evidence the prosecution put forward to support his conviction. Defendant also claimed that the trial court lacked jurisdiction because he was not informed of his right to put on evidence. The court held that art. 1.15 did not deny defendant any rights, and the trial court had jurisdiction. Defendant never claimed he tried to put on evidence. The court also dismissed defendant's argument that the trial court committed error in failing to inform him of the rights he was waiving by pleading guilty. The record showed that defendant waived his privilege against self-incrimination, his right to trial by jury, and his right to confront accusers. There was no requirement that he be presented with a laundry list of constitutional rights that were waived by a plea of guilty or that he make a separate waiver of each for the purpose of the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's aggravated assault and murder convictions. The court held that the statute in dispute was not unconstitutional. The statute provided an additional safeguard not required by the United States Constitution, and defendant did not claim that he tried to offer evidence. Because defendant waived his rights in writing, it was not necessary for him to specifically waive each one separately.

 

779 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hosey v. State


No. 13-87-185-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


760 S.W.2d 778; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2738



November 3, 1988  
November 3, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 24th District Court of Refugio County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for aggravated robbery handed down by the 24th District Court of Refugio County (Texas). Appellant presented ten points of error for review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery in connection with an altercation with a peace officer wherein the officer was shot and some of his property taken. The appellate court reversed the conviction and remanded. The court ruled that it was reversible error for the prosecution to argue to the jury that appellant should be given a long sentence because he would be given time off for good behavior, and might be paroled. The court rejected appellant's other nine points of error.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery. Although the court rejected nine of the ten points of error appellant raised on appeal, it agreed with appellant that reversible error was committed when the state argued that appellant should be given a long sentence because he would receive time off for good behavior and might be placed on parole.

 

780 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Krchnak v. Fulton


No. 07-88-0124-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


759 S.W.2d 524; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2719



November 1, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled November 30, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY, 237TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 87-518,522; Honorable John R. McFall, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant horse breeder sought review of a default summary judgment of the District Court of Lubbock County, 237th Judicial District (Texas), awarding appellee veterinarian a money judgment for boarding care, stud fees, and veterinary services rendered to appellant's mare, plus attorney's fees, and a foreclosure of a stableman's lien.


OVERVIEW: Appellee veterinarian filed a motion for summary judgment in his action against appellant horse breeder for damages for breach of contract. Notice of the motion was served on appellant, but not on his attorney, who as a result, did not file a response until after the hearing date. After entry of a default summary judgment, appellant filed a motion for new trial, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the summary judgment standard set forth in the Craddock rule should apply with equal force to a motion for new trial following entry of a default summary judgment. The court concluded appellant had met that test. The record showed that appellant's failure to file a response to the summary judgment motion was not intentional but was the result of a mistaken assumption regarding the time allowed to answer. Appellant's motion for new trial and supporting affidavit were sufficient to establish the existence of fact questions requiring resolution by a trier of fact. The motion for new trial was filed at a time when granting it would not have occasioned delay or otherwise worked injury to appellee.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellee veterinarian was reversed and the case remanded for trial. The trial court erred in denying appellant horse breeder's motion for new trial following default summary judgment. The motion and supporting affidavit set up a meritorious defense; the default did not result from conscious indifference; and the motion was filed at a time when granting it would not have caused delay or other injury to appellee.

 

781 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Erbs v. Bedard


No. 05-88-01044-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


760 S.W.2d 750; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3082



November 1, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] AN ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON WRIT OF MANDAMUS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator directors sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, presiding and visiting judges of the probate court, to dismiss certain litigation for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and in the alternative to compel respondent, visiting judge, to vacate an order assigning himself as a visiting judge to preside over the litigation or to disqualify himself from so presiding.


OVERVIEW: Relator directors sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, presiding and visiting judges of the probate court, to dismiss the litigation for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and to compel respondent, visiting judge, to disqualify himself from the litigation. The court concluded that the probate court lacked subject matter jurisdiction of the second through the fifth causes of action because the administrators brought those causes of action not as personal representatives of deceased's estate but as shareholders in trust for the estate and, therefore, those causes of action were shareholders' derivative actions. The court also found that Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 25.0022, governing the assignment of judges, was not unconstitutional because Tex. Const. art. V, § 1 gave the legislature broad and general power to establish and prescribe the organization of courts. Finally, the court found that Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 74.053 providing for the automatic disqualification of a judge upon a party's objection did not clearly and unambiguously apply to an assignment under the Tex. Gov't Code and, therefore, respondent, visiting judge, had no clear legal duty to disqualify himself.


OUTCOME: The court granted relator directors' petition only to the extent that it directed respondent, presiding judge of the probate court, to dismiss relators for lack of subject matter jurisdiction as to the second through the fifth causes of action because those causes of action were essentially shareholders' derivative actions. The court also found that respondent, visiting judge, did not abuse his discretion in assigning himself to the litigation.

 

782 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 01-88-00124-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2618



October 27, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 14, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 973,843 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction on the misdemeanor offense of obscenity and corresponding sentence of three days' confinement and a $ 250 fine, entered in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 14, Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded nolo contendere to the misdemeanor offense of obscenity, and the trial court sentenced her to three days' confinement and a $ 250 fine. Defendant appealed the trial court's denial of her motion to quash the information under contentions that Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 43.21(a)(1)(A) was unconstitutionally vague and that the evidence was insufficient due to the state's failure to obtain a prior adjudication that the magazine was obscene. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that a higher court previously adjudicated article 43.21(a)(1)(A) not unconstitutionally vague and that the court lacked jurisdiction to consider defendant's insufficiency of the evidence claim because she failed to assert it in her motion to quash and then pled nolo contendere.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because a higher court had previously adjudicated the obscenity statute not unconstitutionally vague and because defendant failed to assert her insufficiency of the evidence claim within her motion to quash the information and then pled nolo contendere, thereby eliminating the court's jurisdiction to consider the claim on appeal.

784 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Randle v. State


No. 01-86-00396-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


760 S.W.2d 30; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2633



October 27, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 240th District Court of Fort Bend County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 16,165.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the 240th District Court of Fort Bend County (Texas), which convicted defendant of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery. Defense counsel (counsel) initially filed a notice of appeal; however, counsel failed to timely file a statement of facts and made numerous requests for extensions. Finally, more than two years later, counsel filed a six-page brief. The court noted that the brief only alluded to the sufficiency of the evidence to support the conviction. More importantly, counsel failed to raise the fact that the jury instructions of the parole charge was declared unconstitutional more than seven months prior to the filing of the brief. Therefore, defendant's brief was defective and constituted actual error. The court struck defendant's brief because it failed to meet the minimum requirements of state and federal law and ordered rebriefing of the case. Furthermore, the court ordered that should the trial court choose not to appoint new counsel, it was instructed to conduct a hearing to determine whether counsel was capable of rendering effective assistance and to advise the court of its findings within 30 days.


OUTCOME: The appellate court determined that, on appeal, defendant was receiving ineffective assistance of counsel. Defense counsel made numerous delays in filing his brief and failed to raise the issue that a jury charge had been found unconstitutional. Therefore, the matter was remanded to the trial court for a determination that defense counsel could render effective assistance on appeal or for the appointment of new appellate counsel.

 

785 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Revada v. State


No. A14-87-00505-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


761 S.W.2d 426; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2649



October 27, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 351st District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 471,771.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 351st District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of delivery of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, appellant was convicted of delivery of a controlled substance. The appellate court affirmed the conviction, holding that evidence regarding the nature of the area where the offense took place, that it was a high crime area, was admissible under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 404(b). Similarly, the officer's testimony regarding his initial encounter with appellant, such that appellant was a dealer of a different type of drug, was admissible to allow the jury to understand the facts and circumstances surrounding the commission of the offense. The appellate court held that the evidence did not warrant a jury instruction of the defense of entrapment. Although the giving of the parole instruction, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1998) was error, it was harmless error because it made no contribution to conviction or punishment. The prosecutor's closing argument that appellant was a businessman in dope was a proper deduction from the evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's conviction of appellant for delivery of a controlled substance, because testimony concerning the nature of the area in which the offense took place was admissible, the evidence did not warrant an instruction on the defense of entrapment, the giving of the parole instruction was harmless error, and the state's jury argument was a reasonable deduction from the evidence.

 

786 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Drummond v. State


No. 01-88-00138-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2682



October 27, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 967,498


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7, Harris County (Texas) that found him guilty after entering a plea of nolo contendere to the misdemeanor offense of obscenity and assessed a sentence of three days confinement along with a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded nolo contendere to the misdemeanor offense of obscenity and was assessed a punishment of three days confinement along with a fine. Appellant sought review, challenging the constitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(1)(A), and arguing that the evidence was insufficient because the state failed to obtain a prior adjudication that the magazine he possessed was obscene. On appeal the court affirmed the conviction. The court stated that a determination of the statute's constitutionality had been previously upheld by the court of criminal appeals, which noted the statute was not unconstitutional in its use of the terms "prurient interest" and "patently offensive." Further, the court held that in appellant's motion to quash, he failed to assert that it was error for the trial court not to have a prior adjudication regarding whether the magazine was obscene. As such, the court was without jurisdiction to consider the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for obscenity because the statute under which he was convicted had previously been found to be constitutional. Additionally, the court was without jurisdiction to determine whether it was error in not having a final adjudication regarding whether the magazine was obscene because appellant, in his motion to quash, had failed to argue that contention.

Urbano v. State


No. 01-87-00674-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


760 S.W.2d 33; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2813



October 27, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Denied July 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 466,775.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision by the United States District Court for the 178th District, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of aggravated robbery and sentenced him to 99 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for aggravated robbery. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in granting the state's motion to shuffle because the venire already had been shuffled once. Existing case law on the issue was in conflict. The court reasoned that each party had an equal right to a shuffle under Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. art. 35.11; therefore, no error occurred. Defendant had waived his objection to lack of notice relating to the trial court's grant of state's motion to shuffle because defendant's objection, on this ground, was not timely. Defendant argued that the prosecutor committed reversible error by discussing victim rights during argument at the punishment phase of trial. Prosecutor's comments were a proper reminder to the jury to consider defendant's prior conviction in determining his sentence and that such comments were harmless. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred in charging the jury on the law of parole. The court found that the manner in which the charge was raised was harmful to defendant. Therefore, the court affirmed defendant's conviction, but reversed his sentence for a new trial on punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because defendant failed to demonstrate reversible error; however, the court reversed defendant's sentence because the trial court erred in charging the jury on the law of parole, which caused harm warranting reversal.

Ford v. State


No. 01-87-01125-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2559



October 20, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 963,477


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction for selling obscene materials, which was entered by the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9, Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea bargain, defendant pleaded nolo contendere to a charge of selling obscene materials. The trial court found defendant guilty. Defendant appealed and argued that the trial court erred in denying her pretrial motion to quash because Texas Penal Code § 43(B) violated the U.S. Const. amend. I, XIV. The court held that defendant failed to enumerate what part of the statute was vague, and defendant did not detail a risk or detriment to which she had been exposed without fair warning. Thus, defendant presented nothing for the court to review. The court concluded that defendant had failed to enumerate a single example of an unconstitutional application, and, therefore, the presumption of the statute's constitutionality remained unrebutted. Defendant made two additional arguments on the trial court' denial of her motion to quash, and the court held that defendant did not raise those particular arguments in her motion to quash, nor did she obtain the trial court's permission to argue so on appeal; thus, the court lacked jurisdiction to address defendant's argument, and the conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for selling obscene materials because defendant failed to identify the portions of the statute that she claimed were unconstitutionally vague. Thus, defendant had not presented anything to the appellate court to review.

Turner v. State


No. A14-87-00397-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2573



October 20, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 21st District Court, Burleson County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 9613


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the 21st District Court, Burleson County (Texas) for aggravated assault under Tex Penal Code Ann. § 22.02. Defendant contended that his right to a speedy trial was violated pursuant to the Texas Speedy Trial Statute, Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. § 32A.02, the Texas Constitution, and the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to aggravated assault. Tex Penal Code Ann. § 22.02. He contended that he was not given a speedy trial under the Texas Speedy Trial Statute, Tex. Crim. P. In addition, defendant did not raise his constitutional speedy trial claims to the trial court and those issues were not preserved for appellate review.

Sears v. Texas State Bd. of Dental Examiners


No. 3-88-046-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


759 S.W.2d 748; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2890



October 19, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled November 23, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SAN SABA COUNTY, 33RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 5960, HONORABLE CLAYTON E. EVANS, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dentist sought relief from an order which suspended his license to practice dentistry for five years, which was entered by the District Court of San Saba County, Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant dentist suffered from back pain, and he began writing himself prescriptions. Appellant dentist was found by appellee board to be guilty of prescribing controlled substances not necessary or required in the practice of dentistry and guilty of dishonorable conduct in the practice of dentistry. Appellee suspended appellant's license to practice dentistry. The court held Cal. Board Rule Art. 4549, § 3(c), taken together with appellee's rule, made clear the meaning of dishonorable conduct, and appellant did not challenge the validity of appellee board's rule upon any basis. The court held that valid agency rules, promulgated within the agency's authority, had the force and effect of law and that appellant failed to complain of the incorrect citation in his motion for rehearing filed with appellee. The court concluded that appellant had not demonstrated that any substantial right was prejudiced by the incorrect citation to the statute and that appellant had adequate notice of the claimed violation and of the basis for suspension of his dental license. Therefore, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining an order of appellee board that suspended appellant dentist's license to practice dentistry because appellant failed to establish that any of his substantial rights were prejudiced when appellee incorrectly cited the statute under which his license was suspended, and appellant had adequate notice of the charges against him.

Bridwell v. State


Nos. 05-87-00197-CR, 05-87-00198-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


761 S.W.2d 401; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3238



October 19, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the orders of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas) which convicted him of violating the Texas Securities Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-29, and sentenced him to 2 20-year terms in prison to run cumulatively.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was involved in a continuing scheme to defraud investors by selling several investors substantially the same type of security investments, the prospective drilling of oil wells. A jury convicted appellant of two counts of violating the Texas Security Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-29 (Act), and sentenced him to 2 20-year sentences to run cumulatively. Art. 581-29 required sellers of securities to be truthful and provide investors with all material facts, thus allowing them to make informed decisions. On appeal the court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that the Act was constitutional because appellant was given fair notice that his conduct was forbidden by the statute. Moreover, the court held that appellant's U.S. Const. amend. V argument was meritless because neither the United States Constitution nor the Texas Constitution provided a cloak protecting criminal fraud. The court further held that the self-incrimination clause was not applicable because the Act required appellant to disclosure material facts to purchasers of securities. Lastly, the court upheld the trial court's sentencing order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to convict appellant for securities fraud, holding that the Texas Security Act (Act) was not unconstitutional because appellant was given fair notice that his conduct was forbidden. The court further held that appellant was not protected by the Fifth Amendment, because the Act required that he disclose material facts about his securities to his purchasers.

Gomez v. State


No. B14-85-00899-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2511



October 13, 1988 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 432,041


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his murder conviction and sentence to 18 years confinement, entered by the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sitting at a table at cafe talking with another patron. The victim slammed the door into the chair of defendant's companion. A fight ensued, and defendant walked up behind the victim, shot him two times, and killed him. The trial court convicted defendant of murder. Defendant appealed, contending that the jury charge contained fundamental error in that it contained an instruction on good time and parole under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4. The court held that the instruction was violative of the separation of powers and the due process provisions of the Texas Constitution, and error occurred. The court held that defendant did not show that the jury failed to follow this instruction, and the fact that defendant's sentence was lower than the maximum punishment corroborated the presumption that the jury followed the curative instruction. The court concluded that the erroneous instruction did not affect defendant's conviction or punishment, thus the error in submitting the instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt and made no contribution to the punishment assessed pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2). Therefore the conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction because an erroneous jury instruction on good time and parole did not affect appellant's conviction or punishment, supporting the presumption that the jury followed the trial court's curative instruction.

OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of aggravated robbery. However, the court determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion and that the errors were harmless. Defendant raised several points of error in relation to the trial court's charge to the jury, which the court found to be without merit. The court rejected defendant's argument that it was error for the jury not to take the jury charge and verdict form into the jury room pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 36.18 (1979). The court determined that penitentiary packets were properly admitted into evidence during the punishment stage of the trial. The court found the jury charge on punishment was unconstitutional, but determined that the error was harmless. The court found no error in either side's closing arguments. Since the court found no merit in defendant's numerous points of error, the court determined that defendant was not deprived of a fair trial. Accordingly, the court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery because defendant failed to show that any error occurred at trial.

 

796 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Blanco v. State


No. B14-87-00218-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


761 S.W.2d 38; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2475



October 6, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6 Harris County, TExas, Trial Court Cause No. 914,127.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought reversal of the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6 of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of disorderly conduct by intentionally making unreasonable noise in a public place under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.01(a)(5). Appellant challenged the constitutionality of the statute under which he was convicted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.01(a)(5) of disorderly conduct by intentionally making unreasonable noise in a public place when he refused to turn down the volume on his stereo. Appellant sought reversal and challenged the statute under which he was convicted as being unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Appellant also contended that the judgment did not reflect the jury's verdict as to the fine assessed by it. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that the statute was constitutional. The court found that appellant's conduct fell clearly within the proscribed activity of the statute, and that he knew that his conduct was prohibited. Therefore, the court determined that the statute did not impede any of appellant's constitutionally protected conduct, nor was it impermissibly vague as to appellant's conduct. Further, the court reformed the judgment to reflect the fine that the jury assessed in their verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for disorderly conduct by intentionally making unreasonable noise in a public place because the statute under which appellant was convicted was constitutional. The court determined that the statute did not impede any of appellant's constitutionally protected conduct, nor was it impermissibly vague as to appellant's conduct.

 

797 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Birdville Independent School Dist. v. First Baptist Church


No. 2-87-239-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


788 S.W.2d 26; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3445



October 6, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled May 15, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 236TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY; Hon. Jack Gray, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, school district, county, and city, sought review of a decision of the 236th District of Tarrant County (Texas), which rendered judgment for appellee church and held that the tax exemption application procedure violated appellee's right to the free exercise of religion under U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, school district, county, and city, filed suit against appellee church for delinquent taxes owed on property owned by appellee and used for a private school. The trial court held that procedure for claiming tax exempt status violated appellee's rights to the free exercise of religion under U.S. Const. I and entered judgment for appellee. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found that by substantially complying with the procedure for claiming tax exempt status, appellee ceded its constitutional complaint. Since appellee did not participate in an appeal to the appraisal review board to protest the assessment, appellee was foreclosed from contesting the validity of the assessment on factual grounds. Appellants established a prima facie case of delinquency and were entitled to delinquent taxes. Thus, the court rendered judgment for appellants. The court found that while the evidence of the religious use was conflicting, there was some evidence that the entire tract was used for religious worship on a regular basis. The evidence amounted to more than a scintilla and was ample enough that the jury's findings thereon were not manifestly unfair.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered judgment for the delinquent taxes for the tax years 1982 through 1986, and affirmed that portion of the judgment stating that appellants, school district, county, and city, take nothing for the tax years 1977 through 1981. By substantially complying with the procedure to claim tax exempt status, appellee church ceded its constitutional complaint.

 

798 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Mares v. State


No. 08-87-00263-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


758 S.W.2d 932; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2462



October 5, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As amended January 5, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 168th District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 49734-168), Honorable Ward L. Koehler, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the 168th District Court of El Paso County (Texas) which convicted him of indecency with a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant teacher was sentenced to seven years' imprisonment for indecency with a child, his student. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed because appellant's "running objection" did not preserve for review the admission of the victim's outcry statements to her mother. The court held that the statements were ripe for inclusion in the substantive evidence of the offense and that the child's case-in-chief testimony satisfied appellant's confrontation right. The court could not review the sufficiency of evidence, absent a recorded description of the scope of the victim's demonstrations regarding the misconduct. The court held that the testimony of the state's rebuttal witnesses, who were the victim's classmates at the time of the incident, were admissible for impeachment of appellant's testimony that he was unlikely to commit the charged offense and his overbroad assertion that nothing was ever done in his classroom to sexually arouse the victim. The court held that the testimony was admissible to show that the indicted and extraneous offenses were connected to a common criminal scheme to progressively exploit the teacher-student relationship.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for indecency, because appellant waived objection to the admission of outcry statements, the child was subjected to full cross-examination before the jury, a sufficiency of the evidence review was unavailable from the record, and the trial court properly admitted extraneous offense testimony for the impeachment of appellant's testimony and as proof of a common criminal scheme.

 

799 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Montgomery v. State


Nos. 05-87-00677-CR, 05-87-00678-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


760 S.W.2d 323; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2954



October 5, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Reported at: 773 S.W.2d 569.
Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied February 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of two charges of indecency with a child, on grounds that evidence of an extraneous offense was improperly introduced and that an unconstitutional jury instruction regarding parole was given under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4)(c).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two counts of indecency with a child in the trial court. The complainants, aged 7 and 10 at the time of trial, were appellant's daughters. Appellant sought review of the convictions. The court affirmed the trial court. The court held that evidence of an extraneous offense regarding appellant's prior inappropriate sexual conduct directed toward the complainants was properly admitted because it placed the charged offense in context. The probative value of the extraneous offense outweighed any possibility of prejudice. The court ruled that an unconstitutional jury instruction concerning the parole laws that was given to the jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4)(c) was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the state properly introduced evidence of the long-term effects of the offense on the complainants because appellant failed to preserve error and the trial court instructed the jury to disregard the questions. An objection by appellant to a witness's testimony about the coaching of the complainants' testimony was made after the question was asked and answered, which was too late to preserve error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that convicted appellant of two counts of indecency with a child because evidence of an extraneous offense was properly admitted to place the charged offense in context and its probative value outweighed any prejudicial effect, and an unconstitutional instruction given to the jury regarding the parole laws constituted harmless error.

 

800 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. State


No. 01-85-00873-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2868



September 29, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 429,980


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the 228th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of robbery, on grounds that the trial court improperly denied appellant's motion for a continuance under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 29.06 (1966), that appellant's right to confrontation and cross-examination was violated, and that the jury charge on the parole law was improper.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of robbery and the jury found the enhancement paragraphs to be true and assessed a punishment of 70 years confinement. Appellant sought review of the conviction. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that convicted appellant. The court held that the trial court properly denied appellant's motion for continuance on the day of trial pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 29.06 (1966). Appellant's motion for a continuance failed to comport with the requirements of art. 29.06 because the motion did not mention the subpoenaed witness and there was no evidence that appellant exerted any effort to secure service on the subpoenaed witness other than the instanter subpoena. The motion also failed to state what material facts were expected to be proved, that the witness was not absent by appellant's procurement or consent, and that the motion was not made for purposes of delay. Appellant was not denied the right to confrontation and cross-examination because appellant failed to show on the record why the cross-examination of the complainant about bias was relevant. An unconstitutional jury charge on the parole law was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that convicted appellant of robbery because the trial court properly denied appellant's motion for continuance based on appellant's failure to meet the statutory requirements, appellant was not denied the right to confrontation and cross-examination of the complainant, and an unconstitutional jury charge on the parole law was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.
